<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5b5e8603b0094d4f87a8b484c1a08283"><span data-offset-key="5b5e8603b0094d4f87a8b484c1a08283:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#and" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="caf30257d2234262b4b1a76086817be9"><span data-offset-key="caf30257d2234262b4b1a76086817be9:0">and</span></span></a><span data-key="b2d31a23669c4a69a0013aa9d4f79088"><span data-offset-key="b2d31a23669c4a69a0013aa9d4f79088:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#boolean-operations-and-or-not" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="70483df9ce624dbbb0d41668512d620e"><span data-offset-key="70483df9ce624dbbb0d41668512d620e:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="b52ca1d7c88b46d290d3b0982d6d71ea"><span data-offset-key="b52ca1d7c88b46d290d3b0982d6d71ea:0">A </span><span data-offset-key="b52ca1d7c88b46d290d3b0982d6d71ea:1">_binary_</span><span data-offset-key="b52ca1d7c88b46d290d3b0982d6d71ea:2"> OPERATOR that checks the </span><span data-offset-key="b52ca1d7c88b46d290d3b0982d6d71ea:3">_truth-value_</span><span data-offset-key="b52ca1d7c88b46d290d3b0982d6d71ea:4"> of two things, evaluating to the thing on the left if it tested </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ec2afa36513b4fea9ac681b107044bdb"><span data-offset-key="ec2afa36513b4fea9ac681b107044bdb:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e3827ff20ea44b119b8d871fc79b1beb"><span data-offset-key="e3827ff20ea44b119b8d871fc79b1beb:0"> , otherwise to the thing on the right.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="13540ff80b194dc7bf86c32ed376b35d"><span data-offset-key="13540ff80b194dc7bf86c32ed376b35d:0">An ancient Old English conjunction with Germanic roots vaguely meaning “thereupon” or “next \[to\]” and used to combine two words or phrases, as in “coffee </span><span data-offset-key="13540ff80b194dc7bf86c32ed376b35d:1">**_and_**</span><span data-offset-key="13540ff80b194dc7bf86c32ed376b35d:2"> tea”. The meaning in Python, however, comes entirely from </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logical_conjunction" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="489a4c6c5b5940cb88a5b22c6eabdacf"><span data-offset-key="489a4c6c5b5940cb88a5b22c6eabdacf:0">logical conjunction</span></span></a><span data-key="4c25d27b2d314002ae7082d941306bb8"><span data-offset-key="4c25d27b2d314002ae7082d941306bb8:0">, and implies that either </span><span data-offset-key="4c25d27b2d314002ae7082d941306bb8:1">_both_</span><span data-offset-key="4c25d27b2d314002ae7082d941306bb8:2"> things it combines are true or the whole combination is false.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c5cedf974d344270ab6dd55749584659"><span data-offset-key="c5cedf974d344270ab6dd55749584659:0">This is Python’s </span><span data-offset-key="c5cedf974d344270ab6dd55749584659:1">_Boolean conjunction_</span><span data-offset-key="c5cedf974d344270ab6dd55749584659:2"> OPERATOR; used whenever you need to test if </span><span data-offset-key="c5cedf974d344270ab6dd55749584659:3">_both_</span><span data-offset-key="c5cedf974d344270ab6dd55749584659:4"> sides of the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#and" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="54fa064033bd4fa3a80371d96aea47db"><span data-offset-key="54fa064033bd4fa3a80371d96aea47db:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">and</code></span></span></a><span data-key="6f3d1a77826e431eb2950ca15b619e68"><span data-offset-key="6f3d1a77826e431eb2950ca15b619e68:0"> are considered </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="dbd4d2eb00b040e9a23cb370377263f0"><span data-offset-key="dbd4d2eb00b040e9a23cb370377263f0:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e0f1ca190d9f4f9e9f2b85f4cb9ba386"><span data-offset-key="e0f1ca190d9f4f9e9f2b85f4cb9ba386:0"> . It is a </span><span data-offset-key="e0f1ca190d9f4f9e9f2b85f4cb9ba386:1">_short-circuiting_</span><span data-offset-key="e0f1ca190d9f4f9e9f2b85f4cb9ba386:2"> operation; if the left-hand EXPRESSION is considered </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="05ae5d430c4e4ce688ec7fa91c8c4939"><span data-offset-key="05ae5d430c4e4ce688ec7fa91c8c4939:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="efbcd19738664665836bf896f3652cf3"><span data-offset-key="efbcd19738664665836bf896f3652cf3:0"> the entire operation is considered </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="45d2f725fd774e44aea57f815a8951bf"><span data-offset-key="45d2f725fd774e44aea57f815a8951bf:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="8bd336191a79412b954da575c8f9967a"><span data-offset-key="8bd336191a79412b954da575c8f9967a:0"> and the right-hand side will never be evaluated at all. And unlike </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#not" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="979f98342994416f8d29d67e797fafdc"><span data-offset-key="979f98342994416f8d29d67e797fafdc:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">not</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a2b27f1f6db8491fb863903a67cb980d"><span data-offset-key="a2b27f1f6db8491fb863903a67cb980d:0"> it does not necessarily evaluate to either </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="566721886c494d4e8b54bebc63344e2e"><span data-offset-key="566721886c494d4e8b54bebc63344e2e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5dba6cfb65e947a2bfcbbc8f8bb8503a"><span data-offset-key="5dba6cfb65e947a2bfcbbc8f8bb8503a:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="489f9b0c8de04e8d858af68bb44f18cd"><span data-offset-key="489f9b0c8de04e8d858af68bb44f18cd:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="701f3b735ac7459aafbe3a0bf5b8d505"><span data-offset-key="701f3b735ac7459aafbe3a0bf5b8d505:0"> , evaluating instead to either the left side (if considered </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9c4c83cf82ac443fbd2ee759113ea2fa"><span data-offset-key="9c4c83cf82ac443fbd2ee759113ea2fa:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="8dd5a7be3cf8417ea38a6d3581cc8485"><span data-offset-key="8dd5a7be3cf8417ea38a6d3581cc8485:0"> ) or the right side.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="25c2eeda458c40268cf1659346fcc71d"><span data-offset-key="25c2eeda458c40268cf1659346fcc71d:0">Thus the usage:</span></span></span>

    EXPRESSION_A and EXPRESSION_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3e8ad5b325184646ab320bb702a66c62"><span data-offset-key="3e8ad5b325184646ab320bb702a66c62:0">Can be thought of as working like the following </span><span data-offset-key="3e8ad5b325184646ab320bb702a66c62:1">_ternary_</span><span data-offset-key="3e8ad5b325184646ab320bb702a66c62:2"> </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#if" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4c0ada15419c4b889dc66b91c6aa0ac6"><span data-offset-key="4c0ada15419c4b889dc66b91c6aa0ac6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">if</code></span></span></a><span data-key="f7a2dc7eb5824b1abfe8f1d3c812d4e2"><span data-offset-key="f7a2dc7eb5824b1abfe8f1d3c812d4e2:0"> :</span></span></span>

    EXPRESSION_B if EXPRESSION_A else EXPRESSION_A

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1d87c96a62e04aaf8d81e5ed4001b26c"><span data-offset-key="1d87c96a62e04aaf8d81e5ed4001b26c:0">Which is why you may one day find yourself surprised to find that </span><span data-offset-key="1d87c96a62e04aaf8d81e5ed4001b26c:1">`True and 1`</span><span data-offset-key="1d87c96a62e04aaf8d81e5ed4001b26c:2"> evaluates to </span><span data-offset-key="1d87c96a62e04aaf8d81e5ed4001b26c:3">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="1d87c96a62e04aaf8d81e5ed4001b26c:4"> while </span><span data-offset-key="1d87c96a62e04aaf8d81e5ed4001b26c:5">`1 and True`</span><span data-offset-key="1d87c96a62e04aaf8d81e5ed4001b26c:6"> evaluates to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d6295158faec49cf97ee7396bc39f226"><span data-offset-key="d6295158faec49cf97ee7396bc39f226:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a5ec01c3498744b38887e71e9dba4a51"><span data-offset-key="a5ec01c3498744b38887e71e9dba4a51:0"> .</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#or" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="65877357994742778471904c60a509e2"><span data-offset-key="65877357994742778471904c60a509e2:0">or</span></span></a><span data-key="12a7d22162d3470c95e1cef6c1ad7ca4"><span data-offset-key="12a7d22162d3470c95e1cef6c1ad7ca4:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#boolean-operations-and-or-not" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fc12eb488952411ba967b826d5279a53"><span data-offset-key="fc12eb488952411ba967b826d5279a53:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="e3201f2dc0fd4cd1a490e93b021ecf17"><span data-offset-key="e3201f2dc0fd4cd1a490e93b021ecf17:0">A </span><span data-offset-key="e3201f2dc0fd4cd1a490e93b021ecf17:1">_binary_</span><span data-offset-key="e3201f2dc0fd4cd1a490e93b021ecf17:2"> OPERATOR that checks the </span><span data-offset-key="e3201f2dc0fd4cd1a490e93b021ecf17:3">_truth-value_</span><span data-offset-key="e3201f2dc0fd4cd1a490e93b021ecf17:4"> of two things, evaluating to the thing on the left if it tested </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fcc052bf2657458c8930185195e9cf47"><span data-offset-key="fcc052bf2657458c8930185195e9cf47:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ef38b3bd447e49d1b064144d56530e83"><span data-offset-key="ef38b3bd447e49d1b064144d56530e83:0"> , otherwise to the thing on the right.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0ab605b6346f4a3a8ebd4355be29065c"><span data-offset-key="0ab605b6346f4a3a8ebd4355be29065c:0">Derived from the Old English conjunction </span><span data-offset-key="0ab605b6346f4a3a8ebd4355be29065c:1">**_oþþe_**</span><span data-offset-key="0ab605b6346f4a3a8ebd4355be29065c:2">, meaning “either”, and implying that either of the ideas conjoined are acceptable, as in “coffee </span><span data-offset-key="0ab605b6346f4a3a8ebd4355be29065c:3">**_or_**</span><span data-offset-key="0ab605b6346f4a3a8ebd4355be29065c:4"> tea”. In Python the meaning comes from </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logical_disjunction" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e1e28c7708354ddc8a912d61b4b24387"><span data-offset-key="e1e28c7708354ddc8a912d61b4b24387:0">logical disjunction</span></span></a><span data-key="77e742243fb741c58253a3fb496b4c87"><span data-offset-key="77e742243fb741c58253a3fb496b4c87:0">, and implies that either </span><span data-offset-key="77e742243fb741c58253a3fb496b4c87:1">_one_</span><span data-offset-key="77e742243fb741c58253a3fb496b4c87:2"> of the things it combines is true or the whole combination is false.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="da33ff5aebca44e7bcf9476d9c7070c7"><span data-offset-key="da33ff5aebca44e7bcf9476d9c7070c7:0">This is Python’s </span><span data-offset-key="da33ff5aebca44e7bcf9476d9c7070c7:1">_Boolean disjunction_</span><span data-offset-key="da33ff5aebca44e7bcf9476d9c7070c7:2"> OPERATOR; used whenever you need to test if </span><span data-offset-key="da33ff5aebca44e7bcf9476d9c7070c7:3">_either_</span><span data-offset-key="da33ff5aebca44e7bcf9476d9c7070c7:4"> side of the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#or" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c5e9dac3112a415783b301619cc05f65"><span data-offset-key="c5e9dac3112a415783b301619cc05f65:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">or</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ecf68db885034a84b8b138ee19e8f3cc"><span data-offset-key="ecf68db885034a84b8b138ee19e8f3cc:0"> is considered </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5b1453026edf4b6ab7448e4c1db5f528"><span data-offset-key="5b1453026edf4b6ab7448e4c1db5f528:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="90b093c8fe6b43cbbcc35a641a3e5201"><span data-offset-key="90b093c8fe6b43cbbcc35a641a3e5201:0"> . It is a </span><span data-offset-key="90b093c8fe6b43cbbcc35a641a3e5201:1">_short-circuiting_</span><span data-offset-key="90b093c8fe6b43cbbcc35a641a3e5201:2"> operation; if the left-hand EXPRESSION is considered </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="713a411ca2394b8c9f6ea277b6e6b76c"><span data-offset-key="713a411ca2394b8c9f6ea277b6e6b76c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="9127bb5ef786416f8dffb103e621da43"><span data-offset-key="9127bb5ef786416f8dffb103e621da43:0"> the entire operation is considered </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0e9a6559121d46bfae2eabcb37cf5921"><span data-offset-key="0e9a6559121d46bfae2eabcb37cf5921:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4a415299fe84417186188e0d27e7b987"><span data-offset-key="4a415299fe84417186188e0d27e7b987:0"> and the right-hand side will never be evaluated at all. Also, unlike </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#not" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a5cb73c86792489d9f61e2cc99ece288"><span data-offset-key="a5cb73c86792489d9f61e2cc99ece288:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">not</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e3c32780d17c4b11b0a6019785631bd1"><span data-offset-key="e3c32780d17c4b11b0a6019785631bd1:0"> it does not necessarily evaluate to either </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b9bcd746739249a099e8079ce230edd9"><span data-offset-key="b9bcd746739249a099e8079ce230edd9:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7421a49bd4ae43b6b1a035811b82cc49"><span data-offset-key="7421a49bd4ae43b6b1a035811b82cc49:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4df5c384da8c4a7a82e891ec7e7acaee"><span data-offset-key="4df5c384da8c4a7a82e891ec7e7acaee:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3ff091f17bd545d8a38adc4426824bfd"><span data-offset-key="3ff091f17bd545d8a38adc4426824bfd:0"> , evaluating instead to either the left side (if considered </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="971f40a975074ad899ede5b8f7e34efc"><span data-offset-key="971f40a975074ad899ede5b8f7e34efc:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b4a70733733f4ae4a927bd9a9c9bd79d"><span data-offset-key="b4a70733733f4ae4a927bd9a9c9bd79d:0"> ) or the right side.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bf73e90255cf471f8a5f300ea6b640df"><span data-offset-key="bf73e90255cf471f8a5f300ea6b640df:0">Thus the usage:</span></span></span>

    EXPRESSION_A or EXPRESSION_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="18587d54d56b4a308815b34b9fc00f66"><span data-offset-key="18587d54d56b4a308815b34b9fc00f66:0">Can be thought of as working like the following </span><span data-offset-key="18587d54d56b4a308815b34b9fc00f66:1">_ternary_</span><span data-offset-key="18587d54d56b4a308815b34b9fc00f66:2"> </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#if" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e7ee9b70c6ff4d6a8891e8098240705f"><span data-offset-key="e7ee9b70c6ff4d6a8891e8098240705f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">if</code></span></span></a><span data-key="533dfbf9138340c58f201a3536b65c74"><span data-offset-key="533dfbf9138340c58f201a3536b65c74:0"> :</span></span></span>

    EXPRESSION_A if EXPRESSION_A else EXPRESSION_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2aaa3418762a4ed09755158bd1629c6d"><span data-offset-key="2aaa3418762a4ed09755158bd1629c6d:0">This subtlety can catch you out when you find that </span><span data-offset-key="2aaa3418762a4ed09755158bd1629c6d:1">`True or 1`</span><span data-offset-key="2aaa3418762a4ed09755158bd1629c6d:2"> evaluates to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3d8a96f9b97547be97875fa53e050073"><span data-offset-key="3d8a96f9b97547be97875fa53e050073:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="f15c57737d0a417fb28ba4d5fe950dcc"><span data-offset-key="f15c57737d0a417fb28ba4d5fe950dcc:0"> but </span><span data-offset-key="f15c57737d0a417fb28ba4d5fe950dcc:1">`1 or True`</span><span data-offset-key="f15c57737d0a417fb28ba4d5fe950dcc:2"> evaluates to </span><span data-offset-key="f15c57737d0a417fb28ba4d5fe950dcc:3">`1`</span><span data-offset-key="f15c57737d0a417fb28ba4d5fe950dcc:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b339e8b88fac4ee4b22803c6a8992e8a"><span data-offset-key="b339e8b88fac4ee4b22803c6a8992e8a:0">**identity checking operator(s)**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e7f1809c6ea24601be9d8a1881cb42cd"><span data-offset-key="e7f1809c6ea24601be9d8a1881cb42cd:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cb8e0342f2d9460fad0fe12b61ef1f73"><span data-offset-key="cb8e0342f2d9460fad0fe12b61ef1f73:0">is</span></span></a><span data-key="7ef2ed6b79d94ce4bb9bf00c175acf43"><span data-offset-key="7ef2ed6b79d94ce4bb9bf00c175acf43:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/expressions.html#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="40b3c8c6f377434b80b56a6d51b789b9"><span data-offset-key="40b3c8c6f377434b80b56a6d51b789b9:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="d2998f5d6fba4c9b85a5756d8763e3e2"><span data-offset-key="d2998f5d6fba4c9b85a5756d8763e3e2:0">A </span><span data-offset-key="d2998f5d6fba4c9b85a5756d8763e3e2:1">_binary_</span><span data-offset-key="d2998f5d6fba4c9b85a5756d8763e3e2:2"> OPERATOR that tests if the OBJECT on the left has the same </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identity_%28object-oriented_programming%29" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4bd8475f6f194ef392b8d1503693b64e"><span data-offset-key="4bd8475f6f194ef392b8d1503693b64e:0">identity</span></span></a><span data-key="c1408812262943a1aba02aac9d4924e8"><span data-offset-key="c1408812262943a1aba02aac9d4924e8:0"> as the OBJECT on the right and then evaluates to either </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e4a7bae84cc74b17a4a6d3e533dd651a"><span data-offset-key="e4a7bae84cc74b17a4a6d3e533dd651a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a43949b628864ab59db633a0b2f24a2d"><span data-offset-key="a43949b628864ab59db633a0b2f24a2d:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f5ddde3edd0f4a2cbebf8e896d3b1d13"><span data-offset-key="f5ddde3edd0f4a2cbebf8e896d3b1d13:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3d025629ab0d46fb992ad70e1f3c71bd"><span data-offset-key="3d025629ab0d46fb992ad70e1f3c71bd:0"> .Can be inverted by </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#not" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="69269c5ec821497eaf97ab3eee835b8c"><span data-offset-key="69269c5ec821497eaf97ab3eee835b8c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">not</code></span></span></a><span data-key="32d0605df9bd481b85f45164dc44480d"><span data-offset-key="32d0605df9bd481b85f45164dc44480d:0"> to become the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="07c6b3b4c6a341ee8a4d6047f7255946"><span data-offset-key="07c6b3b4c6a341ee8a4d6047f7255946:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">is not</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b18d17edf6524259b66af2003ccfcb05"><span data-offset-key="b18d17edf6524259b66af2003ccfcb05:0"> operator.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6d7a5f7fb2d1482b851d6642e2174187"><span data-offset-key="6d7a5f7fb2d1482b851d6642e2174187:0">An Old English verb from the Germanic stem </span><span data-offset-key="6d7a5f7fb2d1482b851d6642e2174187:1">**_\*es-_**</span><span data-offset-key="6d7a5f7fb2d1482b851d6642e2174187:2">; it’s the third person singular present indicative form of the word </span><span data-offset-key="6d7a5f7fb2d1482b851d6642e2174187:3">**_be_**</span><span data-offset-key="6d7a5f7fb2d1482b851d6642e2174187:4">, so it generally means “to be \[a thing\]“. In Python its meaning is specific to </span><span data-offset-key="6d7a5f7fb2d1482b851d6642e2174187:5">_identity_</span><span data-offset-key="6d7a5f7fb2d1482b851d6642e2174187:6">, and implies something more like “to be \[some unique thing\]“.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="43ff34f539b24f468355b0411b1e937b"><span data-offset-key="43ff34f539b24f468355b0411b1e937b:0">The usage is straightforward:</span></span></span>

    EXPRESSION_A is EXPRESSION_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a4e2344b83034c5e93932ddf538a3d8e"><span data-offset-key="a4e2344b83034c5e93932ddf538a3d8e:0">And the usage with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#not" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cad50117619848d29b1f64b336290834"><span data-offset-key="cad50117619848d29b1f64b336290834:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">not</code></span></span></a><span data-key="dfffb1f18e4a45c18ae46f6389aff8cb"><span data-offset-key="dfffb1f18e4a45c18ae46f6389aff8cb:0"> is:</span></span></span>

    EXPRESSION_A is not EXPRESSION_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="faf94318bf1841f3824d8ff1507b60bd"><span data-offset-key="faf94318bf1841f3824d8ff1507b60bd:0">The notion of </span><span data-offset-key="faf94318bf1841f3824d8ff1507b60bd:1">_identity_</span><span data-offset-key="faf94318bf1841f3824d8ff1507b60bd:2"> is a little abstract, but think of it like this: Tom and Bob are twins, they’re the same height, age, and weight, and they share the same birthday, but they </span><span data-offset-key="faf94318bf1841f3824d8ff1507b60bd:3">_do not_</span><span data-offset-key="faf94318bf1841f3824d8ff1507b60bd:4"> have the same identity. Tom is Tom, and Bob is Bob, but Tom is not Bob.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f1082153b3f846e2aa9ef774f40764e1"><span data-offset-key="f1082153b3f846e2aa9ef774f40764e1:0">In most implementations of Python the identity of an OBJECT can be thought of as its unique address in memory, and since </span><span data-offset-key="f1082153b3f846e2aa9ef774f40764e1:1">_every_</span><span data-offset-key="f1082153b3f846e2aa9ef774f40764e1:2"> OBJECT you work with will have its own unique address, </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a11f70a72eea4d0e85b668afcfc108f7"><span data-offset-key="a11f70a72eea4d0e85b668afcfc108f7:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">is</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0dd154dd3b9c4d67abf97719370863d7"><span data-offset-key="0dd154dd3b9c4d67abf97719370863d7:0"> is usually only useful for telling if a NAME refers to a specific OBJECT:</span></span></span>

    NAME is OBJECTNAME is not OBJECT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8f6b4c2c0bd042ffa258fdcd4b9cef95"><span data-offset-key="8f6b4c2c0bd042ffa258fdcd4b9cef95:0">Or for testing if two different NAMEs refer to the same OBJECT in memory.</span></span></span>

    NAME is OTHER_NAMENAME is not OTHER_NAME

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7a5975c0302c4d9a8b08acbb96060617"><span data-offset-key="7a5975c0302c4d9a8b08acbb96060617:0">There </span><span data-offset-key="7a5975c0302c4d9a8b08acbb96060617:1">_are_</span><span data-offset-key="7a5975c0302c4d9a8b08acbb96060617:2"> however some special cases: for instance, </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5bb26dd8572e48bc87bcb0fcf02809e9"><span data-offset-key="5bb26dd8572e48bc87bcb0fcf02809e9:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a3eb4567511d48d79b4db2d5069d9f5f"><span data-offset-key="a3eb4567511d48d79b4db2d5069d9f5f:0"> , </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1ad27fed5ff24287b3a65fe102aeb5d8"><span data-offset-key="1ad27fed5ff24287b3a65fe102aeb5d8:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="76553cb828fc4d4bac96d194d2e33290"><span data-offset-key="76553cb828fc4d4bac96d194d2e33290:0"> , and </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#none" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9a55fdc5bdb14c1491a629b056ec8ccb"><span data-offset-key="9a55fdc5bdb14c1491a629b056ec8ccb:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">None</code></span></span></a><span data-key="1ae611e91e38458cb61af160d1d07b2f"><span data-offset-key="1ae611e91e38458cb61af160d1d07b2f:0"> are all </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Singleton_pattern" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4b49a62dd9a946d2bf06e4bd479ef8b7"><span data-offset-key="4b49a62dd9a946d2bf06e4bd479ef8b7:0">singletons</span></span></a><span data-key="94363206f7164632895dfa5df2ee8147"><span data-offset-key="94363206f7164632895dfa5df2ee8147:0"> in memory, meaning there is only </span><span data-offset-key="94363206f7164632895dfa5df2ee8147:1">_ever_</span><span data-offset-key="94363206f7164632895dfa5df2ee8147:2"> one copy of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4dd7b651fb8b4031bd13e66096f1d63d"><span data-offset-key="4dd7b651fb8b4031bd13e66096f1d63d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2"><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:0"> in </span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:1">_any_</span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:2"> Python program. For the most part this is just a space-saving detail you don’t need to worry about, but it explains why in Python we use </span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:3">`VALUE == True`</span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:5">_not_</span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:6"> </span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:7">`VALUE is True`</span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:8"> when checking if something is considered </span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:9">_equivalent_</span><span data-offset-key="81812dbf284147e3b0ff739ef06132b2:10"> to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="57c54692c7104c43a08d5ebb526cb2b8"><span data-offset-key="57c54692c7104c43a08d5ebb526cb2b8:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7c2416638378431b8e5babd69b33019c"><span data-offset-key="7c2416638378431b8e5babd69b33019c:0"> . Testing </span><span data-offset-key="7c2416638378431b8e5babd69b33019c:1">_identity_</span><span data-offset-key="7c2416638378431b8e5babd69b33019c:2"> is </span><span data-offset-key="7c2416638378431b8e5babd69b33019c:3">_not_</span><span data-offset-key="7c2416638378431b8e5babd69b33019c:4"> the same as testing </span><span data-offset-key="7c2416638378431b8e5babd69b33019c:5">_value_</span><span data-offset-key="7c2416638378431b8e5babd69b33019c:6">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ac2d92f69ffe464d9ed44df235ffba14"><span data-offset-key="ac2d92f69ffe464d9ed44df235ffba14:0">For this reason the uses of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2bb47eab18744b79943c2c97190946a2"><span data-offset-key="2bb47eab18744b79943c2c97190946a2:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">is</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5632135bc99846d5a197322965f30e5d"><span data-offset-key="5632135bc99846d5a197322965f30e5d:0"> are limited and specific, which is why you’ll only rarely see </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d282ebc209e74c7988c8adff1897403b"><span data-offset-key="d282ebc209e74c7988c8adff1897403b:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">is</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c573f96d2fd2426980c26bc632e3580c"><span data-offset-key="c573f96d2fd2426980c26bc632e3580c:0"> and </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="345e99cc2b844d54806b98189c6c0f5e"><span data-offset-key="345e99cc2b844d54806b98189c6c0f5e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">is not</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2571e2f1bb5c47f38a49f6155d3c6038"><span data-offset-key="2571e2f1bb5c47f38a49f6155d3c6038:0"> used in practice.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="974640ce20314c44b1517627d8f5a04f"><span data-offset-key="974640ce20314c44b1517627d8f5a04f:0">**membership testing operator(s)**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d60386450dff4253b1c80f82f83d865e"><span data-offset-key="d60386450dff4253b1c80f82f83d865e:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#in" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3027c8f470f64df3b96071819dbf9373"><span data-offset-key="3027c8f470f64df3b96071819dbf9373:0">in</span></span></a><span data-key="2c755b4371c7464b936e53352aa1fd0f"><span data-offset-key="2c755b4371c7464b936e53352aa1fd0f:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/expressions.html#membership-test-operations" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b8fc62d48ba04dc8b43f9743646df80f"><span data-offset-key="b8fc62d48ba04dc8b43f9743646df80f:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="ca517ba6315c44dd8c85080575126678"><span data-offset-key="ca517ba6315c44dd8c85080575126678:0">A </span><span data-offset-key="ca517ba6315c44dd8c85080575126678:1">_binary_</span><span data-offset-key="ca517ba6315c44dd8c85080575126678:2"> OPERATOR that tests if the OBJECT on the left is a member of the COLLECTION on the right and then evaluates to either </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="264dfe83854d49b4bd6f38b6de2e564e"><span data-offset-key="264dfe83854d49b4bd6f38b6de2e564e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="f2643bd2ced94bb2a8b5c92010f15ab4"><span data-offset-key="f2643bd2ced94bb2a8b5c92010f15ab4:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ba5970c837bd4f9d87f792d6d8a2a7e8"><span data-offset-key="ba5970c837bd4f9d87f792d6d8a2a7e8:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3d604c180d5d4cfe8c227616b63ee49b"><span data-offset-key="3d604c180d5d4cfe8c227616b63ee49b:0"> . Also known as Python’s </span><span data-offset-key="3d604c180d5d4cfe8c227616b63ee49b:1">_inclusion operator_</span><span data-offset-key="3d604c180d5d4cfe8c227616b63ee49b:2">.Can be inverted by </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#not" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="075e36179f624b5da886e9cb84ffa55a"><span data-offset-key="075e36179f624b5da886e9cb84ffa55a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">not</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3afe043fc910429b8c3d0941f76128cd"><span data-offset-key="3afe043fc910429b8c3d0941f76128cd:0"> to become the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#in" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="dffeb5dbaa76417a9881a0b472c3dde1"><span data-offset-key="dffeb5dbaa76417a9881a0b472c3dde1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">not in</code></span></span></a><span data-key="fc5ce96a160d4b00baaf47a165e0b31f"><span data-offset-key="fc5ce96a160d4b00baaf47a165e0b31f:0"> </span><span data-offset-key="fc5ce96a160d4b00baaf47a165e0b31f:1">_exclusion operator_</span><span data-offset-key="fc5ce96a160d4b00baaf47a165e0b31f:2">.Also used with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="99e35b7980a644dca45e709049e643d5"><span data-offset-key="99e35b7980a644dca45e709049e643d5:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="793219f66e394443adc3fbf01880342d"><span data-offset-key="793219f66e394443adc3fbf01880342d:0"> , see below.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00"><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:0">A Middle English merger of the Old English words </span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:1">**_in_**</span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:2">, meaning “among”, and </span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:3">**_inne_**</span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:4">, meaning “within” or “inside”. The merged word has many usages and meanings, but the general sense here is from the prepositional form, which implies that some thing is contained within or inside some larger thing, as in “a page </span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:5">**_in_**</span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:6"> a book” or “a book </span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:7">**_in_**</span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:8"> a library”. In Python it is specifically used for </span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:9">_membership testing_</span><span data-offset-key="6be11b1edc3a4a8cba3e367515bc7e00:10">, when checking if an item is contained within a group of items.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d17b19824fd746548b694f6999eb0fe8"><span data-offset-key="d17b19824fd746548b694f6999eb0fe8:0">The usual usage of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#in" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a72226fce70d4092b6a6508d697f753c"><span data-offset-key="a72226fce70d4092b6a6508d697f753c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">in</code></span></span></a><span data-key="46e585365f7e49338d228c9306fc0ce2"><span data-offset-key="46e585365f7e49338d228c9306fc0ce2:0"> is to test if an OBJECT is a member of a specific CONTAINER:</span></span></span>

    OBJECT in CONTAINER

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9137f07e2c784e178940984a48bd519e"><span data-offset-key="9137f07e2c784e178940984a48bd519e:0">Or to test if OBJECT is </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#not" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="35d69fa14c324766be6f31202a6658ff"><span data-offset-key="35d69fa14c324766be6f31202a6658ff:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">not</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3738fd21d7044a0c95d3d724cd1a683d"><span data-offset-key="3738fd21d7044a0c95d3d724cd1a683d:0"> a member of CONTAINER:</span></span></span>

    OBJECT not in CONTAINER

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1c660d52fecf41ecb3990c366097d5bc"><span data-offset-key="1c660d52fecf41ecb3990c366097d5bc:0">It can be tempting to think you can use </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e8f0e45a5b814f60a146da130f70ccb6"><span data-offset-key="e8f0e45a5b814f60a146da130f70ccb6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">is</code></span></span></a><span data-key="27658cc0eabc4aa7931ec3ceb383efc4"><span data-offset-key="27658cc0eabc4aa7931ec3ceb383efc4:0"> with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#in" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f80856f579844d7b9787796956ebfeaa"><span data-offset-key="f80856f579844d7b9787796956ebfeaa:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">in</code></span></span></a><span data-key="1a1be8ebc2864e5bacd86c6a11d2ea4d"><span data-offset-key="1a1be8ebc2864e5bacd86c6a11d2ea4d:0"> , but that’s invalid syntax. It helps to remember that since </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fc6441c19bef462b81a135fb347f388a"><span data-offset-key="fc6441c19bef462b81a135fb347f388a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">is</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c314087f89b34831a450874f801be1ac"><span data-offset-key="c314087f89b34831a450874f801be1ac:0"> , </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#is" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a309412acdb8446b8667330b695f6b83"><span data-offset-key="a309412acdb8446b8667330b695f6b83:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">is not</code></span></span></a><span data-key="38d0a8f54a104530a621bbaa4e9da364"><span data-offset-key="38d0a8f54a104530a621bbaa4e9da364:0"> , </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#in" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="026a943d51ed4185bb0ba76219611b19"><span data-offset-key="026a943d51ed4185bb0ba76219611b19:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">in</code></span></span></a><span data-key="00b73cd9dcdf4c04912448e1d99b5e50"><span data-offset-key="00b73cd9dcdf4c04912448e1d99b5e50:0"> , and </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#in" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="bcb12f664e934d7f8482fef1b4675eaa"><span data-offset-key="bcb12f664e934d7f8482fef1b4675eaa:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">not in</code></span></span></a><span data-key="fd306755b4284af9bca9d6d3e4f24f79"><span data-offset-key="fd306755b4284af9bca9d6d3e4f24f79:0"> are all binary OPERATORs they </span><span data-offset-key="fd306755b4284af9bca9d6d3e4f24f79:1">_must_</span><span data-offset-key="fd306755b4284af9bca9d6d3e4f24f79:2"> have either an OBJECT or EXPRESSION on either side, </span><span data-offset-key="fd306755b4284af9bca9d6d3e4f24f79:3">_not_</span><span data-offset-key="fd306755b4284af9bca9d6d3e4f24f79:4"> another KEYWORD.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fcacfc4c12e24ff0bb46fd7002c40ebf"><span data-offset-key="fcacfc4c12e24ff0bb46fd7002c40ebf:0">Four Used to Loop</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="00887e476fc6475badd1aa7c4d5861d6"><span data-offset-key="00887e476fc6475badd1aa7c4d5861d6:0">The above keywords give you everything you need to perform simple decision making and to take basic actions, but they’re useless whenever you need to do something </span><span data-offset-key="00887e476fc6475badd1aa7c4d5861d6:1">_repeatedly_</span><span data-offset-key="00887e476fc6475badd1aa7c4d5861d6:2">; that’s where </span><span data-offset-key="00887e476fc6475badd1aa7c4d5861d6:3">_looping_</span><span data-offset-key="00887e476fc6475badd1aa7c4d5861d6:4"> comes in. In Python the following four keywords give you everything you need to do that.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="65d7d231b065413ab0fe41b0672e6d12"><span data-offset-key="65d7d231b065413ab0fe41b0672e6d12:0">**starting a loop**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6cce96b2f39b46b48575b388c0100dd3"><span data-offset-key="6cce96b2f39b46b48575b388c0100dd3:0">There are two ways to start a loop in Python, and they’re conceptually pretty similar, but your choice of which depends a great deal on exactly what you need to do with that loop.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dce5a6b5460748959cd8f1cbec413741"><span data-offset-key="dce5a6b5460748959cd8f1cbec413741:0">**looping until some condition is reached**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5cbb677b8f624e248cb905f4eecfb172"><span data-offset-key="5cbb677b8f624e248cb905f4eecfb172:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0e0917df123d4d9f8a5825e3f5d9790c"><span data-offset-key="0e0917df123d4d9f8a5825e3f5d9790c:0">while</span></span></a><span data-key="f742ea8369ad43cdbd15cb2ce0a65f81"><span data-offset-key="f742ea8369ad43cdbd15cb2ce0a65f81:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#the-while-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0cbd5d5474d54730aacc066c441ac2b5"><span data-offset-key="0cbd5d5474d54730aacc066c441ac2b5:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="cbcedf5a56bc493b8d85d6d9db0b3dad"><span data-offset-key="cbcedf5a56bc493b8d85d6d9db0b3dad:0">Starts a loop BLOCK by testing a the truth-value of an EXPRESSION; will iterate continuously until EXPRESSION evaluates to False.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250"><span data-offset-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250:0">From the Old English word </span><span data-offset-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250:1">**_hwile_**</span><span data-offset-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250:2"> for “a duration of time”, but here we’re using the conjunctive form which implies “\[during the\] time \[that something is true\]” or “for as long as \[something is true\]“. In programming languages the keyword is always associated with something to </span><span data-offset-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250:3">_test_</span><span data-offset-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250:4"> and something to </span><span data-offset-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250:5">_do_</span><span data-offset-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250:6">, so the meaning becomes “</span><span data-offset-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250:7">**_while_**</span><span data-offset-key="f95663eccdca430ea9df12d6595c4250:8"> \[the test is true\], \[do something\]“.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="767ed842265d4fceac56d3e72f6b1b3a"><span data-offset-key="767ed842265d4fceac56d3e72f6b1b3a:0">The form of a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ecf40a66a9b24deea0ff55f8ce6ee5f8"><span data-offset-key="ecf40a66a9b24deea0ff55f8ce6ee5f8:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">while</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b30aaad92ff2443a9eebb5e9ba2e9598"><span data-offset-key="b30aaad92ff2443a9eebb5e9ba2e9598:0"> loop BLOCK is always the same:</span></span></span>

    while EXPRESSION:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8bc38b17cded429e9f0a89ccac005b95"><span data-offset-key="8bc38b17cded429e9f0a89ccac005b95:0">If the EXPRESSION evaluates as </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="7040f702a9a84966ada18642b75649ea"><span data-offset-key="7040f702a9a84966ada18642b75649ea:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7dc756dfcf974fabaaa22f4c83caea54"><span data-offset-key="7dc756dfcf974fabaaa22f4c83caea54:0"> then STATEMENT will be reached and executed. When the end of the indented BLOCK is reached, control returns immediately to the top, then EXPRESSION is tested again, and so on. So long as EXPRESSION evaluates as </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3eaceb47f7504766a3e7b2de0f7cb394"><span data-offset-key="3eaceb47f7504766a3e7b2de0f7cb394:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="15708cf1f1204c498a4bab361c937f84"><span data-offset-key="15708cf1f1204c498a4bab361c937f84:0"> the entire indented BLOCK will be run again and again.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8d2c7418c0504ed49b2d13272a427260"><span data-offset-key="8d2c7418c0504ed49b2d13272a427260:0">The </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c9ff050f34e44f57af1b73beec26a374"><span data-offset-key="c9ff050f34e44f57af1b73beec26a374:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">while</code></span></span></a><span data-key="89c527416c434e34996f9f099b8f7538"><span data-offset-key="89c527416c434e34996f9f099b8f7538:0"> loop can also </span><span data-offset-key="89c527416c434e34996f9f099b8f7538:1">_optionally_</span><span data-offset-key="89c527416c434e34996f9f099b8f7538:2"> be terminated by an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#else" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6d26157c63424bfcb15793a0823f4da5"><span data-offset-key="6d26157c63424bfcb15793a0823f4da5:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">else</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3498f2fe66d44c0cbd6b0e7fce4c1ca7"><span data-offset-key="3498f2fe66d44c0cbd6b0e7fce4c1ca7:0"> BLOCK:</span></span></span>

    while EXPRESSION:    [...]else:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ce078595ceb743fca8e665e983522040"><span data-offset-key="ce078595ceb743fca8e665e983522040:0">In this case the STATEMENT inside the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#else" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9008d3dad4644bb69aa5ae74f63bc465"><span data-offset-key="9008d3dad4644bb69aa5ae74f63bc465:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">else</code></span></span></a><span data-key="1cfe369dd08a4c428d9b3da664af1b2a"><span data-offset-key="1cfe369dd08a4c428d9b3da664af1b2a:0"> block will executed if the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a920930051c04624957f82745142e858"><span data-offset-key="a920930051c04624957f82745142e858:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">while</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b5fd3b52fc2f4905b1afd266c18d248a"><span data-offset-key="b5fd3b52fc2f4905b1afd266c18d248a:0"> loop runs all the way to completion (its test evaluates to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4221816d15ee482d9dac4c9ea892cd2a"><span data-offset-key="4221816d15ee482d9dac4c9ea892cd2a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="42a580e259ef4c29a5ff5676b3fec052"><span data-offset-key="42a580e259ef4c29a5ff5676b3fec052:0"> ) </span><span data-offset-key="42a580e259ef4c29a5ff5676b3fec052:1">_without_</span><span data-offset-key="42a580e259ef4c29a5ff5676b3fec052:2"> encountering </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#break" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="39f3208664784e83b8b716e28cac3d98"><span data-offset-key="39f3208664784e83b8b716e28cac3d98:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">break</code></span></span></a><span data-key="93b35c2d03744215bb3eaa629cc83ea7"><span data-offset-key="93b35c2d03744215bb3eaa629cc83ea7:0"> . This can be useful when there is some cleanup action that needs to occur when a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="df5c3565511d4eb0b8600f702285f340"><span data-offset-key="df5c3565511d4eb0b8600f702285f340:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">while</code></span></span></a><span data-key="f16d12b5dc4247b3a3bf9119c9142273"><span data-offset-key="f16d12b5dc4247b3a3bf9119c9142273:0"> loop has exited naturally.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d87d625a7c6545f3a742d0a9739e2f8b"><span data-offset-key="d87d625a7c6545f3a742d0a9739e2f8b:0">The </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8477ec9751724d3cba181b77f82d29c3"><span data-offset-key="8477ec9751724d3cba181b77f82d29c3:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">while</code></span></span></a><span data-key="05e08bcb7701446c827eb602d7bda5c8"><span data-offset-key="05e08bcb7701446c827eb602d7bda5c8:0"> is the most basic form of loop, but it’s a little dangerous if not used with care. This is because any EXPRESSION that </span><span data-offset-key="05e08bcb7701446c827eb602d7bda5c8:1">_always_</span><span data-offset-key="05e08bcb7701446c827eb602d7bda5c8:2"> evaluates as </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9e6cba34fbd64077857d533d2c24aa47"><span data-offset-key="9e6cba34fbd64077857d533d2c24aa47:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="007a16a54c1b4788916c9cd550c91a65"><span data-offset-key="007a16a54c1b4788916c9cd550c91a65:0"> will run </span><span data-offset-key="007a16a54c1b4788916c9cd550c91a65:1">_forever_</span><span data-offset-key="007a16a54c1b4788916c9cd550c91a65:2">. For this reason it’s generally important to design the EXPRESSION so that it will </span><span data-offset-key="007a16a54c1b4788916c9cd550c91a65:3">_eventually_</span><span data-offset-key="007a16a54c1b4788916c9cd550c91a65:4"> evaluate to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#false" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="7e6eeb3b1149431dbed5d65db6895ddc"><span data-offset-key="7e6eeb3b1149431dbed5d65db6895ddc:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">False</code></span></span></a><span data-key="532864161c44460f89030e608fd94590"><span data-offset-key="532864161c44460f89030e608fd94590:0"> .</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5dcf3ec464cb40a4b7a8ac767dcf4580"><span data-offset-key="5dcf3ec464cb40a4b7a8ac767dcf4580:0">**looping through the members of a collection**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d44925f4428a4d6d971029255c805e2c"><span data-offset-key="d44925f4428a4d6d971029255c805e2c:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="965cf6c93c0d4339ab255652ff38e304"><span data-offset-key="965cf6c93c0d4339ab255652ff38e304:0">for</span></span></a><span data-key="b114e530d47a45a9aaeac8f80674316f"><span data-offset-key="b114e530d47a45a9aaeac8f80674316f:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#the-for-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b68d53e353df49249e3adad7a9fb9744"><span data-offset-key="b68d53e353df49249e3adad7a9fb9744:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="62d9d610e5cc4a22a8a11e394908c81b"><span data-offset-key="62d9d610e5cc4a22a8a11e394908c81b:0">Starts a loop BLOCK that will iterate </span><span data-offset-key="62d9d610e5cc4a22a8a11e394908c81b:1">_once_</span><span data-offset-key="62d9d610e5cc4a22a8a11e394908c81b:2"> over a COLLECTION, visiting every item in it.Can also be marked with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cc5393bdc5a449e780a4ba419644aff9"><span data-offset-key="cc5393bdc5a449e780a4ba419644aff9:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2a3678ba79694731b341f8d22045d4f9"><span data-offset-key="2a3678ba79694731b341f8d22045d4f9:0"> , to start an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="41fbb43d4c384646a219d011ff3b20d3"><span data-offset-key="41fbb43d4c384646a219d011ff3b20d3:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e98c5326eaa14f62b064473de4c13586"><span data-offset-key="e98c5326eaa14f62b064473de4c13586:0"> loop, see below.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4"><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:0">An Old English word via the German </span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:1">**_für_**</span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:2"> with a great many meanings; the general meaning is taken from a prepositional sense of “\[performing an action\] on behalf of \[some thing\]“. In computing, though, the meaning is actually taken from the contraction of the word </span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:3">**_for_**</span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:4"> with either </span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:5">**_every_**</span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:6"> (meaning “each \[item\] in a group”) or </span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:7">**_each_**</span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:8"> (meaning “all \[of a group\]“) to form </span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:9">**_for every_**</span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:10"> or </span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:11">**_for each_**</span><span data-offset-key="4b684fb66bbe44699b6510b4a55f6db4:12">, both of which mean “\[to perform an action\] on behalf of each item \[in a group\]“. In programming languages that descend from ALGOL </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/For_loop" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1439bc0e7a1146f5837a0b87853d320a"><span data-offset-key="1439bc0e7a1146f5837a0b87853d320a:0"><strong><em>for</em></strong></span></span></a><span data-key="bb0ada06a1ee4272a9d127b6b3b6f000"><span data-offset-key="bb0ada06a1ee4272a9d127b6b3b6f000:0"> has traditionally been the most common name for such a loop, with </span><span data-offset-key="bb0ada06a1ee4272a9d127b6b3b6f000:1">**_do_**</span><span data-offset-key="bb0ada06a1ee4272a9d127b6b3b6f000:2"> used in a smaller number of languages. Python takes the name from the traditional usage in ALGOL via C, however it is more accurate to describe Python’s version as a </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreach_loop" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2d96a04003f844adb7627feafc3a3393"><span data-offset-key="2d96a04003f844adb7627feafc3a3393:0"><strong><em>foreach</em></strong></span></span></a><span data-key="a6dfb2f2e4cf4d049c6325b9ca00d040"><span data-offset-key="a6dfb2f2e4cf4d049c6325b9ca00d040:0"> loop, because there is no explicit counter and the thing being looped over must be </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iteration" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a014ddeea7bc400da3e4f823526b9583"><span data-offset-key="a014ddeea7bc400da3e4f823526b9583:0"><em>iterable</em></span></span></a><span data-key="9633150d7414421e913290f7e3d3793c"><span data-offset-key="9633150d7414421e913290f7e3d3793c:0">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="06f650ff039a4c91a110c351c6975056"><span data-offset-key="06f650ff039a4c91a110c351c6975056:0">The usage of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c393026001964020ba1bed933f2e19ac"><span data-offset-key="c393026001964020ba1bed933f2e19ac:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5c0d5547982a4c0db91c8adb2f74f328"><span data-offset-key="5c0d5547982a4c0db91c8adb2f74f328:0"> consistently involves assigning a user-assigned NAME to every OBJECT </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#in" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="17a627dc94f243b8b4517b64cca9497c"><span data-offset-key="17a627dc94f243b8b4517b64cca9497c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">in</code></span></span></a><span data-key="1a775e1d89bb4e9fb01d86a06c537cae"><span data-offset-key="1a775e1d89bb4e9fb01d86a06c537cae:0"> a COLLECTION.</span></span></span>

    for NAME in COLLECTION:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6458b3fbfa424b49907c30f92bdee4a6"><span data-offset-key="6458b3fbfa424b49907c30f92bdee4a6:0">Thus </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f169aaf7af234a9d9dd2b723e5d25765"><span data-offset-key="f169aaf7af234a9d9dd2b723e5d25765:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="aa4a3379eccc464aac7d216c02387e67"><span data-offset-key="aa4a3379eccc464aac7d216c02387e67:0"> every item in the COLLECTION the NAME will refer to that item </span><span data-offset-key="aa4a3379eccc464aac7d216c02387e67:1">_inside_</span><span data-offset-key="aa4a3379eccc464aac7d216c02387e67:2"> the scope of the BLOCK; this allows the STATEMENT to use NAME to act on that thing.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a7869c0838ab4f84bab54cb8ac5b3dbd"><span data-offset-key="a7869c0838ab4f84bab54cb8ac5b3dbd:0">This can be a little easier to grasp if you think of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0f1a85ed6b2c4bf7912377278baaa083"><span data-offset-key="0f1a85ed6b2c4bf7912377278baaa083:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4342317e29504194b2be8ef900d32a0d"><span data-offset-key="4342317e29504194b2be8ef900d32a0d:0"> as a specialized form of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2c85e49fa1fa4ef992dcde19005c4cdf"><span data-offset-key="2c85e49fa1fa4ef992dcde19005c4cdf:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">while</code></span></span></a><span data-key="fb5b16fa6bd446878527391c2d1ddf28"><span data-offset-key="fb5b16fa6bd446878527391c2d1ddf28:0"> loop:</span></span></span>

    while [items remain in COLLECTION to visit]:    NAME = [increment to the next item]    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="aca8e30cc2024016bbfcacd3eacf8bdc"><span data-offset-key="aca8e30cc2024016bbfcacd3eacf8bdc:0">But obviously the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ee415bf8427e49cd81ec58238f7d0321"><span data-offset-key="ee415bf8427e49cd81ec58238f7d0321:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b551cd132abc4dda8795dcd86f8bc943"><span data-offset-key="b551cd132abc4dda8795dcd86f8bc943:0"> loop is much simpler to work with, as you don’t need to worry about implementing the machinery necessary to track the start and stop conditions of the loop. You’ll find that you can, and usually should, use a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="563333542c2d4959b14968dd27a6dfc5"><span data-offset-key="563333542c2d4959b14968dd27a6dfc5:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e7da132bc20f41ccb9258185f1560706"><span data-offset-key="e7da132bc20f41ccb9258185f1560706:0"> loop whenever you’re visiting the individual contents of a COLLECTION, rather than risk a runaway </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ad0b1c6e3d164af7bf3f02a7b0f5f5f6"><span data-offset-key="ad0b1c6e3d164af7bf3f02a7b0f5f5f6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">while</code></span></span></a><span data-key="32f8b81d99204f128b88a52db3c845b6"><span data-offset-key="32f8b81d99204f128b88a52db3c845b6:0"> loop.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="364360d5a43c4da198b0c85bc9fccd67"><span data-offset-key="364360d5a43c4da198b0c85bc9fccd67:0">The </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="45df1196012b4aefa949db65288ebd81"><span data-offset-key="45df1196012b4aefa949db65288ebd81:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0c09dbbb44a24840bfc7747333c3c3b3"><span data-offset-key="0c09dbbb44a24840bfc7747333c3c3b3:0"> loop can also </span><span data-offset-key="0c09dbbb44a24840bfc7747333c3c3b3:1">_optionally_</span><span data-offset-key="0c09dbbb44a24840bfc7747333c3c3b3:2"> be terminated by an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#else" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fddaf280daf240118c6e460584ee0516"><span data-offset-key="fddaf280daf240118c6e460584ee0516:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">else</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3711709c9f8442b49178ae8323ad394e"><span data-offset-key="3711709c9f8442b49178ae8323ad394e:0"> BLOCK:</span></span></span>

    for NAME in COLLECTION:    [...]else:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="122a3ddf2b3e4a4bab6fdab7bed18978"><span data-offset-key="122a3ddf2b3e4a4bab6fdab7bed18978:0">In this case the STATEMENT inside the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#else" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4ebdf0545a9c4fb5b342ab2252165329"><span data-offset-key="4ebdf0545a9c4fb5b342ab2252165329:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">else</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b6ba928affc74bf3a51312895cf3e407"><span data-offset-key="b6ba928affc74bf3a51312895cf3e407:0"> block will executed if the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="586ec09618324071b22b9667ea09534c"><span data-offset-key="586ec09618324071b22b9667ea09534c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2a1642b0f5554aea9c17cbc4780785b2"><span data-offset-key="2a1642b0f5554aea9c17cbc4780785b2:0"> loop has run to completion </span><span data-offset-key="2a1642b0f5554aea9c17cbc4780785b2:1">_without_</span><span data-offset-key="2a1642b0f5554aea9c17cbc4780785b2:2"> encountering </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#break" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0ed961d394aa407396c77d4c5086a245"><span data-offset-key="0ed961d394aa407396c77d4c5086a245:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">break</code></span></span></a><span data-key="384125f2c2b94fa482da3ad8d931c750"><span data-offset-key="384125f2c2b94fa482da3ad8d931c750:0"> . This can be useful when there is some cleanup action that needs to occur when a </span><span data-offset-key="384125f2c2b94fa482da3ad8d931c750:1">`for`</span><span data-offset-key="384125f2c2b94fa482da3ad8d931c750:2"> loop has exited naturally.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0a8633fc4fa74c44af04a39cfd1de4df"><span data-offset-key="0a8633fc4fa74c44af04a39cfd1de4df:0">**controlling a loop**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b8b41ef0fc094d92b262caa1a24c9f59"><span data-offset-key="b8b41ef0fc094d92b262caa1a24c9f59:0">You don’t always want to simply run the loop to completion; there may be good reason to exit early, or to skip a round of the loop.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#break" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a4d21fa91ef14110bfd489637b42a1f1"><span data-offset-key="a4d21fa91ef14110bfd489637b42a1f1:0">break</span></span></a><span data-key="05a636ec196341dd9de51e9a698928da"><span data-offset-key="05a636ec196341dd9de51e9a698928da:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-break-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="84b7ad16e0134a9897a83afb99b05bde"><span data-offset-key="84b7ad16e0134a9897a83afb99b05bde:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="d0c6332bcd1042828aa53cfea3aa519f"><span data-offset-key="d0c6332bcd1042828aa53cfea3aa519f:0">Used to immediately interrupt the current loop iteration, ending the BLOCK it is found within. For this reason must </span><span data-offset-key="d0c6332bcd1042828aa53cfea3aa519f:1">_only_</span><span data-offset-key="d0c6332bcd1042828aa53cfea3aa519f:2"> be used within a loop BLOCK.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f3a7ed61c035489bac31f9febcf84ac7"><span data-offset-key="f3a7ed61c035489bac31f9febcf84ac7:0">From the Old English word </span><span data-offset-key="f3a7ed61c035489bac31f9febcf84ac7:1">**_brecan_**</span><span data-offset-key="f3a7ed61c035489bac31f9febcf84ac7:2">, which has several forms and meanings. The noun form generally means “to damage, destroy, or render unusable”, as in “to </span><span data-offset-key="f3a7ed61c035489bac31f9febcf84ac7:3">**_break_**</span><span data-offset-key="f3a7ed61c035489bac31f9febcf84ac7:4"> a leg”. Here, however, we use the alternative meaning “to interrupt \[a continuous sequence\]“, as in “to </span><span data-offset-key="f3a7ed61c035489bac31f9febcf84ac7:5">**_break_**</span><span data-offset-key="f3a7ed61c035489bac31f9febcf84ac7:6"> an electrical circuit”. In programming it specifically means to interrupt a loop from inside that loop.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ede945df736e460e872344dc0f9749d9"><span data-offset-key="ede945df736e460e872344dc0f9749d9:0">The </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#break" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="741d202b669441eda05ef04f469bc7b2"><span data-offset-key="741d202b669441eda05ef04f469bc7b2:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">break</code></span></span></a><span data-key="53be77a51c194d9594969b8407bad661"><span data-offset-key="53be77a51c194d9594969b8407bad661:0"> statement always forms a line of its own, and it </span><span data-offset-key="53be77a51c194d9594969b8407bad661:1">_must_</span><span data-offset-key="53be77a51c194d9594969b8407bad661:2"> be used in either a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ce41a7ed7c034944bd9eaac27bb6dfd0"><span data-offset-key="ce41a7ed7c034944bd9eaac27bb6dfd0:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="8e3e9566e24c4aa889e7a1ef12eb5640"><span data-offset-key="8e3e9566e24c4aa889e7a1ef12eb5640:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cf8aaa18cba6413f8ece2c58683bcb95"><span data-offset-key="cf8aaa18cba6413f8ece2c58683bcb95:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">while</code></span></span></a><span data-key="64f97714d6e2418fb6fc097e2a621d11"><span data-offset-key="64f97714d6e2418fb6fc097e2a621d11:0"> loop. The most common use is to stop a loop immediately if some particular condition is reached:</span></span></span>

    while True:    if EXPRESSION:        break    STATEMENT

    for NAME in COLLECTION:    if EXPRESSION:        break    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="189546c8ed1d482b830d818f1e7663dc"><span data-offset-key="189546c8ed1d482b830d818f1e7663dc:0">This is particularly useful if there’s some situation that warrants stopping the loop before it would normally be completed.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#continue" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d2499271c6a045e7b83abe416651c101"><span data-offset-key="d2499271c6a045e7b83abe416651c101:0">continue</span></span></a><span data-key="0ab830bbec584467b7edf3420ded2976"><span data-offset-key="0ab830bbec584467b7edf3420ded2976:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-continue-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c9801158860b42909e3c82a307623089"><span data-offset-key="c9801158860b42909e3c82a307623089:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="5bc77d88b91e4a60a54fce137c2b7bb3"><span data-offset-key="5bc77d88b91e4a60a54fce137c2b7bb3:0">Immediately skips the rest of the current loop BLOCK, allowing the loop to continue on to the next iteration. For this reason must </span><span data-offset-key="5bc77d88b91e4a60a54fce137c2b7bb3:1">_only_</span><span data-offset-key="5bc77d88b91e4a60a54fce137c2b7bb3:2"> be used within a loop BLOCK.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6fd7b742760046289910c4c5cecd4d67"><span data-offset-key="6fd7b742760046289910c4c5cecd4d67:0">A Middle English verb borrowed via the Old French </span><span data-offset-key="6fd7b742760046289910c4c5cecd4d67:1">**_continuer_**</span><span data-offset-key="6fd7b742760046289910c4c5cecd4d67:2"> from the Latin </span><span data-offset-key="6fd7b742760046289910c4c5cecd4d67:3">**_continuare_**</span><span data-offset-key="6fd7b742760046289910c4c5cecd4d67:4">. The general meaning used here is to “go forward or onward”, “carry on”, or “proceed”. In programming it means to cause a loop to start executing the next iteration, skipping any instructions that follow it.</span></span></span>
