<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8f3aef07d4d84ca2882324c2901d6d5b"><span data-offset-key="8f3aef07d4d84ca2882324c2901d6d5b:0">The </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#continue" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8bbfd27a7fe443af8218182cf8e28428"><span data-offset-key="8bbfd27a7fe443af8218182cf8e28428:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">continue</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3eee0e26715641738b6000eb53a62355"><span data-offset-key="3eee0e26715641738b6000eb53a62355:0"> statement always forms a line of its own, and it must be used in either a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d47f8516f444429da7cac4643871251b"><span data-offset-key="d47f8516f444429da7cac4643871251b:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0ee2c19c48ed4253abb24b0ae3795460"><span data-offset-key="0ee2c19c48ed4253abb24b0ae3795460:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#while" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="671c1aac3cfd4d32b6735167cde8fdb1"><span data-offset-key="671c1aac3cfd4d32b6735167cde8fdb1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">while</code></span></span></a><span data-key="281473e5eca34259b2005883217a7cf9"><span data-offset-key="281473e5eca34259b2005883217a7cf9:0"> loop. The most common use is to skip to the next iteration of a loop immediately when some particular condition is reached:</span></span></span>

    while True:    if EXPRESSION:        continue    STATEMENT

    for NAME in COLLECTION:    if EXPRESSION:        continue    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a5d5169dfa8343ccb84390d8237381e5"><span data-offset-key="a5d5169dfa8343ccb84390d8237381e5:0">This is particularly useful if there’s some situation that warrants skipping the current loop; for example if you only wanted to act on every second iteration.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="66c1d5633aa04cb98d98df6db2febc64"><span data-offset-key="66c1d5633aa04cb98d98df6db2febc64:0">Three for Importing Other Things</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7e4b64fe533e43659a407d2009def8cd"><span data-offset-key="7e4b64fe533e43659a407d2009def8cd:0">All of the above, plus the </span><span data-offset-key="7e4b64fe533e43659a407d2009def8cd:1">_builtin_</span><span data-offset-key="7e4b64fe533e43659a407d2009def8cd:2"> functions we’ll talk about in a later article, are sufficient to let you start using Python as a </span><span data-offset-key="7e4b64fe533e43659a407d2009def8cd:3">_scripting_</span><span data-offset-key="7e4b64fe533e43659a407d2009def8cd:4"> language, where you glue together things others have written with your own code to do some task you want to accomplish. But you need to be able to access those “things others have written” to do so. That’s what Python’s </span><span data-offset-key="7e4b64fe533e43659a407d2009def8cd:5">_import mechanism_</span><span data-offset-key="7e4b64fe533e43659a407d2009def8cd:6"> is for.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="bac3c2d305ee49aca33d92c0fae843ef"><span data-offset-key="bac3c2d305ee49aca33d92c0fae843ef:0">import</span></span></a><span data-key="a70f8b8c68a24bbf96ca1ba1687b4660"><span data-offset-key="a70f8b8c68a24bbf96ca1ba1687b4660:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-import-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ed00bfe9238c484ea93079637e3b5242"><span data-offset-key="ed00bfe9238c484ea93079637e3b5242:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="0db0b8038b46466db29744fe8efc8db0"><span data-offset-key="0db0b8038b46466db29744fe8efc8db0:0">Used to bring the functionality of an external MODULE into your own code.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49"><span data-offset-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49:0">A verb from the Middle English </span><span data-offset-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49:1">**_importen_**</span><span data-offset-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49:2">, via the Old French from the Latin </span><span data-offset-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49:3">**_importare_**</span><span data-offset-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49:4">. The general meaning is to “bring/carry \[goods into this country\] from abroad”. In computing it means to bring or </span><span data-offset-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49:5">**_import_**</span><span data-offset-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49:6"> some functionality </span><span data-offset-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49:7">_exported_</span><span data-offset-key="1454dcfe301b45f982d9e3d4606efa49:8"> by another program written in the same language into the current program.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="23aea6ea7ba044818d34ba978e3b6217"><span data-offset-key="23aea6ea7ba044818d34ba978e3b6217:0">The most common usage is very simple, the keyword is followed by the MODULE you want to access:</span></span></span>

    import MODULE

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d142635002004503a443f17a4d985718"><span data-offset-key="d142635002004503a443f17a4d985718:0">You can also import multiple MODULEs separated by commas:</span></span></span>

    import MODULE_A, MODULE_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="82170d6f18e14eaeb4007148e67f55e9"><span data-offset-key="82170d6f18e14eaeb4007148e67f55e9:0">And for organizational purposes you can put parentheses around them as well:</span></span></span>

    import (MODULE_A, MODULE_B)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fb6af582acb04cefac91d1280b830840"><span data-offset-key="fb6af582acb04cefac91d1280b830840:0">Any NAME inside the imported MODULE(s) can then be accessed within your own program using the </span><span data-offset-key="fb6af582acb04cefac91d1280b830840:1">_dot access_</span><span data-offset-key="fb6af582acb04cefac91d1280b830840:2"> pattern in the form MODULE.NAME. So, for instance, if you wanted to get the circumference of a circle:</span></span></span>

    import math​radius = 3circumference = math.tau * radius

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f992ea2f382f4ef48a77451c33024298"><span data-offset-key="f992ea2f382f4ef48a77451c33024298:0">Usually you’ll find all the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="adfe23d44b4345b0b8df7f032d848d0f"><span data-offset-key="adfe23d44b4345b0b8df7f032d848d0f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0b64e4fe94ef413498f9f0a592d879e1"><span data-offset-key="0b64e4fe94ef413498f9f0a592d879e1:0"> usage at the top of a MODULE, which makes it pretty easy to determine where such functionality comes from.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#from" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fdf4073da65449e188e9b39145568601"><span data-offset-key="fdf4073da65449e188e9b39145568601:0">from</span></span></a><span data-key="2ed23200d4e34f299e098119020a9046"><span data-offset-key="2ed23200d4e34f299e098119020a9046:0">Modifies </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6dc1b2b0ac6a40209a7923f36f800431"><span data-offset-key="6dc1b2b0ac6a40209a7923f36f800431:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="1052178e4cd14ddcaa37345cc42039fa"><span data-offset-key="1052178e4cd14ddcaa37345cc42039fa:0"> to allow you to import specific NAMEs from within an external MODULE.Can also be used with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#raise" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4166aa0b42664f15b184113bd7189492"><span data-offset-key="4166aa0b42664f15b184113bd7189492:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">raise</code></span></span></a><span data-key="f60fd8da10ee48d4a936fdb9df12d3c0"><span data-offset-key="f60fd8da10ee48d4a936fdb9df12d3c0:0"> and </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8ae0f6d4b5b441f2b93ed735f939b8c5"><span data-offset-key="8ae0f6d4b5b441f2b93ed735f939b8c5:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e476d0a674d5483687f78679b85b62b4"><span data-offset-key="e476d0a674d5483687f78679b85b62b4:0"> , see below.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a40934b8d8f04d95be20fafbf8e087f4"><span data-offset-key="a40934b8d8f04d95be20fafbf8e087f4:0">A Middle English word from the Old English </span><span data-offset-key="a40934b8d8f04d95be20fafbf8e087f4:1">**_fram_**</span><span data-offset-key="a40934b8d8f04d95be20fafbf8e087f4:2">, here we use the preposition form, with a general sense of “departure or movement away \[from something\]“; in computing we use a more specific sense of “taken </span><span data-offset-key="a40934b8d8f04d95be20fafbf8e087f4:3">**_from_**</span><span data-offset-key="a40934b8d8f04d95be20fafbf8e087f4:4"> a source”.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d31491f1e0eb4b6d9136f51ace6987d5"><span data-offset-key="d31491f1e0eb4b6d9136f51ace6987d5:0">It’s used to modify </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b9907517f5eb41a6a87217f27df0f6df"><span data-offset-key="b9907517f5eb41a6a87217f27df0f6df:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="278d469773414e728f626ca8e50c026a"><span data-offset-key="278d469773414e728f626ca8e50c026a:0"> to import a specific NAME from a MODULE, rather than the </span><span data-offset-key="278d469773414e728f626ca8e50c026a:1">_entire_</span><span data-offset-key="278d469773414e728f626ca8e50c026a:2"> MODULE:</span></span></span>

    from MODULE import NAME

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6875a03c4961421794fddd09104ff177"><span data-offset-key="6875a03c4961421794fddd09104ff177:0">If you wish to import more than one NAME they can be separated by commas:</span></span></span>

    from MODULE import NAME_A, NAME_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="671327f3e8da45248f2687f0a97848a7"><span data-offset-key="671327f3e8da45248f2687f0a97848a7:0">And for organizational purposes you can put parentheses around them as well:</span></span></span>

    from MODULE import (NAME_A, NAME_B)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="14249a0e0e544282b60131e885dd9a0a"><span data-offset-key="14249a0e0e544282b60131e885dd9a0a:0">In all cases you can then use the imported NAME directly, so for instance if you want the area of a circle:</span></span></span>

    from math import tau​radius = 3area = tau * radius ** 2 / 2

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d38d1699906b474489131d7d5c9eec12"><span data-offset-key="d38d1699906b474489131d7d5c9eec12:0">The main reason for </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#from" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="90133814329b407080e88509bade50e6"><span data-offset-key="90133814329b407080e88509bade50e6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">from</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2e870a95897b4ad9937804f526912f83"><span data-offset-key="2e870a95897b4ad9937804f526912f83:0"> is to remove the need to have many references to a MODULE peppered throughout your code, but it’s best reserved for when the MODULE has many NAMEs that it exports and you want to just use one or two.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#as" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b5dd8f9690cf43438c3506c9a546de6f"><span data-offset-key="b5dd8f9690cf43438c3506c9a546de6f:0">as</span></span></a><span data-key="4c37e6c8da09410aacc847467af0d445"><span data-offset-key="4c37e6c8da09410aacc847467af0d445:0">Modifies </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="98d7ab1b7dae402ea1052081c85e635d"><span data-offset-key="98d7ab1b7dae402ea1052081c85e635d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a98b201654a445eba03e35b8ad2fd26e"><span data-offset-key="a98b201654a445eba03e35b8ad2fd26e:0"> to create an alternative NAME (or alias) for an imported NAME.Can also be used with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="216e2506e4a24a079f1f58f30ceed597"><span data-offset-key="216e2506e4a24a079f1f58f30ceed597:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0b996868c5324e338dd1aa1322315454"><span data-offset-key="0b996868c5324e338dd1aa1322315454:0"> and </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#with" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b51a6779ff9e45a692343143c072896f"><span data-offset-key="b51a6779ff9e45a692343143c072896f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">with</code></span></span></a><span data-key="242e65bf54c24e97ad27a4112097f50b"><span data-offset-key="242e65bf54c24e97ad27a4112097f50b:0"> , see below.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a3f97bc80d0e4bd1b1b4b624838278fe"><span data-offset-key="a3f97bc80d0e4bd1b1b4b624838278fe:0">From the Old English </span><span data-offset-key="a3f97bc80d0e4bd1b1b4b624838278fe:1">**_eallswā_**</span><span data-offset-key="a3f97bc80d0e4bd1b1b4b624838278fe:2"> meaning “just so” or simply “all so”, which makes it a reduced form of </span><span data-offset-key="a3f97bc80d0e4bd1b1b4b624838278fe:3">**_also_**</span><span data-offset-key="a3f97bc80d0e4bd1b1b4b624838278fe:4">. The usage here comes from the adverb form meaning “\[to act\] in the manner or role \[of some other thing\]“. In Python it very specifically means “\[from here on refer to this thing\] </span><span data-offset-key="a3f97bc80d0e4bd1b1b4b624838278fe:5">**_as_**</span><span data-offset-key="a3f97bc80d0e4bd1b1b4b624838278fe:6"> \[this instead\]“.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0ca90c16b149494c8f208b1e525791ed"><span data-offset-key="0ca90c16b149494c8f208b1e525791ed:0">Because </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#from" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d399d5970e9b4c3e8f415ad8ad9ea10b"><span data-offset-key="d399d5970e9b4c3e8f415ad8ad9ea10b:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">from</code></span></span></a><span data-key="1d7c4c45ad574c63ac5b9cf30921a5b3"><span data-offset-key="1d7c4c45ad574c63ac5b9cf30921a5b3:0"> exists there are two forms of usage:</span></span></span>

    import MODULE as MODULE_ALIASfrom MODULE import NAME as NAME_ALIAS

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e383a9d483bf4bd0b3d5cf31b3737d60"><span data-offset-key="e383a9d483bf4bd0b3d5cf31b3737d60:0">The point of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#as" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="106ba40aa97d4fb496c8199ce678d64e"><span data-offset-key="106ba40aa97d4fb496c8199ce678d64e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">as</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3edb1bdcebfa409faef7b812c66e9f6c"><span data-offset-key="3edb1bdcebfa409faef7b812c66e9f6c:0"> is to allow you to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#import" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="bf4c643196404ba9ab2d2f3bbe28173f"><span data-offset-key="bf4c643196404ba9ab2d2f3bbe28173f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">import</code></span></span></a><span data-key="412d882ae1cf449b9b83a9ebc5f4d6a6"><span data-offset-key="412d882ae1cf449b9b83a9ebc5f4d6a6:0"> some MODULE or NAME but refer to it by some other name. This is useful if the original name is particularly long, would conflict with one already in use in your code, or could simply use some extra information in context.</span></span></span>

    from math import pi as half_as_good_as_tau

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fdce00aa21a54ae78d32cc99a3f28b91"><span data-offset-key="fdce00aa21a54ae78d32cc99a3f28b91:0">Five for Exceptional Situations</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="417f7e38271644c293041312414015f0"><span data-offset-key="417f7e38271644c293041312414015f0:0">Now that you’ve got the basics down, you’re getting into more complicated territory. What happens if you find yourself reaching a point in the code where you’re in an obvious error state and you don’t want to continue? This is where the notion of </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exception_handling" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9374d3c392a2461fa92ec0a0bbed5d39"><span data-offset-key="9374d3c392a2461fa92ec0a0bbed5d39:0">exception handling</span></span></a><span data-key="17bfd99987454779893297ddb270d442"><span data-offset-key="17bfd99987454779893297ddb270d442:0"> come into play. We’ll go into more detail on the standard Exceptions in later articles, but for now let’s just say that an EXCEPTION is a special type of VALUE that signifies a specific issue that has come up in your program. That issue </span><span data-offset-key="17bfd99987454779893297ddb270d442:1">_might_</span><span data-offset-key="17bfd99987454779893297ddb270d442:2"> be an </span><span data-offset-key="17bfd99987454779893297ddb270d442:3">_error_</span><span data-offset-key="17bfd99987454779893297ddb270d442:4">, in which case you might want to crash out of the program, or it might be a signal that something </span><span data-offset-key="17bfd99987454779893297ddb270d442:5">_unusual_</span><span data-offset-key="17bfd99987454779893297ddb270d442:6"> but expected has occurred. Either way you need to be able to emit those signals from your own code, as well as catch and react to such signals emitted by other code.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f0e0d76a35ab4accbc19287579f86dfe"><span data-offset-key="f0e0d76a35ab4accbc19287579f86dfe:0">**to signal that there’s a problem**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0dd0590a0bcc4cff8c196daebe96cf1b"><span data-offset-key="0dd0590a0bcc4cff8c196daebe96cf1b:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#raise" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5183334044904cf2915642c7e67f749e"><span data-offset-key="5183334044904cf2915642c7e67f749e:0">raise</span></span></a><span data-key="7a35546630e849bcad1eb3b4b197688f"><span data-offset-key="7a35546630e849bcad1eb3b4b197688f:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-raise-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="75ceb5242d5645909a9a740604915d6d"><span data-offset-key="75ceb5242d5645909a9a740604915d6d:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="7a3f04cc4a8c428d89fb716597f05f8c"><span data-offset-key="7a3f04cc4a8c428d89fb716597f05f8c:0">Used to raise a specified EXCEPTION, which will cause the program to stop immediately and exit if not handled by an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ef7230d3d8bd41f990e79fff481bd9e9"><span data-offset-key="ef7230d3d8bd41f990e79fff481bd9e9:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4a93500b777e42c691f903d58f240add"><span data-offset-key="4a93500b777e42c691f903d58f240add:0"> BLOCK.If used without an argument inside an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="7650bf5db5294fd7a093bb06db8770b1"><span data-offset-key="7650bf5db5294fd7a093bb06db8770b1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c5db1cafa9fb434d896e57c15d260396"><span data-offset-key="c5db1cafa9fb434d896e57c15d260396:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#finally" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8273feed28804a31b7f85c8a16a97bef"><span data-offset-key="8273feed28804a31b7f85c8a16a97bef:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">finally</code></span></span></a><span data-key="71b6b27867534e3b93e25fc56bf83068"><span data-offset-key="71b6b27867534e3b93e25fc56bf83068:0"> BLOCK, re-raises the EXCEPTION being handled by the BLOCK.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bfc45ecdf56a462fb77b22c4d7b1db01"><span data-offset-key="bfc45ecdf56a462fb77b22c4d7b1db01:0">A Middle English word with </span><span data-offset-key="bfc45ecdf56a462fb77b22c4d7b1db01:1">_many_</span><span data-offset-key="bfc45ecdf56a462fb77b22c4d7b1db01:2"> meanings, but in this case it comes from the verb form meaning “to lift upright, build, or construct” or “to make higher”. The meaning in computing is more specifically from a newer sense of “to mention \[a question, issue, or argument\] for discussion”, as in “to </span><span data-offset-key="bfc45ecdf56a462fb77b22c4d7b1db01:3">**_raise_**</span><span data-offset-key="bfc45ecdf56a462fb77b22c4d7b1db01:4"> attention \[to an issue\]“. In several other programming languages </span><span data-offset-key="bfc45ecdf56a462fb77b22c4d7b1db01:5">**_throw_**</span><span data-offset-key="bfc45ecdf56a462fb77b22c4d7b1db01:6"> is used with similar meaning.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7057598ef2fa4393bcf0193a96d6da01"><span data-offset-key="7057598ef2fa4393bcf0193a96d6da01:0">The usage is </span><span data-offset-key="7057598ef2fa4393bcf0193a96d6da01:1">_usually_</span><span data-offset-key="7057598ef2fa4393bcf0193a96d6da01:2"> going to be:</span></span></span>

    raise EXCEPTION

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f276aee332dd4566a8f22ffca79c0e7f"><span data-offset-key="f276aee332dd4566a8f22ffca79c0e7f:0">Quite rarely you might see the </span><span data-offset-key="f276aee332dd4566a8f22ffca79c0e7f:1">_chained_</span><span data-offset-key="f276aee332dd4566a8f22ffca79c0e7f:2"> form:</span></span></span>

    raise EXCEPTION from OTHER_EXCEPTION

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c9f380ca0d99404db2c3fdd10daf9ebd"><span data-offset-key="c9f380ca0d99404db2c3fdd10daf9ebd:0">Which is used to indicate that the EXCEPTION being raised was </span><span data-offset-key="c9f380ca0d99404db2c3fdd10daf9ebd:1">_caused by_</span><span data-offset-key="c9f380ca0d99404db2c3fdd10daf9ebd:2"> (or </span><span data-offset-key="c9f380ca0d99404db2c3fdd10daf9ebd:3">_came from_</span><span data-offset-key="c9f380ca0d99404db2c3fdd10daf9ebd:4">) some other EXCEPTION. This isn’t used often, but sometimes is useful when you attempt to handle an exception raised by other code but somehow cannot do so.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="036fbbf7d0154e829313f7206f20d5a9"><span data-offset-key="036fbbf7d0154e829313f7206f20d5a9:0">Lastly </span><span data-offset-key="036fbbf7d0154e829313f7206f20d5a9:1">_inside_</span><span data-offset-key="036fbbf7d0154e829313f7206f20d5a9:2"> an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="bad4c1a066cc43949bf4c6161c4ada0d"><span data-offset-key="bad4c1a066cc43949bf4c6161c4ada0d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="07e10e5f3de94b8d8f25419b6387ed81"><span data-offset-key="07e10e5f3de94b8d8f25419b6387ed81:0"> BLOCK you can simply:</span></span></span>

    raise

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="362d00bcfd4c4a92b44ea86fee96e7bb"><span data-offset-key="362d00bcfd4c4a92b44ea86fee96e7bb:0">Which will re-raise whatever EXCEPTION is currently being handled inside that BLOCK.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f313cc781f7b4d26afa6bf7acf51383e"><span data-offset-key="f313cc781f7b4d26afa6bf7acf51383e:0">**to signal that a particular condition is not met**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="441e37010ff8489c882f4d938fc34757"><span data-offset-key="441e37010ff8489c882f4d938fc34757:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#assert" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="455da04f7eea411396c9ea6086835d08"><span data-offset-key="455da04f7eea411396c9ea6086835d08:0">assert</span></span></a><span data-key="f6ef6d8405374cb1b09257dfbf978ab9"><span data-offset-key="f6ef6d8405374cb1b09257dfbf978ab9:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-assert-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e33ff4d4c3da449395c417f65eb2bf33"><span data-offset-key="e33ff4d4c3da449395c417f65eb2bf33:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="2ffcb18ee631496691d7186b987bf17b"><span data-offset-key="2ffcb18ee631496691d7186b987bf17b:0">Used to test if some EXPRESSION is considered True, and if not raise an AssertionError.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="764e5b77499e461380803d2ce5278b9c"><span data-offset-key="764e5b77499e461380803d2ce5278b9c:0">From the Latin </span><span data-offset-key="764e5b77499e461380803d2ce5278b9c:1">**_assertus_**</span><span data-offset-key="764e5b77499e461380803d2ce5278b9c:2">, with the general sense of “declared, protected, or claimed”. In programming it specifically means to specify that a condition must be met at a particular point in the code, and to error if it is not.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4425d03252bc400d98ea96bf5fe03640"><span data-offset-key="4425d03252bc400d98ea96bf5fe03640:0">The usage of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#assert" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5a6804ef06e74313891033841d365029"><span data-offset-key="5a6804ef06e74313891033841d365029:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">assert</code></span></span></a><span data-key="81151e0cc12f4beeb3c658f5cef18d3a"><span data-offset-key="81151e0cc12f4beeb3c658f5cef18d3a:0"> is usually going to be in the form:</span></span></span>

    assert EXPRESSION

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="540e82b6c7524907bcfc3df468a0f0c7"><span data-offset-key="540e82b6c7524907bcfc3df468a0f0c7:0">Which will simply </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#raise" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e92bab419cbc485abd73ee5b299a4452"><span data-offset-key="e92bab419cbc485abd73ee5b299a4452:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">raise</code></span></span></a><span data-key="447c01b1a7bb4cf6b4ad50494152c9b6"><span data-offset-key="447c01b1a7bb4cf6b4ad50494152c9b6:0"> an AssertionError if EXPRESSION does not evaluate as </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="bd5e63f6e66e43e49ea96b5f7f116727"><span data-offset-key="bd5e63f6e66e43e49ea96b5f7f116727:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c3767f5e1c1d4661896d6e70a22216d6"><span data-offset-key="c3767f5e1c1d4661896d6e70a22216d6:0"> .</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0aad076e4ec24b4c9c7604f55a25ab66"><span data-offset-key="0aad076e4ec24b4c9c7604f55a25ab66:0">An alternative form allows you to specify a message:</span></span></span>

    assert EXPRESSION, "something is wrong!"

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="06ec23c4330944d9b23c5418c3ce6d6b"><span data-offset-key="06ec23c4330944d9b23c5418c3ce6d6b:0">And this message will be incorporated into the AssertionError.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="156630370dd34a21b5775b941ac5984f"><span data-offset-key="156630370dd34a21b5775b941ac5984f:0">The </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#assert" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="68a003304996474eb3fc97bcac3f4bb5"><span data-offset-key="68a003304996474eb3fc97bcac3f4bb5:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">assert</code></span></span></a><span data-key="29756a4b46a84c9598a95671070855a4"><span data-offset-key="29756a4b46a84c9598a95671070855a4:0"> statement exists for you to test the things that </span><span data-offset-key="29756a4b46a84c9598a95671070855a4:1">_must_</span><span data-offset-key="29756a4b46a84c9598a95671070855a4:2"> be </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#true" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="349f83c27b3b41b5aeba6b780cfd832e"><span data-offset-key="349f83c27b3b41b5aeba6b780cfd832e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">True</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ce06adfd62644d9e8e996988bda4b5f7"><span data-offset-key="ce06adfd62644d9e8e996988bda4b5f7:0"> for your program to continue to work (we call these your </span><span data-offset-key="ce06adfd62644d9e8e996988bda4b5f7:1">_invariants_</span><span data-offset-key="ce06adfd62644d9e8e996988bda4b5f7:2">). This can be very helpful when developing and debugging, but should not be relied on, </span><span data-offset-key="ce06adfd62644d9e8e996988bda4b5f7:3">_at all_</span><span data-offset-key="ce06adfd62644d9e8e996988bda4b5f7:4">, in production code, as the person running your program can elect to disable all </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#assert" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="84d7506de5cf4d29b07e09688670c167"><span data-offset-key="84d7506de5cf4d29b07e09688670c167:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">assert</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c314af56cb284247924f8a860c381cd9"><span data-offset-key="c314af56cb284247924f8a860c381cd9:0"> statements by passing the </span><span data-offset-key="c314af56cb284247924f8a860c381cd9:1">`-O`</span><span data-offset-key="c314af56cb284247924f8a860c381cd9:2"> command line option to Python. Basically you can imagine that </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#assert" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="39aa8f980c0147dc8a00f1f47a9f8e49"><span data-offset-key="39aa8f980c0147dc8a00f1f47a9f8e49:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">assert</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3dd5684783d24029a995e97e24cd1c23"><span data-offset-key="3dd5684783d24029a995e97e24cd1c23:0"> works like:</span></span></span>

    if [the -O command line flag was not passed]:    if not EXPRESSION:        raise AssertionError

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="387e25efc77c4143b303633a87adea7f"><span data-offset-key="387e25efc77c4143b303633a87adea7f:0">… except that if the </span><span data-offset-key="387e25efc77c4143b303633a87adea7f:1">`-O`</span><span data-offset-key="387e25efc77c4143b303633a87adea7f:2"> flag was passed the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#assert" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="22c659b40917469e802738a1c633cfc6"><span data-offset-key="22c659b40917469e802738a1c633cfc6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">assert</code></span></span></a><span data-key="6cc2d0567e4141b69cb8fed54d627741"><span data-offset-key="6cc2d0567e4141b69cb8fed54d627741:0"> statement will simply be replaced by </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#pass" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1a4505cd4922490388b0a49a590f6a44"><span data-offset-key="1a4505cd4922490388b0a49a590f6a44:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">pass</code></span></span></a><span data-key="6ecaf2ec15e64107bf8e5414f1124f99"><span data-offset-key="6ecaf2ec15e64107bf8e5414f1124f99:0"> and nothing whatsoever will happen.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e97065fa1f3c4b83bffcf1f3e851e994"><span data-offset-key="e97065fa1f3c4b83bffcf1f3e851e994:0">**to catch a signal and react to it**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1a52f5fbed754984a23e3000a319872f"><span data-offset-key="1a52f5fbed754984a23e3000a319872f:0">With both </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#raise" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0f239301700a4b1ebb023d1b137793b1"><span data-offset-key="0f239301700a4b1ebb023d1b137793b1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">raise</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a065a6a8f36c4005b7a13cc6d44aeee3"><span data-offset-key="a065a6a8f36c4005b7a13cc6d44aeee3:0"> and </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#assert" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0f9a9f41e0584cd5aeba300cd9a53312"><span data-offset-key="0f9a9f41e0584cd5aeba300cd9a53312:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">assert</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0d7ac2aa979f4426bf2708f1c5eb92da"><span data-offset-key="0d7ac2aa979f4426bf2708f1c5eb92da:0"> in your toolkit you know how to signal an EXCEPTION, but how do you catch and react to (or ignore) one? This is where </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/tutorial/errors.html#handling-exceptions" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6e19bc98ddb049bfa4fd4329257efdb7"><span data-offset-key="6e19bc98ddb049bfa4fd4329257efdb7:0">Python’s exception handling</span></span></a><span data-key="d546f5e9f17b4feea50e9658e7dd4130"><span data-offset-key="d546f5e9f17b4feea50e9658e7dd4130:0"> mechanism comes into play.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#try" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ee9615a866374c149d68d86c9427ac8c"><span data-offset-key="ee9615a866374c149d68d86c9427ac8c:0">try</span></span></a><span data-key="20f712ba004e4e88b1e6a241cb06e5d0"><span data-offset-key="20f712ba004e4e88b1e6a241cb06e5d0:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#the-try-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5bfac8dc99ea4a188dce623f7f85a7a6"><span data-offset-key="5bfac8dc99ea4a188dce623f7f85a7a6:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="eae5281a29894c59a6f086efdf36c872"><span data-offset-key="eae5281a29894c59a6f086efdf36c872:0">Starts an exception handler BLOCK; </span><span data-offset-key="eae5281a29894c59a6f086efdf36c872:1">_must_</span><span data-offset-key="eae5281a29894c59a6f086efdf36c872:2"> be followed either an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c165a77d07bc458d92b4f5eb00faf8af"><span data-offset-key="c165a77d07bc458d92b4f5eb00faf8af:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b1cf288adb3149718b7ab1a4702c80df"><span data-offset-key="b1cf288adb3149718b7ab1a4702c80df:0"> BLOCK, an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#else" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d5d3d7e8b5d341fd92bed953f4bdc811"><span data-offset-key="d5d3d7e8b5d341fd92bed953f4bdc811:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">else</code></span></span></a><span data-key="33910b0706554631a53432c16e883be6"><span data-offset-key="33910b0706554631a53432c16e883be6:0"> block or a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#finally" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="25106456241144199588592206ab3eff"><span data-offset-key="25106456241144199588592206ab3eff:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">finally</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c09ba3f3be4a44f18db2d84999a6ca12"><span data-offset-key="c09ba3f3be4a44f18db2d84999a6ca12:0"> BLOCK in order to be valid syntax.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="50f613b7473a4da0ab06146d1b675d91"><span data-offset-key="50f613b7473a4da0ab06146d1b675d91:0">A verb borrowed from the Old French word </span><span data-offset-key="50f613b7473a4da0ab06146d1b675d91:1">**_trier_**</span><span data-offset-key="50f613b7473a4da0ab06146d1b675d91:2">, meaning to “test”, “experiment”, or “attempt to do”. The meaning in Python is essentially the same, “\[start a\] test \[of something that </span><span data-offset-key="50f613b7473a4da0ab06146d1b675d91:3">_may_</span><span data-offset-key="50f613b7473a4da0ab06146d1b675d91:4"> error\]“.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="eff758cc237b4e3fb91a967282a22631"><span data-offset-key="eff758cc237b4e3fb91a967282a22631:0">except</span></span></a><span data-key="e00fcb071a2c42e59e456e9cd8910900"><span data-offset-key="e00fcb071a2c42e59e456e9cd8910900:0">Optionally </span><span data-offset-key="e00fcb071a2c42e59e456e9cd8910900:1">_continues_</span><span data-offset-key="e00fcb071a2c42e59e456e9cd8910900:2"> an exception handler BLOCK by catching EXCEPTIONs; can (and </span><span data-offset-key="e00fcb071a2c42e59e456e9cd8910900:3">_should_</span><span data-offset-key="e00fcb071a2c42e59e456e9cd8910900:4">) be limited to specific types of EXCEPTION. More than one of these can follow a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#try" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="7f9a9ab2bc1e4ef581026c4c2bb88a97"><span data-offset-key="7f9a9ab2bc1e4ef581026c4c2bb88a97:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">try</code></span></span></a><span data-key="370cc2c6a89c4672979f85deb158322a"><span data-offset-key="370cc2c6a89c4672979f85deb158322a:0"> and each will be checked in turn until either the EXCEPTION is handled or no more </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9e6b06c32b6a4cb895407bdfc6fcf332"><span data-offset-key="9e6b06c32b6a4cb895407bdfc6fcf332:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0c971ace3fee48b1acb4784719ff3f30"><span data-offset-key="0c971ace3fee48b1acb4784719ff3f30:0"> statements remain.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87"><span data-offset-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87:0">A verb borrowed from the Middle French </span><span data-offset-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87:1">**_excepter_**</span><span data-offset-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87:2"> and Latin </span><span data-offset-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87:3">**_exceptus_**</span><span data-offset-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87:4">; the original meaning is “to receive”, but the more general uses it to “exclude \[something\]” or “object to \[something\]“, as in “every fruit except apples”. The meaning in Python is a little vague, but can be thought of as “catch, capture, or trap \[an exception\]“. In fact in many other languages </span><span data-offset-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87:5">**_catch_**</span><span data-offset-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87:6"> is used for the same purpose; Python’s </span><span data-offset-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87:7">**_except_**</span><span data-offset-key="ee6f989e716948ef948d1b1fcd1aab87:8"> is the exception to that rule.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#finally" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="7db10ba6844f4572a0f736c2999e4865"><span data-offset-key="7db10ba6844f4572a0f736c2999e4865:0">finally</span></span></a><span data-key="ae756ce2041443e493484de33ae1c20c"><span data-offset-key="ae756ce2041443e493484de33ae1c20c:0">Optionally </span><span data-offset-key="ae756ce2041443e493484de33ae1c20c:1">_cleans up_</span><span data-offset-key="ae756ce2041443e493484de33ae1c20c:2"> an exception handler BLOCK to provide a means of </span><span data-offset-key="ae756ce2041443e493484de33ae1c20c:3">_always_</span><span data-offset-key="ae756ce2041443e493484de33ae1c20c:4"> performing some action whether or not the EXCEPTION was handled. </span><span data-offset-key="ae756ce2041443e493484de33ae1c20c:5">_Must_</span><span data-offset-key="ae756ce2041443e493484de33ae1c20c:6"> follow any </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3044c2e0e67f49ffa9f7076296252ea0"><span data-offset-key="3044c2e0e67f49ffa9f7076296252ea0:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ba1e687a3a6547eaa4845e05527276b1"><span data-offset-key="ba1e687a3a6547eaa4845e05527276b1:0"> BLOCKS that are present, as well as the optional </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#else" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e50762ffba934261953cb19544718ab7"><span data-offset-key="e50762ffba934261953cb19544718ab7:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">else</code></span></span></a><span data-key="265beeece34748b6879d52270bc18a7d"><span data-offset-key="265beeece34748b6879d52270bc18a7d:0"> BLOCK if that is also present. If no </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="583a2cf9f0ff433ab46c4a3d3e8f5fe9"><span data-offset-key="583a2cf9f0ff433ab46c4a3d3e8f5fe9:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="12cb0341c0034bf091ab48422907b3e9"><span data-offset-key="12cb0341c0034bf091ab48422907b3e9:0"> BLOCK is present then </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#finally" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3a92a94df13a4afeb0843e20bc9c1dcb"><span data-offset-key="3a92a94df13a4afeb0843e20bc9c1dcb:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">finally</code></span></span></a><span data-key="9e3805fbd9ea4734936535580f6e9d15"><span data-offset-key="9e3805fbd9ea4734936535580f6e9d15:0"> </span><span data-offset-key="9e3805fbd9ea4734936535580f6e9d15:1">_must_</span><span data-offset-key="9e3805fbd9ea4734936535580f6e9d15:2"> terminate the exception handler.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7fac0641a52d468aa627a3fca633f06f"><span data-offset-key="7fac0641a52d468aa627a3fca633f06f:0">From the Middle English </span><span data-offset-key="7fac0641a52d468aa627a3fca633f06f:1">**_fynaly_**</span><span data-offset-key="7fac0641a52d468aa627a3fca633f06f:2"> meaning “at the end or conclusion” or just “lastly”. It implies the very last thing to do in a sequence, which is the meaning here as well.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5037db962e354103a2901a4acb9acbc6"><span data-offset-key="5037db962e354103a2901a4acb9acbc6:0">Exception handling is the first circumstance you’ve encountered in which one BLOCK </span><span data-offset-key="5037db962e354103a2901a4acb9acbc6:1">_must_</span><span data-offset-key="5037db962e354103a2901a4acb9acbc6:2"> be followed by another, and the rules are somewhat more complicated than anything you’ve yet seen. For instance there are </span><span data-offset-key="5037db962e354103a2901a4acb9acbc6:3">_two_</span><span data-offset-key="5037db962e354103a2901a4acb9acbc6:4"> different </span><span data-offset-key="5037db962e354103a2901a4acb9acbc6:5">_minimal syntactically valid_</span><span data-offset-key="5037db962e354103a2901a4acb9acbc6:6"> forms of exception handler:</span></span></span>

    try:    BLOCKfinally:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7efd585ee98945959c01f67f72be4881"><span data-offset-key="7efd585ee98945959c01f67f72be4881:0">This form does not actually handle any EXCEPTION raised within BLOCK, it merely ensures that STATEMENT is run in all circumstances. Any EXCEPTION not handled will continue to “raise up” until it is either handled or crashes your program. This is useful for situations in which you want to do the same action (such as closing a file or database connection) whether or not there has been an error.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ed2240d955f14402a9fd1fa827cb3dd7"><span data-offset-key="ed2240d955f14402a9fd1fa827cb3dd7:0">The second form </span><span data-offset-key="ed2240d955f14402a9fd1fa827cb3dd7:1">_does_</span><span data-offset-key="ed2240d955f14402a9fd1fa827cb3dd7:2"> handle an EXCEPTION:</span></span></span>

    try:    BLOCKexcept:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="683a3ab5fd6e4de18a5a0d30542d5be1"><span data-offset-key="683a3ab5fd6e4de18a5a0d30542d5be1:0">**Note**</span><span data-offset-key="683a3ab5fd6e4de18a5a0d30542d5be1:1">: because this form will catch </span><span data-offset-key="683a3ab5fd6e4de18a5a0d30542d5be1:2">_any_</span><span data-offset-key="683a3ab5fd6e4de18a5a0d30542d5be1:3"> EXCEPTION, including several that are used by Python to perform critical operations, you should, practically speaking, </span><span data-offset-key="683a3ab5fd6e4de18a5a0d30542d5be1:4">**never**</span><span data-offset-key="683a3ab5fd6e4de18a5a0d30542d5be1:5"> use the above form. Instead use the </span><span data-offset-key="683a3ab5fd6e4de18a5a0d30542d5be1:6">_minimum safe_</span><span data-offset-key="683a3ab5fd6e4de18a5a0d30542d5be1:7"> form:</span></span></span>

    try:    BLOCKexcept EXCEPTION:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cd0188fe686941569b68c95357c01cd2"><span data-offset-key="cd0188fe686941569b68c95357c01cd2:0">This ensures that the exception handler </span><span data-offset-key="cd0188fe686941569b68c95357c01cd2:1">_only_</span><span data-offset-key="cd0188fe686941569b68c95357c01cd2:2"> handles the EXCEPTION </span><span data-offset-key="cd0188fe686941569b68c95357c01cd2:3">_type_</span><span data-offset-key="cd0188fe686941569b68c95357c01cd2:4"> specified. The </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/exceptions.html#exception-hierarchy" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="09ac6e4ff7aa44f6b2a707f3afb5e35a"><span data-offset-key="09ac6e4ff7aa44f6b2a707f3afb5e35a:0">hierarchy of built-in exceptions</span></span></a><span data-key="7d43368cdfeb4c2abce162118a6ec41c"><span data-offset-key="7d43368cdfeb4c2abce162118a6ec41c:0"> in Python is complex and touches on concepts we can’t cover in this article, but for now just know that </span><span data-offset-key="7d43368cdfeb4c2abce162118a6ec41c:1">`except Exception`</span><span data-offset-key="7d43368cdfeb4c2abce162118a6ec41c:2"> is the </span><span data-offset-key="7d43368cdfeb4c2abce162118a6ec41c:3">_least_</span><span data-offset-key="7d43368cdfeb4c2abce162118a6ec41c:4"> specific </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a9f9a7af29a64e6f92544848d7877a91"><span data-offset-key="a9f9a7af29a64e6f92544848d7877a91:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a2bc745ba94541358ced7fa07f1589bc"><span data-offset-key="a2bc745ba94541358ced7fa07f1589bc:0"> statement you should ever use in production code.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e23460beab4d44a590059b7290019f31"><span data-offset-key="e23460beab4d44a590059b7290019f31:0">That minimum safe form, however, isn’t particularly useful, because the STATEMENT can’t actually know what EXCEPTION it’s handling. Most of the time you’ll see something like this:</span></span></span>

    except EXCEPTION as NAME:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fe5082c3019545548152d37b3b53666f"><span data-offset-key="fe5082c3019545548152d37b3b53666f:0">Which uses </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#as" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fc6228c4dc85495d9be3c117e768b70f"><span data-offset-key="fc6228c4dc85495d9be3c117e768b70f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">as</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a210302c940e403ba7467e3965444ae1"><span data-offset-key="a210302c940e403ba7467e3965444ae1:0"> to provide an alias NAME that can be used to inspect the actual EXCEPTION that was raised. This can be very helpful for seeing precisely what went wrong, which will help you decide if you can ignore the problem or need to respond in some way.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2c7bc566ccb444ea9ebadf75e7f4e3e9"><span data-offset-key="2c7bc566ccb444ea9ebadf75e7f4e3e9:0">You can also specify multiple different types of EXCEPTION to catch, which can be helpful if you want to respond to any of those forms in the </span><span data-offset-key="2c7bc566ccb444ea9ebadf75e7f4e3e9:1">_same_</span><span data-offset-key="2c7bc566ccb444ea9ebadf75e7f4e3e9:2"> way:</span></span></span>

    except (EXCEPTION_A, EXCEPTION_B, EXCEPTION_C) as NAME:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="469296f115d247e2ab99a93350728527"><span data-offset-key="469296f115d247e2ab99a93350728527:0">And if you want to respond to them each in a </span><span data-offset-key="469296f115d247e2ab99a93350728527:1">_different_</span><span data-offset-key="469296f115d247e2ab99a93350728527:2"> way you can just stack </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="78aa43be98834f949bedbe76d6ef97a2"><span data-offset-key="78aa43be98834f949bedbe76d6ef97a2:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="35eda1cb440b47dea07a17862e7900cf"><span data-offset-key="35eda1cb440b47dea07a17862e7900cf:0"> BLOCKS:</span></span></span>

    except EXCEPTION_A as NAME:    STATEMENT_Aexcept EXCEPTION_B as NAME:    STATEMENT_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d9d7c5977add4b68aead9995c5c96aba"><span data-offset-key="d9d7c5977add4b68aead9995c5c96aba:0">You can also optionally use </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#else" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="59f4bf0a1ce84141baccfa96d8e67992"><span data-offset-key="59f4bf0a1ce84141baccfa96d8e67992:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">else</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5b03f2def7174cf792a8d0d12e7ae385"><span data-offset-key="5b03f2def7174cf792a8d0d12e7ae385:0"> with an exception handler, so long as at least one </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#except" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="751ab513d9484cb9b82c7573ed49793f"><span data-offset-key="751ab513d9484cb9b82c7573ed49793f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">except</code></span></span></a><span data-key="62614823c5654f8c922e558f2428f0b3"><span data-offset-key="62614823c5654f8c922e558f2428f0b3:0"> statement is used, and as long as the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#else" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4d0660af46584652a364ee4ddb8d3876"><span data-offset-key="4d0660af46584652a364ee4ddb8d3876:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">else</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2070c090e815438a9c0c019579fd423c"><span data-offset-key="2070c090e815438a9c0c019579fd423c:0"> is positioned </span><span data-offset-key="2070c090e815438a9c0c019579fd423c:1">_before_</span><span data-offset-key="2070c090e815438a9c0c019579fd423c:2"> any </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#finally" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="38edfdff672d418f8fdb87c3ca0b6472"><span data-offset-key="38edfdff672d418f8fdb87c3ca0b6472:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">finally</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ac2111ca8a6340d2896e4dfdf24839d6"><span data-offset-key="ac2111ca8a6340d2896e4dfdf24839d6:0"> :</span></span></span>

    try:    BLOCK_Aexcept EXCEPTION as NAME:    BLOCK_Belse:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d0c078e5aeea4d698267490e042ce804"><span data-offset-key="d0c078e5aeea4d698267490e042ce804:0">However this is relatively rare, because the STATEMENT indented under </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#else" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="740efa96091649b28777c382843734cb"><span data-offset-key="740efa96091649b28777c382843734cb:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">else</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5eff077b93d04d288d043caefbdff896"><span data-offset-key="5eff077b93d04d288d043caefbdff896:0"> will </span><span data-offset-key="5eff077b93d04d288d043caefbdff896:1">_only_</span><span data-offset-key="5eff077b93d04d288d043caefbdff896:2"> be executed when no EXCEPTION was raised inside the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#try" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3304af613e9d4fc19c366ab18bca1f79"><span data-offset-key="3304af613e9d4fc19c366ab18bca1f79:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">try</code></span></span></a><span data-key="dc4f3a49a5d9447d862409ff8b6e94a6"><span data-offset-key="dc4f3a49a5d9447d862409ff8b6e94a6:0"> BLOCK </span><span data-offset-key="dc4f3a49a5d9447d862409ff8b6e94a6:1">_and_</span><span data-offset-key="dc4f3a49a5d9447d862409ff8b6e94a6:2"> no </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#break" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="403a1d23483e45739dac60497051d54e"><span data-offset-key="403a1d23483e45739dac60497051d54e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">break</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c8513b716aad42c5b8bbefbfd7775418"><span data-offset-key="c8513b716aad42c5b8bbefbfd7775418:0"> , </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#continue" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="bdb89e2e1d594b3ca1b81bedc1ee0322"><span data-offset-key="bdb89e2e1d594b3ca1b81bedc1ee0322:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">continue</code></span></span></a><span data-key="41f5a4987bc44e8a8fbc475a83cdf2ee"><span data-offset-key="41f5a4987bc44e8a8fbc475a83cdf2ee:0"> , or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8eb8409407c04a7e86cc51100ecb9ef8"><span data-offset-key="8eb8409407c04a7e86cc51100ecb9ef8:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ea5af7107368415187d31e11e5ec39df"><span data-offset-key="ea5af7107368415187d31e11e5ec39df:0"> statements were encountered within it.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="52b769b65f9d432895fe090b3d0cc98d"><span data-offset-key="52b769b65f9d432895fe090b3d0cc98d:0">As you’ve seen exception handling has some fairly dense syntax compared to the rest of Python. A fully fleshed out exception handler in a program that does something fairly complex, like interacting with a database, might involve all these parts.</span></span></span>

    try:    [connect to database]    [query the database]except ConnectionError as error:    [log the error]else:    [log success]finally:    [close the connection]

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4266b7f992dc4514b50100712c5d9da5"><span data-offset-key="4266b7f992dc4514b50100712c5d9da5:0">But, thankfully, it’s often not that complex, and you usually only have to deal with exception handling when something truly exceptional has happened.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2207a104eb9c4ddda9bdca87419cb778"><span data-offset-key="2207a104eb9c4ddda9bdca87419cb778:0">Four for Writing Functions</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="eea9b2cb7eb04b64b901650535e6bead"><span data-offset-key="eea9b2cb7eb04b64b901650535e6bead:0">Now that you’ve got all the structures you need to write an arbitrarily complex program, with the ability to make decisions, loop, and handle errors, your biggest problem is going to be organizing those structures into re-usable units. For instance you don’t want to type out a complex exception handler for every single time you connect to and query a database, as that would quickly lead to an unmanageable amount of repetition.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e9d9053c9c6340fea5c31fa5f492a05d"><span data-offset-key="e9d9053c9c6340fea5c31fa5f492a05d:0">One of the key mantras of programming is </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don%27t_repeat_yourself" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="91a8553ff5f946159a106eea71694d64"><span data-offset-key="91a8553ff5f946159a106eea71694d64:0">Don’t Repeat Yourself</span></span></a><span data-key="c351a3a7a04041a4b3c74cd7b7d15bf8"><span data-offset-key="c351a3a7a04041a4b3c74cd7b7d15bf8:0"> (aka </span><span data-offset-key="c351a3a7a04041a4b3c74cd7b7d15bf8:1">**DRY**</span><span data-offset-key="c351a3a7a04041a4b3c74cd7b7d15bf8:2">); the less boilerplate, the better, and so you want to be able to create </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subroutine" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f3dd76e6824e405fa3cfffa9921fc9a6"><span data-offset-key="f3dd76e6824e405fa3cfffa9921fc9a6:0">subroutines</span></span></a><span data-key="fa9b0442172049ebb4521f03c497358d"><span data-offset-key="fa9b0442172049ebb4521f03c497358d:0">, which are the most basic form of </span><span data-offset-key="fa9b0442172049ebb4521f03c497358d:1">_code re-use_</span><span data-offset-key="fa9b0442172049ebb4521f03c497358d:2">. In Python the most common form of subroutine is the </span><span data-offset-key="fa9b0442172049ebb4521f03c497358d:3">_function_</span><span data-offset-key="fa9b0442172049ebb4521f03c497358d:4">, which comes in two primary forms.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="167f0de91e694766873b465ec48883da"><span data-offset-key="167f0de91e694766873b465ec48883da:0">**anonymous (unnamed) functions**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2f3ef8ea7d1d4dd8a42f4e690a96ccc6"><span data-offset-key="2f3ef8ea7d1d4dd8a42f4e690a96ccc6:0">A lot of people teaching (and learning) Python tend to skip over anonymous functions, or treat them as an advanced feature, but that’s really just because they’re poorly named. The “anonymous” part just means the function isn’t given a specific name at creation time. That might not sound like the easiest thing to re-use – and you’re right – but it’s useful to understand them before we head on to </span><span data-offset-key="2f3ef8ea7d1d4dd8a42f4e690a96ccc6:1">_named_</span><span data-offset-key="2f3ef8ea7d1d4dd8a42f4e690a96ccc6:2"> functions because they’re fundamentally simpler and more constrained.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1d51b2d5192e41098c6618812a804e3f"><span data-offset-key="1d51b2d5192e41098c6618812a804e3f:0">Unfortunately the powers that be decided that anonymous functions, already saddled with a bad and confusing name, should </span><span data-offset-key="1d51b2d5192e41098c6618812a804e3f:1">_definitely_</span><span data-offset-key="1d51b2d5192e41098c6618812a804e3f:2"> get a worse name in Python.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e5b9227accb845ba8782b5c59d2c0052"><span data-offset-key="e5b9227accb845ba8782b5c59d2c0052:0">lambda</span></span></a><span data-key="8f9b83dd43a2440eb19b791b78e6bef5"><span data-offset-key="8f9b83dd43a2440eb19b791b78e6bef5:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/expressions.html#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c6e1c70f86174fe6bef3af4b2e0a0731"><span data-offset-key="c6e1c70f86174fe6bef3af4b2e0a0731:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="f8e5585051ac48e992544686b5e5fd8a"><span data-offset-key="f8e5585051ac48e992544686b5e5fd8a:0">Used to define a CALLABLE </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anonymous_function" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cdbab1107fa34088a6dd31c901beabb1"><span data-offset-key="cdbab1107fa34088a6dd31c901beabb1:0">anonymous function</span></span></a><span data-key="45262a0a4a3d4f8f9495a6f37cb812a7"><span data-offset-key="45262a0a4a3d4f8f9495a6f37cb812a7:0"> and its </span><span data-offset-key="45262a0a4a3d4f8f9495a6f37cb812a7:1">_signature_</span><span data-offset-key="45262a0a4a3d4f8f9495a6f37cb812a7:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="08d762b2130f4350836dc6afd2fbcb7e"><span data-offset-key="08d762b2130f4350836dc6afd2fbcb7e:0">The 11th letter of the Classical Greek alphabet, </span><span data-offset-key="08d762b2130f4350836dc6afd2fbcb7e:1">**_λ_**</span><span data-offset-key="08d762b2130f4350836dc6afd2fbcb7e:2">; it has no general meaning in English. In Python it is used because anonymous functions are a fundamental unit of </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lambda_calculus" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5838b52cc2074edfacbffd07d556ad34"><span data-offset-key="5838b52cc2074edfacbffd07d556ad34:0">Alonzo Church’s Lambda Calculus</span></span></a><span data-key="6e38d82928ba4350b2f17142c87d541a"><span data-offset-key="6e38d82928ba4350b2f17142c87d541a:0">, which provides much of the mathematical underpinnings of modern computation. As an honor, that’s nice; in reality </span><span data-offset-key="6e38d82928ba4350b2f17142c87d541a:1">**_lambda_**</span><span data-offset-key="6e38d82928ba4350b2f17142c87d541a:2"> would be used more often if it had a more fun name.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="845d98b074a945e19d822cd9a00d0cf0"><span data-offset-key="845d98b074a945e19d822cd9a00d0cf0:0">Despite the name a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="835e94aab03b481d97c1f032b654c83e"><span data-offset-key="835e94aab03b481d97c1f032b654c83e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="9613596786e4466eb9232337f18f9452"><span data-offset-key="9613596786e4466eb9232337f18f9452:0"> is actually the conceptually simplest form of function in Python, because you can think of it as a just a way of creating a delayed-evaluation EXPRESSION that’s stated with a specific form:</span></span></span>

    lambda : EXPRESSION

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c7d27218a09f432bb349220e17e07dff"><span data-offset-key="c7d27218a09f432bb349220e17e07dff:0">Which evaluates to a CALLABLE that will evaluate the EXPRESSION that comes </span><span data-offset-key="c7d27218a09f432bb349220e17e07dff:1">_after_</span><span data-offset-key="c7d27218a09f432bb349220e17e07dff:2"> the colon only when the CALLABLE is itself called. To call it you use the </span><span data-offset-key="c7d27218a09f432bb349220e17e07dff:3">_call syntax_</span><span data-offset-key="c7d27218a09f432bb349220e17e07dff:4"> that is common to all Python CALLABLEs, however since the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="27ef3e4725794f95bde8834ea17a323d"><span data-offset-key="27ef3e4725794f95bde8834ea17a323d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="420488006bea43c09c2834e81e2c4d8f"><span data-offset-key="420488006bea43c09c2834e81e2c4d8f:0"> is itself an EXPRESSION you need to surround it with parentheses to do that.</span></span></span>

    (lambda : EXPRESSION)()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f39c682e3dbf4f9995054ba96d1351da"><span data-offset-key="f39c682e3dbf4f9995054ba96d1351da:0">And </span><span data-offset-key="f39c682e3dbf4f9995054ba96d1351da:1">_voila_</span><span data-offset-key="f39c682e3dbf4f9995054ba96d1351da:2">, everything you’ve just written will instantly be replaced by whatever the inner EXPRESSION evaluates to.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cc603a6f9eec4975b88addfc08a1e9f2"><span data-offset-key="cc603a6f9eec4975b88addfc08a1e9f2:0">Thus all three of these are entirely identical:</span></span></span>

    x = (lambda : 2 + 2)()x = 2 + 2x = 4

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0d63b808b74a4885ae6b4b692442ec09"><span data-offset-key="0d63b808b74a4885ae6b4b692442ec09:0">But just delaying an EXPRESSION isn’t really the most useful tool. So the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="94163462bea6444a9c28b0f0cb23adc3"><span data-offset-key="94163462bea6444a9c28b0f0cb23adc3:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e6442fd3c9ad4a2fb2a962045e0dfe1d"><span data-offset-key="e6442fd3c9ad4a2fb2a962045e0dfe1d:0"> introduces the idea of a </span><span data-offset-key="e6442fd3c9ad4a2fb2a962045e0dfe1d:1">_function signature_</span><span data-offset-key="e6442fd3c9ad4a2fb2a962045e0dfe1d:2">: you can add a NAME to the left side of the colon and the thing that NAME refers to will able to be used inside the inner EXPRESSION when it evaluates. This name is known as a </span><span data-offset-key="e6442fd3c9ad4a2fb2a962045e0dfe1d:3">_parameter_</span><span data-offset-key="e6442fd3c9ad4a2fb2a962045e0dfe1d:4"> of the function.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="edd78a4c6b4d48e7b425c9e763f2a518"><span data-offset-key="edd78a4c6b4d48e7b425c9e763f2a518:0">Here’s a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="14cbd88b40be4f6fbb661e9c97eea90d"><span data-offset-key="14cbd88b40be4f6fbb661e9c97eea90d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="07ce2ddc13d84d10b507ea7de4448ec1"><span data-offset-key="07ce2ddc13d84d10b507ea7de4448ec1:0"> with a single parameter:</span></span></span>

    lambda NAME: EXPRESSION

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="14e16117169440bfa066110362fea6a7"><span data-offset-key="14e16117169440bfa066110362fea6a7:0">And here’s one with two parameters:</span></span></span>

    lambda NAME_A, NAME_B: EXPRESSION

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dc0486cac82042c0b1adf4090ab2fd98"><span data-offset-key="dc0486cac82042c0b1adf4090ab2fd98:0">And when we want to use the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5d61337ac5fc4257bf0bf88a36cbf324"><span data-offset-key="5d61337ac5fc4257bf0bf88a36cbf324:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7557fae9c05e4f948c2878fbd61ff9aa"><span data-offset-key="7557fae9c05e4f948c2878fbd61ff9aa:0"> we just call it, passing in a concrete VALUE for every parameter in the signature:</span></span></span>

    (lambda NAME_A, NAME_B: EXPRESSION)(VALUE_A, VALUE_B)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="987c37286be24b168d5e98358151b277"><span data-offset-key="987c37286be24b168d5e98358151b277:0">Which you can imagine can be useful if we want to calculate the area of a rectangle:</span></span></span>

    lambda width, height: width * height

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="619dd9980973487a89a6cd36be20d1b7"><span data-offset-key="619dd9980973487a89a6cd36be20d1b7:0">But, again, we’re going to end up writing that a lot if we don’t assign it to a NAME:</span></span></span>

    area = lambda width, height: width * heightsquare = area(2, 2)rectangle = area(3, 5)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787"><span data-offset-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787:0">Great! The </span><span data-offset-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787:1">`square`</span><span data-offset-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787:2"> is now </span><span data-offset-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787:3">`4`</span><span data-offset-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787:4"> and </span><span data-offset-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787:5">`rectangle`</span><span data-offset-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787:6"> is </span><span data-offset-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787:7">`15`</span><span data-offset-key="c3e605a470814dad89fa0b5fee4e9787:8">; we’ve got the basis of code re-use!</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c7fdc50271194c3d8024d46d135f423b"><span data-offset-key="c7fdc50271194c3d8024d46d135f423b:0">But </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4f786541f09341e08a71239f853c18e6"><span data-offset-key="4f786541f09341e08a71239f853c18e6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="6086af8b1b8f4ef09b7d7d38ed939b41"><span data-offset-key="6086af8b1b8f4ef09b7d7d38ed939b41:0"> is going to get pretty nasty when the EXPRESSION starts to get long. And beyond that there are some pretty significant limitations, since we actually </span><span data-offset-key="6086af8b1b8f4ef09b7d7d38ed939b41:1">_cannot_</span><span data-offset-key="6086af8b1b8f4ef09b7d7d38ed939b41:2"> execute many kinds of STATEMENT within a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f3c0bcb717c943ccbe18a91afdd352f1"><span data-offset-key="f3c0bcb717c943ccbe18a91afdd352f1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="bf79c47ec99a4a1abf4f6e9ea45c533a"><span data-offset-key="bf79c47ec99a4a1abf4f6e9ea45c533a:0"> , much less an arbitrary BLOCK. They have their place, but maybe there’s a better and more flexible way?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0af4bbf9b0404e56a0a9f86db016bffb"><span data-offset-key="0af4bbf9b0404e56a0a9f86db016bffb:0">Since we’ve just gone and assigned what is supposed to be an </span><span data-offset-key="0af4bbf9b0404e56a0a9f86db016bffb:1">_anonymous_</span><span data-offset-key="0af4bbf9b0404e56a0a9f86db016bffb:2"> (which means “has no name”) function to a NAME, let’s look at how we should </span><span data-offset-key="0af4bbf9b0404e56a0a9f86db016bffb:3">_usually_</span><span data-offset-key="0af4bbf9b0404e56a0a9f86db016bffb:4"> write functions in Python.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="af9ff63555bd4bc3af525904902545d6"><span data-offset-key="af9ff63555bd4bc3af525904902545d6:0">**named functions**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fc1002bfeb1f474d980b0e87076f359f"><span data-offset-key="fc1002bfeb1f474d980b0e87076f359f:0">The </span><span data-offset-key="fc1002bfeb1f474d980b0e87076f359f:1">_named_</span><span data-offset-key="fc1002bfeb1f474d980b0e87076f359f:2"> function builds on the ideas of the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e9a9f8d3176845899edbae3b7172b159"><span data-offset-key="e9a9f8d3176845899edbae3b7172b159:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="718f245ccf834212a948a4f049aef45f"><span data-offset-key="718f245ccf834212a948a4f049aef45f:0"> but take them to a </span><span data-offset-key="718f245ccf834212a948a4f049aef45f:1">_much_</span><span data-offset-key="718f245ccf834212a948a4f049aef45f:2"> more flexible place, allowing you to re-use large chunks of code quite easily. They’re a little more subtle to master too, because they don’t evaluate exactly like an EXPRESSION.
