In fact by default they’ll always evaluate to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#none" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6aad7e405d5943cc8eddf80985880777"><span data-offset-key="6aad7e405d5943cc8eddf80985880777:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">None</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2dcc0027cd45469992bbd0a147a9eea7"><span data-offset-key="2dcc0027cd45469992bbd0a147a9eea7:0"> unless you explicitly tell them to do otherwise.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3e2cbaff52f543f6b0560556cbd60fb9"><span data-offset-key="3e2cbaff52f543f6b0560556cbd60fb9:0">def</span></span></a><span data-key="41e78a95cfd44bb48cc5b977bd451a98"><span data-offset-key="41e78a95cfd44bb48cc5b977bd451a98:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#function-definitions" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d7e855be328a47709ca8fdbefc40fb26"><span data-offset-key="d7e855be328a47709ca8fdbefc40fb26:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="57c4d80d367c4e979a06b57c10f1f6b3"><span data-offset-key="57c4d80d367c4e979a06b57c10f1f6b3:0">Used to define a </span><span data-offset-key="57c4d80d367c4e979a06b57c10f1f6b3:1">_named_</span><span data-offset-key="57c4d80d367c4e979a06b57c10f1f6b3:2"> function and its </span><span data-offset-key="57c4d80d367c4e979a06b57c10f1f6b3:3">_signature_</span><span data-offset-key="57c4d80d367c4e979a06b57c10f1f6b3:4">, the indented BLOCK that follows can then be re-used by calling that NAME using the </span><span data-offset-key="57c4d80d367c4e979a06b57c10f1f6b3:5">`function()`</span><span data-offset-key="57c4d80d367c4e979a06b57c10f1f6b3:6"> syntax.If used inside a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#class" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="26047f307e044a31958c27a7100fbe0e"><span data-offset-key="26047f307e044a31958c27a7100fbe0e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">class</code></span></span></a><span data-key="fcae5477bf164197a27d172d54d12826"><span data-offset-key="fcae5477bf164197a27d172d54d12826:0"> defines a named </span><span data-offset-key="fcae5477bf164197a27d172d54d12826:1">_method_</span><span data-offset-key="fcae5477bf164197a27d172d54d12826:2"> instead, which is called using the </span><span data-offset-key="fcae5477bf164197a27d172d54d12826:3">`class.method()`</span><span data-offset-key="fcae5477bf164197a27d172d54d12826:4"> syntax.Can also be marked with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="02b226fe3ec94e7285b1324e33e6f15f"><span data-offset-key="02b226fe3ec94e7285b1324e33e6f15f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0b11092db4694c268beeb93021612b17"><span data-offset-key="0b11092db4694c268beeb93021612b17:0"> , to start an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="837fe8add2b7429899222acb63f54a74"><span data-offset-key="837fe8add2b7429899222acb63f54a74:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3d76fa4027964fc0904536ca03c74c9f"><span data-offset-key="3d76fa4027964fc0904536ca03c74c9f:0"> , see below.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9"><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:0">A contraction of the word </span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:1">**_define_**</span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:2">, which comes via the Middle English </span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:3">**_deffinen_**</span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:4"> from Old French and Latin roots. It’s a verb that means “to specify or fix \[the meaning of a word or phrase\]“. In Python it is used specifically to create a named subroutine. In other languages </span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:5">**_define_**</span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:6">, </span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:7">**_fn_**</span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:8">, </span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:9">**_fun_**</span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:10">, </span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:11">**_func_**</span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:12">, </span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:13">**_function_**</span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:14">, and </span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:15">**_let_**</span><span data-offset-key="c14ce759ee8249a08d8cbaca1b86a1a9:16"> are often used instead.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1957f2c8a2ca4f15afc5be1ba6a81a1f"><span data-offset-key="1957f2c8a2ca4f15afc5be1ba6a81a1f:0">Because </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d3132e73d3544d1f978593465789b47f"><span data-offset-key="d3132e73d3544d1f978593465789b47f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5e5b82be89dd409097ab82a59fbe4e2d"><span data-offset-key="5e5b82be89dd409097ab82a59fbe4e2d:0"> can be used to create arbitrarily complex CALLABLEs, it’s going to require some explanation. Essentially it’s used to create a new NAME that refers to a CALLABLE. In fact, from now on let’s just use FUNCTION to mean exactly that:</span></span></span>

    def FUNCTION():    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="be5f376f60414a148ebf2d528b780fff"><span data-offset-key="be5f376f60414a148ebf2d528b780fff:0">This defines a FUNCTION that can be called using </span><span data-offset-key="be5f376f60414a148ebf2d528b780fff:1">`FUNCTION()`</span><span data-offset-key="be5f376f60414a148ebf2d528b780fff:2">, which will then execute every STATEMENT inside the indented BLOCK. As you can see it’s conceptually equivalent to the “named” </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="da4b3b6df0f4461d9b72b3ce3cbabc62"><span data-offset-key="da4b3b6df0f4461d9b72b3ce3cbabc62:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="1f78fbad5f4146e29d8e48b307267794"><span data-offset-key="1f78fbad5f4146e29d8e48b307267794:0"> form you saw earlier. Compare these two forms:</span></span></span>

    def FUNCTION(NAME_A, NAME_B): STATEMENTFUNCTION = lambda NAME_A, NAME_B : STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9c72fb2fb9b042cba16c98556ba27116"><span data-offset-key="9c72fb2fb9b042cba16c98556ba27116:0">And you’ll see they’re </span><span data-offset-key="9c72fb2fb9b042cba16c98556ba27116:1">_very_</span><span data-offset-key="9c72fb2fb9b042cba16c98556ba27116:2"> similar, except that the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8a706f2ce81c4c948e14d05b67fa0b06"><span data-offset-key="8a706f2ce81c4c948e14d05b67fa0b06:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a02886692cec47ecb0204af2bfef5f07"><span data-offset-key="a02886692cec47ecb0204af2bfef5f07:0"> version can run an arbitrary number of STATEMENTs</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#fn:3" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0d9bd2c9774c4c56bf0ca81ae682bb51"><span data-offset-key="0d9bd2c9774c4c56bf0ca81ae682bb51:0">3</span></span></a><span data-key="6ba97989a63042ef881446a2c8884695"><span data-offset-key="6ba97989a63042ef881446a2c8884695:0">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46"><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:0">These STATEMENTs will be executed within the </span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:1">_local scope_</span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:2"> of the function, meaning that </span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:3">_any_</span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:4"> NAME assigned </span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:5">_inside_</span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:6"> the function cannot be </span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:7">_directly_</span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:8"> seen or accessed by any code </span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:9">_outside_</span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:10"> the function. In this example there are no such names, but there will be as soon as we change the </span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:11">_signature_</span><span data-offset-key="fec4eb18d0c449b9afe22ba950854c46:12"> of the function:</span></span></span>

    def FUNCTION(NAME):    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5fb4873419f94fca845fbb6cbad917e7"><span data-offset-key="5fb4873419f94fca845fbb6cbad917e7:0">And just as with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="74e3a4c196924e80ae13c710c1880f97"><span data-offset-key="74e3a4c196924e80ae13c710c1880f97:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5215bdc96d824c1f85081d7c0f6fc8c8"><span data-offset-key="5215bdc96d824c1f85081d7c0f6fc8c8:0"> we can have multiple parameters:</span></span></span>

    def FUNCTION(NAME_A, NAME_B):    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="06a81e6b44194c72b813164d38554863"><span data-offset-key="06a81e6b44194c72b813164d38554863:0">Which let’s us build the </span><span data-offset-key="06a81e6b44194c72b813164d38554863:1">`area`</span><span data-offset-key="06a81e6b44194c72b813164d38554863:2"> function we made before with a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a1279fbe12d34377a34f4194ca53fb19"><span data-offset-key="a1279fbe12d34377a34f4194ca53fb19:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c40f20338a084196b0a689396c28cb12"><span data-offset-key="c40f20338a084196b0a689396c28cb12:0"> :</span></span></span>

    def area(width, height):    width * height​square = area(2, 2)rectangle = area(3, 5)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a3636ce7a4ef4d22b2790377f3793944"><span data-offset-key="a3636ce7a4ef4d22b2790377f3793944:0">Except, wait a minute … didn’t I say just above that </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="67ee3e5bc3f14bb88e27c0c3a3fb393a"><span data-offset-key="67ee3e5bc3f14bb88e27c0c3a3fb393a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5745a1b4eda14577925b56e6d0d05821"><span data-offset-key="5745a1b4eda14577925b56e6d0d05821:0"> functions evaluate to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#none" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9a44602fe02c43d4b0ec89af1a0652fc"><span data-offset-key="9a44602fe02c43d4b0ec89af1a0652fc:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">None</code></span></span></a><span data-key="8cf1e04ab9694f5e87def89a5904bbda"><span data-offset-key="8cf1e04ab9694f5e87def89a5904bbda:0"> when called? Yep, right now both </span><span data-offset-key="8cf1e04ab9694f5e87def89a5904bbda:1">`square`</span><span data-offset-key="8cf1e04ab9694f5e87def89a5904bbda:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="8cf1e04ab9694f5e87def89a5904bbda:3">`rectangle`</span><span data-offset-key="8cf1e04ab9694f5e87def89a5904bbda:4"> are assigned to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#none" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e28370a24f584b47b33b0357414abe60"><span data-offset-key="e28370a24f584b47b33b0357414abe60:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">None</code></span></span></a><span data-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2"><span data-offset-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2:0"> . We’ve calculated two areas, but then discard them again as soon as the </span><span data-offset-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2:1">_local scope_</span><span data-offset-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2:2"> of </span><span data-offset-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2:3">`area`</span><span data-offset-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2:4"> is closed. Now, how the heck do we get the area </span><span data-offset-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2:5">_out_</span><span data-offset-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2:6"> of </span><span data-offset-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2:7">`area`</span><span data-offset-key="1b3833f429f844c3baca0418410473e2:8">, anyway?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a3778f81077b4e05b64d1dc70b3b3883"><span data-offset-key="a3778f81077b4e05b64d1dc70b3b3883:0">**stop the function and give back a value**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e83dab4d3ff246e5b69522293c59dc1e"><span data-offset-key="e83dab4d3ff246e5b69522293c59dc1e:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="65f3a667ec364e9798520a4efe610c0e"><span data-offset-key="65f3a667ec364e9798520a4efe610c0e:0">return</span></span></a><span data-key="6fb66f2055534ca781ab2535ca28b8fd"><span data-offset-key="6fb66f2055534ca781ab2535ca28b8fd:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-return-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8009ed1ea38c4f00a51e1ed8a9806785"><span data-offset-key="8009ed1ea38c4f00a51e1ed8a9806785:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="47388e3017cb498b99986af6453e0c8b"><span data-offset-key="47388e3017cb498b99986af6453e0c8b:0">Used to immediately give up control and end execution of the function at the point at which it is encountered. If followed by an EXPRESSION, that is evaluated first and the resulting OBJECT is given back to the caller of the function. If no EXPRESSION is present </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#none" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="844baf29dc304a96b6b807c6c18a4d65"><span data-offset-key="844baf29dc304a96b6b807c6c18a4d65:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">None</code></span></span></a><span data-key="2a6e0a6aadd349ac9c151775ba42afab"><span data-offset-key="2a6e0a6aadd349ac9c151775ba42afab:0"> is returned instead. Has no meaning outside a function, thus if present at all it </span><span data-offset-key="2a6e0a6aadd349ac9c151775ba42afab:1">_must_</span><span data-offset-key="2a6e0a6aadd349ac9c151775ba42afab:2"> be inside a BLOCK that follows a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="07fc8e10a5774c418d35d92e4d3b8c5d"><span data-offset-key="07fc8e10a5774c418d35d92e4d3b8c5d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="fc639d6168c54ab0971ae4a168b8ba4b"><span data-offset-key="fc639d6168c54ab0971ae4a168b8ba4b:0"> .</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4a551daeed384efab78363363799b10c"><span data-offset-key="4a551daeed384efab78363363799b10c:0">A Middle English verb from the Old French </span><span data-offset-key="4a551daeed384efab78363363799b10c:1">**_retourner_**</span><span data-offset-key="4a551daeed384efab78363363799b10c:2">, meaning “to turn back” or “to go back \[to a former position\]“. In computing it has two meanings:</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e82dabd3a45d4bac88319e14797dd4bf"><span data-offset-key="e82dabd3a45d4bac88319e14797dd4bf:0">The intransitive meaning is “to give back (or relinquish) control \[to the calling procedure\]“, as in “when the function exits it will </span><span data-offset-key="e82dabd3a45d4bac88319e14797dd4bf:1">**_return_**</span><span data-offset-key="e82dabd3a45d4bac88319e14797dd4bf:2"> control”.</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="93e781e44223402688cab89f520d3215"><span data-offset-key="93e781e44223402688cab89f520d3215:0">The transitive meaning is “to pass \[some data\] back to the calling procedure”, as in “this function will </span><span data-offset-key="93e781e44223402688cab89f520d3215:1">**_return_**</span><span data-offset-key="93e781e44223402688cab89f520d3215:2"> the current time”.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dd0cce907bb1476cbc1175559d6fea23"><span data-offset-key="dd0cce907bb1476cbc1175559d6fea23:0">In Python both meanings are combined, since a function will always </span><span data-offset-key="dd0cce907bb1476cbc1175559d6fea23:1">**_return_**</span><span data-offset-key="dd0cce907bb1476cbc1175559d6fea23:2"> both control </span><span data-offset-key="dd0cce907bb1476cbc1175559d6fea23:3">_and_</span><span data-offset-key="dd0cce907bb1476cbc1175559d6fea23:4"> data to the caller.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dd44fcf2ab5f4499bdb3b766a920d953"><span data-offset-key="dd44fcf2ab5f4499bdb3b766a920d953:0">The most basic usage of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="7327c3a8cd6f44178006bc7a2729f8a0"><span data-offset-key="7327c3a8cd6f44178006bc7a2729f8a0:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="debaf82cc0a84576a97bae7a077e5b72"><span data-offset-key="debaf82cc0a84576a97bae7a077e5b72:0"> immediately ends the function and returns </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#none" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d9e4fcbbd8394e109d1a2aaec40966d4"><span data-offset-key="d9e4fcbbd8394e109d1a2aaec40966d4:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">None</code></span></span></a><span data-key="6822c4fea0e54cd7a2b7c1ffa14f5ff1"><span data-offset-key="6822c4fea0e54cd7a2b7c1ffa14f5ff1:0"> to the caller:</span></span></span>

    return

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5ed3a690e318459fb5d1659048b07b47"><span data-offset-key="5ed3a690e318459fb5d1659048b07b47:0">This form is relatively rarely used; as mentioned before a function </span><span data-offset-key="5ed3a690e318459fb5d1659048b07b47:1">_always_</span><span data-offset-key="5ed3a690e318459fb5d1659048b07b47:2"> evaluates to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#none" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="78f2cb1cd18e498a93310e5f4ca53a5a"><span data-offset-key="78f2cb1cd18e498a93310e5f4ca53a5a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">None</code></span></span></a><span data-key="52eccec7c77e49eba442440fc5d5451f"><span data-offset-key="52eccec7c77e49eba442440fc5d5451f:0"> by default; thus you can imagine that </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2c164baaea704b9a81312ba95a6e8a27"><span data-offset-key="2c164baaea704b9a81312ba95a6e8a27:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4359555e6fa24a81a96e67ec42eff403"><span data-offset-key="4359555e6fa24a81a96e67ec42eff403:0"> is the implicit last line of </span><span data-offset-key="4359555e6fa24a81a96e67ec42eff403:1">_every_</span><span data-offset-key="4359555e6fa24a81a96e67ec42eff403:2"> function.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bcb2c750176d49fd884501215bf270fc"><span data-offset-key="bcb2c750176d49fd884501215bf270fc:0">Because of that it is much more common to see:</span></span></span>

    return EXPRESSION

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1b01b33fc0b4489ab4c96532181d922a"><span data-offset-key="1b01b33fc0b4489ab4c96532181d922a:0">Which immediately evaluates the EXPRESSION and returns the resulting OBJECT back to the caller.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a190cd1fe62441fb94147c19771909b4"><span data-offset-key="a190cd1fe62441fb94147c19771909b4:0">You can also use </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="24097c477e8045e4a173f42cec9327a0"><span data-offset-key="24097c477e8045e4a173f42cec9327a0:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4df19451097e42ba92176b3f0a1b1a95"><span data-offset-key="4df19451097e42ba92176b3f0a1b1a95:0"> to pass back more than one OBJECT:</span></span></span>

    return EXPRESSION_A, EXPRESSION_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f90ae89bcf3c4f69ab0148234727a9a8"><span data-offset-key="f90ae89bcf3c4f69ab0148234727a9a8:0">This evaluates each EXPRESSION in turn, ends the function, and returns a </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#func-tuple" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="005647fc8cc04d91a84773baf4d73aa9"><span data-offset-key="005647fc8cc04d91a84773baf4d73aa9:0"><strong>tuple</strong></span></span></a><span data-key="67bab25296744c6ca7ab5ba573e9b220"><span data-offset-key="67bab25296744c6ca7ab5ba573e9b220:0"> (a type of fixed-length COLLECTION) containing one OBJECT for each EXPRESSION.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="15e4d35975804d6c8b8a241d6848fb29"><span data-offset-key="15e4d35975804d6c8b8a241d6848fb29:0">This multiple form is also relatively rare, as it can be a bit of a surprise to the user of the code, and so requires a bit more effort in documentation, but it can be convenient for internal functions that you don’t intend to be used by others.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="84a95226942541b3934388b36a42150e"><span data-offset-key="84a95226942541b3934388b36a42150e:0">What you’ll notice is that </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3318a32d27414c45aa68eba5d34bcf57"><span data-offset-key="3318a32d27414c45aa68eba5d34bcf57:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="3bbe0716b7154ec997c62e6682cd74cf"><span data-offset-key="3bbe0716b7154ec997c62e6682cd74cf:0"> </span><span data-offset-key="3bbe0716b7154ec997c62e6682cd74cf:1">_terminates_</span><span data-offset-key="3bbe0716b7154ec997c62e6682cd74cf:2"> a function at the moment it’s evaluated. Anything below that point in the function essentially doesn’t exist (with one exception, the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#finally" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3b3928e00247485ab8c8e8018ebcab09"><span data-offset-key="3b3928e00247485ab8c8e8018ebcab09:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">finally</code></span></span></a><span data-key="edf48a20c15c48bbabe632f7edf041ff"><span data-offset-key="edf48a20c15c48bbabe632f7edf041ff:0"> block inside an exception handler). So how would you handle situations in which you needed to give back data, but continue to work afterwards?</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9602cab808324a28b30a4c9b664a74a5"><span data-offset-key="9602cab808324a28b30a4c9b664a74a5:0">**pause the function and give back a value**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f7e0a783aa714df58ad1b5399134b556"><span data-offset-key="f7e0a783aa714df58ad1b5399134b556:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2f38c3f3d83243d28c192446598ecfbc"><span data-offset-key="2f38c3f3d83243d28c192446598ecfbc:0">yield</span></span></a><span data-key="c5b6c59435c9435fb227ff662a8b1078"><span data-offset-key="c5b6c59435c9435fb227ff662a8b1078:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-yield-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e9aa78e67ca94421b468e63a3e0561d3"><span data-offset-key="e9aa78e67ca94421b468e63a3e0561d3:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="59cdc68af59e45e595f7bb030f9900f8"><span data-offset-key="59cdc68af59e45e595f7bb030f9900f8:0">Used to immediately pause execution and temporarily give up control at the point at which it is encountered. If followed by an EXPRESSION, that is evaluated first and the resulting OBJECT is yielded back to the caller of the function; if no EXPRESSION is present </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#none" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b464546a11f44dca91fa10946e45de75"><span data-offset-key="b464546a11f44dca91fa10946e45de75:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">None</code></span></span></a><span data-key="83b05d57ee314774b5f208ade513e59f"><span data-offset-key="83b05d57ee314774b5f208ade513e59f:0"> is yielded instead. Has no meaning outside a function, thus if present at all it </span><span data-offset-key="83b05d57ee314774b5f208ade513e59f:1">_must_</span><span data-offset-key="83b05d57ee314774b5f208ade513e59f:2"> be used inside a BLOCK that follows a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9ba0fee45ed642b785dedafb79c09e62"><span data-offset-key="9ba0fee45ed642b785dedafb79c09e62:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c85c9e8b92a44005a055f8e3b963f3eb"><span data-offset-key="c85c9e8b92a44005a055f8e3b963f3eb:0"> .Can be modified by </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#from" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f6d822d13f2d4fe1946c25478570ba84"><span data-offset-key="f6d822d13f2d4fe1946c25478570ba84:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">from</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5c71dc21e0d2481cb6e0d27941c89486"><span data-offset-key="5c71dc21e0d2481cb6e0d27941c89486:0"> to form </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e993978729884576b0baf418917d7ba5"><span data-offset-key="e993978729884576b0baf418917d7ba5:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield from</code></span></span></a><span data-key="f44097e6769e4de8819d621ba6fc9db9"><span data-offset-key="f44097e6769e4de8819d621ba6fc9db9:0"> , see below.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad"><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:0">Etymologically the oddest word in this list; derives from the Middle English </span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:1">**_yielden_**</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:2"> and the Old English </span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:3">**_gieldan_**</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:4">, both of which mean “to pay”, and share their root with the Old Norse </span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:5">**_gjald_**</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:6"> and the German </span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:7">**_geld_**</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:8">, both of which mean “money”. Today </span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:9">**_geld_**</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:10"> means an ancient form of compelled tax or ransom, but it also means “to castrate”. Historically the Dangeld was a tax raised on the English by their king. This tax was raised to pay waves of Danish Vikings to, presumably, not castrate the English (or, at the very least, their king). None of this is directly important here, but might explain a little of why the meaning in computing derives from both “to give way and relinquish control”, as in “</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:11">**_yield_**</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:12"> to oncoming traffic”, and “to give back \[a result or return on investment\]” as in “the fund has a </span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:13">**_yield_**</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:14"> of 5% per year”. In both cases the implication is that the situation is not yet final, and is likely recurring: you </span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:15">**_yield_**</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:16">, then you wait, then you </span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:17">**_yield_**</span><span data-offset-key="616534e6257a45ac99f17dd59d41abad:18"> again.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4708d075b7e0456da40acc850ad4fc3d"><span data-offset-key="4708d075b7e0456da40acc850ad4fc3d:0">In Python it helps to remember an allegory: </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c0c9c456b0234527bc28f3e7a365f39d"><span data-offset-key="c0c9c456b0234527bc28f3e7a365f39d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="211d92f19d80466eb000c18930d3b7e3"><span data-offset-key="211d92f19d80466eb000c18930d3b7e3:0"> is Death, and comes exactly once, while </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8cb756815b294451a5d52b9c4b8814a6"><span data-offset-key="8cb756815b294451a5d52b9c4b8814a6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="6e8e34b2ceeb4ee5968d3675803f9a73"><span data-offset-key="6e8e34b2ceeb4ee5968d3675803f9a73:0"> is Taxes, and may only end when Death arrives.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9a27183582d147f39463258cf30f372a"><span data-offset-key="9a27183582d147f39463258cf30f372a:0">The usage of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b850799571584f538c59f6a4107d1d9f"><span data-offset-key="b850799571584f538c59f6a4107d1d9f:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="727f448e1834452f9579cee6aea0cc05"><span data-offset-key="727f448e1834452f9579cee6aea0cc05:0"> is similar to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6ee8db963f5a4f8bb984d7fa0277ae13"><span data-offset-key="6ee8db963f5a4f8bb984d7fa0277ae13:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4d1079152c47460caba6927e37a7d1a9"><span data-offset-key="4d1079152c47460caba6927e37a7d1a9:0"> :</span></span></span>

    yield

    yield EXPRESSION

    yield EXPRESSION_A, EXPRESSION_B

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="70b8f97da89746c19c82620eb34d3442"><span data-offset-key="70b8f97da89746c19c82620eb34d3442:0">However </span><span data-offset-key="70b8f97da89746c19c82620eb34d3442:1">_any_</span><span data-offset-key="70b8f97da89746c19c82620eb34d3442:2"> function that uses </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a5b6e8cef4ae4fe7a18d5f2e12f223de"><span data-offset-key="a5b6e8cef4ae4fe7a18d5f2e12f223de:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="8bd27d39aa7c4f4c89d139d9432516e7"><span data-offset-key="8bd27d39aa7c4f4c89d139d9432516e7:0"> actually returns a special kind of COLLECTION known as a GENERATOR when called. Unlike a normal COLLECTION a GENERATOR does not hold all of its items in memory simultaneously, but instead “generates” each item as required by running through the function until </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5f08945782ce40549a2202d82dca38f1"><span data-offset-key="5f08945782ce40549a2202d82dca38f1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7b691fd1307b4ea8a574bc1044f2a4a3"><span data-offset-key="7b691fd1307b4ea8a574bc1044f2a4a3:0"> is encountered and it gives forth an item. The GENERATOR pauses execution at that point, allowing the code using the GENERATOR to work with that item. When desired it can request the next item, at which point the GENERATOR continues running to the next </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e269d0cf81ec4ef0b44b0aaa89976f76"><span data-offset-key="e269d0cf81ec4ef0b44b0aaa89976f76:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="47c978b54ff44356ae893ab143bd170e"><span data-offset-key="47c978b54ff44356ae893ab143bd170e:0"> , and so on until there are no more </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ce3d21767e984fce8f93a71ac6340903"><span data-offset-key="ce3d21767e984fce8f93a71ac6340903:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7a72a1b1f84243d0ad7c261a15bab255"><span data-offset-key="7a72a1b1f84243d0ad7c261a15bab255:0"> statements left to run or a </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0ed05802d37944a3adf3170807149a9d"><span data-offset-key="0ed05802d37944a3adf3170807149a9d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="09945ac987cd4c4abc91c2599f88a894"><span data-offset-key="09945ac987cd4c4abc91c2599f88a894:0"> is encountered.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9d63d4fb3279428fa369420103d4cc3b"><span data-offset-key="9d63d4fb3279428fa369420103d4cc3b:0">This is what allows the next form:</span></span></span>

    yield from GENERATOR

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e1cfb732f6c940d28708379f67004746"><span data-offset-key="e1cfb732f6c940d28708379f67004746:0">Which is a specialized use case that allows you to write a GENERATOR that will </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5a95cf424b1042c0b776a10684e9bc2e"><span data-offset-key="5a95cf424b1042c0b776a10684e9bc2e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="4041f4a4bf8a4f898002ca22c7afbcab"><span data-offset-key="4041f4a4bf8a4f898002ca22c7afbcab:0"> every item, in turn, from </span><span data-offset-key="4041f4a4bf8a4f898002ca22c7afbcab:1">_another_</span><span data-offset-key="4041f4a4bf8a4f898002ca22c7afbcab:2"> GENERATOR.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="69787a1ec67f4254bfe989a95b45ff06"><span data-offset-key="69787a1ec67f4254bfe989a95b45ff06:0">A thorough explanation of GENERATORs is outside the scope of this series of articles, as they’re a fairly advanced topic. For now it’s sufficient to know that if you encounter </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="f474fdaa8b3d4205af8b5281254a78c2"><span data-offset-key="f474fdaa8b3d4205af8b5281254a78c2:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="95c526442f1f4d38a378fb7968e6e26c"><span data-offset-key="95c526442f1f4d38a378fb7968e6e26c:0"> you’re looking at a GENERATOR.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1df89bf873d14f35b6c417c0312800d7"><span data-offset-key="1df89bf873d14f35b6c417c0312800d7:0">Three for Manipulating Namespaces</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ca352b99911044efa00db145313736f7"><span data-offset-key="ca352b99911044efa00db145313736f7:0">Now that you understand the basics of function, you’ll need to know about </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Namespace" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="459bd52aec604007892eef945c2dc826"><span data-offset-key="459bd52aec604007892eef945c2dc826:0">namespaces</span></span></a><span data-key="da4f516e99914ec0862c9ea1cb421ef7"><span data-offset-key="da4f516e99914ec0862c9ea1cb421ef7:0">, as they become very important when you start building more complex programs.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8054feef90ec47c3a85078ab91b27f47"><span data-offset-key="8054feef90ec47c3a85078ab91b27f47:0">At its simplest a namespace is essentially just the place where Python stores any NAME you create, so they’re used whenever Python needs to look up the OBJECT referred to by that NAME. Each namespace has a </span><span data-offset-key="8054feef90ec47c3a85078ab91b27f47:1">_scope_</span><span data-offset-key="8054feef90ec47c3a85078ab91b27f47:2">, which limits how long the namespace “lives” and whether or not any NAME within it is </span><span data-offset-key="8054feef90ec47c3a85078ab91b27f47:3">_readable_</span><span data-offset-key="8054feef90ec47c3a85078ab91b27f47:4"> and/or </span><span data-offset-key="8054feef90ec47c3a85078ab91b27f47:5">_writable_</span><span data-offset-key="8054feef90ec47c3a85078ab91b27f47:6"> by a given STATEMENT. Namespaces form a hierarchy, however, so the rules can be a bit tricky to remember.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="70a8917cc77749ebb90b05e9fd3c334d"><span data-offset-key="70a8917cc77749ebb90b05e9fd3c334d:0">In any given namespace a STATEMENT can:</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c165ad6404b440349e73aec949e1a6fd"><span data-offset-key="c165ad6404b440349e73aec949e1a6fd:0">both </span><span data-offset-key="c165ad6404b440349e73aec949e1a6fd:1">_read_</span><span data-offset-key="c165ad6404b440349e73aec949e1a6fd:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="c165ad6404b440349e73aec949e1a6fd:3">_write_</span><span data-offset-key="c165ad6404b440349e73aec949e1a6fd:4"> any NAME defined in its own namespace</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f3858b4de5164485bfcfb2c4d8b42a2b"><span data-offset-key="f3858b4de5164485bfcfb2c4d8b42a2b:0">_read_</span><span data-offset-key="f3858b4de5164485bfcfb2c4d8b42a2b:1">, but not </span><span data-offset-key="f3858b4de5164485bfcfb2c4d8b42a2b:2">_write_</span><span data-offset-key="f3858b4de5164485bfcfb2c4d8b42a2b:3">, any NAME defined in an enclosing </span><span data-offset-key="f3858b4de5164485bfcfb2c4d8b42a2b:4">_parent_</span><span data-offset-key="f3858b4de5164485bfcfb2c4d8b42a2b:5"> namespace</span></span></span>

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d"><span data-offset-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d:0">neither </span><span data-offset-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d:1">_read_</span><span data-offset-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d:2"> nor </span><span data-offset-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d:3">_write_</span><span data-offset-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d:4"> any NAME defined in a </span><span data-offset-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d:5">_sibling_</span><span data-offset-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d:6"> or </span><span data-offset-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d:7">_child_</span><span data-offset-key="ddb0ff86692b4a37b651f7e29479633d:8"> namespace</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="857dfae346bc49459b69870199cda9fe"><span data-offset-key="857dfae346bc49459b69870199cda9fe:0">At the top level is Python’s own namespace, which contains all the </span><span data-offset-key="857dfae346bc49459b69870199cda9fe:1">_builtin_</span><span data-offset-key="857dfae346bc49459b69870199cda9fe:2"> NAMEs that Python provides for you. This namespace </span><span data-offset-key="857dfae346bc49459b69870199cda9fe:3">_cannot_</span><span data-offset-key="857dfae346bc49459b69870199cda9fe:4"> be written to, and any NAME in it essentially lives forever.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e1b2e6cf135f4023b872153c18832b09"><span data-offset-key="e1b2e6cf135f4023b872153c18832b09:0">Next comes the </span><span data-offset-key="e1b2e6cf135f4023b872153c18832b09:1">_global_</span><span data-offset-key="e1b2e6cf135f4023b872153c18832b09:2"> namespace, which is the namespace of the MODULE you’re working in; it becomes the parent of all other namespaces created within that MODULE. Any NAME defined here </span><span data-offset-key="e1b2e6cf135f4023b872153c18832b09:3">_usually_</span><span data-offset-key="e1b2e6cf135f4023b872153c18832b09:4"> lives for the duration your program is running.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8c9fb528279f43d79c0d8fce9bf4545c"><span data-offset-key="8c9fb528279f43d79c0d8fce9bf4545c:0">Next, each CALLABLE you create gets its own unique </span><span data-offset-key="8c9fb528279f43d79c0d8fce9bf4545c:1">_local_</span><span data-offset-key="8c9fb528279f43d79c0d8fce9bf4545c:2"> namespace </span><span data-offset-key="8c9fb528279f43d79c0d8fce9bf4545c:3">_when it is called_</span><span data-offset-key="8c9fb528279f43d79c0d8fce9bf4545c:4">; any NAME created here lives only as long as the CALLABLE is running, and when it finishes both the NAME and the OBJECT it refers to will be destroyed, unless either </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d60252ee6dc84ff0bb0de6ecd103022a"><span data-offset-key="d60252ee6dc84ff0bb0de6ecd103022a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="da16b3e42c6040c4934e606451d2c7c4"><span data-offset-key="da16b3e42c6040c4934e606451d2c7c4:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="29e71c46e5f84939a551aabfb577b1a3"><span data-offset-key="29e71c46e5f84939a551aabfb577b1a3:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="594acedf05ea461985b9bea3d93f3e9d"><span data-offset-key="594acedf05ea461985b9bea3d93f3e9d:0"> is used to pass it back to the calling scope.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f63c8a81423846d18c99d7cdd66ec1cf"><span data-offset-key="f63c8a81423846d18c99d7cdd66ec1cf:0">Since you can define a CALLABLE that is nested </span><span data-offset-key="f63c8a81423846d18c99d7cdd66ec1cf:1">_inside_</span><span data-offset-key="f63c8a81423846d18c99d7cdd66ec1cf:2"> another CALLABLE you can build a namespace hierarchy of arbitrary depth, so any given NAME might exist in any number of namespaces further and further removed from where you’re actually trying to use that NAME. This can get unwieldy to think about pretty quick, though, which is why we </span><span data-offset-key="f63c8a81423846d18c99d7cdd66ec1cf:3">_try_</span><span data-offset-key="f63c8a81423846d18c99d7cdd66ec1cf:4"> to limit the amount of nesting we do in practical code.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="58e6ce3832dd4aa1a3df98ae4debd10a"><span data-offset-key="58e6ce3832dd4aa1a3df98ae4debd10a:0">The assignment of a new NAME is pretty straightforward: unless modified by one of the keywords below a NAME is </span><span data-offset-key="58e6ce3832dd4aa1a3df98ae4debd10a:1">_always_</span><span data-offset-key="58e6ce3832dd4aa1a3df98ae4debd10a:2"> assigned in the scope in which the assignment STATEMENT occurs.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0a4d15f9251b414f9a9e7cf892f2583a"><span data-offset-key="0a4d15f9251b414f9a9e7cf892f2583a:0">But the </span><span data-offset-key="0a4d15f9251b414f9a9e7cf892f2583a:1">_use_</span><span data-offset-key="0a4d15f9251b414f9a9e7cf892f2583a:2"> of a NAME is a little less obvious: when used in a STATEMENT Python first searches for the NAME in the immediate </span><span data-offset-key="0a4d15f9251b414f9a9e7cf892f2583a:3">_local_</span><span data-offset-key="0a4d15f9251b414f9a9e7cf892f2583a:4"> scope. If it cannot find the NAME then it searches the immediate parent (known as the </span><span data-offset-key="0a4d15f9251b414f9a9e7cf892f2583a:5">_nonlocal_</span><span data-offset-key="0a4d15f9251b414f9a9e7cf892f2583a:6">) scope, and then it keeps searching each successive parent scope until it either finds the NAME or cannot resolve it and errors.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="666fe478ef5f4f55ae9be79886121ab7"><span data-offset-key="666fe478ef5f4f55ae9be79886121ab7:0">All of this usually somewhat invisible machinery exists to allow you to write code using NAMEs that are appropriate and clear to the scope in which you’re working. So long as it isn’t a keyword and you don’t </span><span data-offset-key="666fe478ef5f4f55ae9be79886121ab7:1">_need_</span><span data-offset-key="666fe478ef5f4f55ae9be79886121ab7:2"> to use the NAME from an ancestor’s scope you can use whatever NAME you want locally and not worry about it overwriting anything </span><span data-offset-key="666fe478ef5f4f55ae9be79886121ab7:3">_outside_</span><span data-offset-key="666fe478ef5f4f55ae9be79886121ab7:4"> its own scope.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b53597fd0e1847e2b013f228156c4897"><span data-offset-key="b53597fd0e1847e2b013f228156c4897:0">_Most_</span><span data-offset-key="b53597fd0e1847e2b013f228156c4897:1"> of the time you don’t want to fool around with that machinery, but every so often there’s a good reason to. Or a bad one that’s gotten you confused.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e147b17d7e36443ab409b83d3772ebda"><span data-offset-key="e147b17d7e36443ab409b83d3772ebda:0">**write to the top from anywhere**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c7aa3528c7a3476f94ea3f6eabb03293"><span data-offset-key="c7aa3528c7a3476f94ea3f6eabb03293:0">In </span><span data-offset-key="c7aa3528c7a3476f94ea3f6eabb03293:1">_extremely rare_</span><span data-offset-key="c7aa3528c7a3476f94ea3f6eabb03293:2"> circumstances you want to directly manipulate the </span><span data-offset-key="c7aa3528c7a3476f94ea3f6eabb03293:3">_global_</span><span data-offset-key="c7aa3528c7a3476f94ea3f6eabb03293:4"> namespace in a way you wouldn’t normally be allowed.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#global" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="8e5b802c4fab42aaa1ea376f267e97a4"><span data-offset-key="8e5b802c4fab42aaa1ea376f267e97a4:0">global</span></span></a><span data-key="e2f6f467a1ce466cad2a8cd7e3b84dd5"><span data-offset-key="e2f6f467a1ce466cad2a8cd7e3b84dd5:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-global-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a21f361f876c4062aca4727c5f0bb57c"><span data-offset-key="a21f361f876c4062aca4727c5f0bb57c:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9"><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:0">Used to declare a NAME as part of the </span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:1">_global_</span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:2"> namespace; the NAME </span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:3">_cannot_</span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:4"> have been used previously in the same namespace. In effect this allows a </span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:5">_local_</span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:6"> STATEMENT to both create and assign to a </span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:7">_global_</span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:8"> NAME it otherwise could only read. </span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:9">_Can_</span><span data-offset-key="34f162a4eedb4437bee83871bbb9e9e9:10"> be used within the global namespace, but has no effect.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db"><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:0">An adjective borrowed from the French, with the general meaning of “worldwide” and “universal”. In computing the meaning is specifically “\[a NAME that is\] accessible by all parts of a program”. In Python it is both the top-most </span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:1">_namespace_</span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:2">, which is </span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:3">_readable_</span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:4"> from within all functions and methods, but is also a keyword that binds a </span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:5">_local_</span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:6"> NAME into the </span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:7">**_global_**</span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:8"> namespace, allowing it to be </span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:9">_writable_</span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:10"> from within that </span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:11">_local_</span><span data-offset-key="da66359c3bc84e6d86ab1b8b72af15db:12"> namespace.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fd75fe122351402e83267ab4f21c5379"><span data-offset-key="fd75fe122351402e83267ab4f21c5379:0">The usage is quite simple; the main restriction is that it cannot appear </span><span data-offset-key="fd75fe122351402e83267ab4f21c5379:1">_after_</span><span data-offset-key="fd75fe122351402e83267ab4f21c5379:2"> the NAME has been used:</span></span></span>

    global NAMENAME = EXPRESSION

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="38a90dac0e794238899e2bc702fa8345"><span data-offset-key="38a90dac0e794238899e2bc702fa8345:0">You should be aware that the use of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#global" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1fde578ac0b546b1a0867fbb942956e6"><span data-offset-key="1fde578ac0b546b1a0867fbb942956e6:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">global</code></span></span></a><span data-key="407c40111ea6407e99ad36dd862c9ded"><span data-offset-key="407c40111ea6407e99ad36dd862c9ded:0"> is an </span><span data-offset-key="407c40111ea6407e99ad36dd862c9ded:1">_immediate_</span><span data-offset-key="407c40111ea6407e99ad36dd862c9ded:2"> </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_smell" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b6f65473462042f6a023ee0da6c562bb"><span data-offset-key="b6f65473462042f6a023ee0da6c562bb:0">code smell</span></span></a><span data-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae"><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:0">, as its use is </span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:1">_almost always_</span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:2"> an indication of bad coding habits, because it </span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:3">_usually_</span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:4"> can – and almost certainly </span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:5">_should_</span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:6"> – be replaced with </span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:7">_argument passing_</span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:8"> and </span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:9">_return values_</span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:10">. There are data structures and dynamic code generation tasks that would be impossible to build without it, but the </span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:11">_odds_</span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:12"> are if you’re thinking about using it, </span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:13">**don’t**</span><span data-offset-key="3536b75bd7384f8bbde45ff161508aae:14">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="812c7d1cd8b9450eb7eca274d0a95444"><span data-offset-key="812c7d1cd8b9450eb7eca274d0a95444:0">**write to the parent from the child**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="67605053b8e042b8ad04efc80873dc05"><span data-offset-key="67605053b8e042b8ad04efc80873dc05:0">Slightly more often there’s a need for the child to tell the parent what to do.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#nonlocal" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cf48bbcf596b43e0a9574c2461208135"><span data-offset-key="cf48bbcf596b43e0a9574c2461208135:0">nonlocal</span></span></a><span data-key="48c8a58d802d4526a6b0d2ae969d4198"><span data-offset-key="48c8a58d802d4526a6b0d2ae969d4198:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-nonlocal-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3c9c84b614614e06af7e0c4cd09fc83b"><span data-offset-key="3c9c84b614614e06af7e0c4cd09fc83b:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72"><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:0">Used exclusively inside </span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:1">_nested_</span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:2"> functions / methods (also known as </span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:3">_closures_</span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:4">) to bind a </span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:5">_pre-existing_</span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:6"> NAME in the </span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:7">_parent_</span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:8">’s namespace. This allows a STATEMENT in the child to have write access to a NAME defined in its parent. </span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:9">_Must_</span><span data-offset-key="695f4b30ff51429c905d5ccf3ed74e72:10"> appear before any reference to that NAME in the local scope.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0375bf746c7d40f38769e7747d2edbdc"><span data-offset-key="0375bf746c7d40f38769e7747d2edbdc:0">An adjective formed by combining the prefix </span><span data-offset-key="0375bf746c7d40f38769e7747d2edbdc:1">**_non-_**</span><span data-offset-key="0375bf746c7d40f38769e7747d2edbdc:2"> (“not”) and </span><span data-offset-key="0375bf746c7d40f38769e7747d2edbdc:3">**_local_**</span><span data-offset-key="0375bf746c7d40f38769e7747d2edbdc:4"> (“pertaining to a particular place”). This is a primarily scientific and technical </span><span data-offset-key="0375bf746c7d40f38769e7747d2edbdc:5">_neologism_</span><span data-offset-key="0375bf746c7d40f38769e7747d2edbdc:6"> (literally “new word”) that has no true general meaning, only specific meanings within specific fields. In programming it signifies a </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-local_variable" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cd8e9cf53d54414f926986a5a8ca9a46"><span data-offset-key="cd8e9cf53d54414f926986a5a8ca9a46:0">non-local variable</span></span></a><span data-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195"><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:0">, meaning “\[a NAME that is\] accessible in neither the </span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:1">_local_</span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:2"> nor the </span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:3">_global_</span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:4"> namespace”. In Python it very specifically applies to the namespace of the enclosing function from the point of view of a nested function, and is also a keyword that binds a </span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:5">_local_</span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:6"> NAME within that nested function into the </span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:7">**_nonlocal_**</span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:8"> namespace, allowing it to be </span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:9">_writable_</span><span data-offset-key="fd46efa6b9b244089abe7d5152af4195:10"> from within the nested function.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5485d2d1e5d44896b7d382b081c42869"><span data-offset-key="5485d2d1e5d44896b7d382b081c42869:0">Because it is </span><span data-offset-key="5485d2d1e5d44896b7d382b081c42869:1">_only_</span><span data-offset-key="5485d2d1e5d44896b7d382b081c42869:2"> of use inside a nested function, usage will always involve some enclosing structure:</span></span></span>

    def OUTER_FUNCTION():    NAME = VALUE    def INNER_FUNCTION():        nonlocal NAME        NAME = EXPRESSION    INNER_FUNCTION()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="42279284301a445b8a458d34d713e045"><span data-offset-key="42279284301a445b8a458d34d713e045:0">The key thing to understand is that </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#nonlocal" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="d24769fda6f2415d859974dd4b127875"><span data-offset-key="d24769fda6f2415d859974dd4b127875:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">nonlocal</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c9e11b42f3ee4d14a50fd248c6a8f856"><span data-offset-key="c9e11b42f3ee4d14a50fd248c6a8f856:0"> is used in a </span><span data-offset-key="c9e11b42f3ee4d14a50fd248c6a8f856:1">_similar_</span><span data-offset-key="c9e11b42f3ee4d14a50fd248c6a8f856:2"> fashion to </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#global" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e3700eb30a13496099a19628af10a3aa"><span data-offset-key="e3700eb30a13496099a19628af10a3aa:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">global</code></span></span></a><span data-key="8b2b92addeb74e27a6eeb2c7a437e8ad"><span data-offset-key="8b2b92addeb74e27a6eeb2c7a437e8ad:0"> , but with the more limited goal of making a variable in the parent of a nested function writable. It has similar caveats as well, though the fact that its impact isn’t felt by the </span><span data-offset-key="8b2b92addeb74e27a6eeb2c7a437e8ad:1">_entire_</span><span data-offset-key="8b2b92addeb74e27a6eeb2c7a437e8ad:2"> program makes it inherently less dangerous. Still, its uses are </span><span data-offset-key="8b2b92addeb74e27a6eeb2c7a437e8ad:3">_very_</span><span data-offset-key="8b2b92addeb74e27a6eeb2c7a437e8ad:4"> narrow and </span><span data-offset-key="8b2b92addeb74e27a6eeb2c7a437e8ad:5">_relatively_</span><span data-offset-key="8b2b92addeb74e27a6eeb2c7a437e8ad:6"> few, so try not to abuse it when argument passing will do.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="05fb32fbdf004d1d9fad437543b3947b"><span data-offset-key="05fb32fbdf004d1d9fad437543b3947b:0">**kill it with fire**</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f44762014edf4e74a44d87f0797c5a17"><span data-offset-key="f44762014edf4e74a44d87f0797c5a17:0">So far you’ve seen how to </span><span data-offset-key="f44762014edf4e74a44d87f0797c5a17:1">_add_</span><span data-offset-key="f44762014edf4e74a44d87f0797c5a17:2"> a NAME to a namespace, but how do you </span><span data-offset-key="f44762014edf4e74a44d87f0797c5a17:3">_remove_</span><span data-offset-key="f44762014edf4e74a44d87f0797c5a17:4"> a NAME from a namespace?</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#del" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="67c88feaa9d248c8b5716a43eb5422c5"><span data-offset-key="67c88feaa9d248c8b5716a43eb5422c5:0">del</span></span></a><span data-key="bbc0fd1a50b54d1aa488f50cf9af602d"><span data-offset-key="bbc0fd1a50b54d1aa488f50cf9af602d:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/simple_stmts.html#the-del-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1112d8d53d064f409561cb124a52a1e8"><span data-offset-key="1112d8d53d064f409561cb124a52a1e8:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="762f41f964b3427b91857fe561a25ac5"><span data-offset-key="762f41f964b3427b91857fe561a25ac5:0">Used to delete a NAME (or NAMEs) from a namespace; if no other references exist to the OBJECT that NAME referred to, the underlying OBJECT is deleted as well.Can also be used to delete an attribute of an OBJECT or a member (or members) of a COLLECTION </span><span data-offset-key="762f41f964b3427b91857fe561a25ac5:1">_if_</span><span data-offset-key="762f41f964b3427b91857fe561a25ac5:2"> the specific type has allowed this operation.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e"><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:0">A contraction of </span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:1">**_delete_**</span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:2">, which is in turn a verb derived from the Latin </span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:3">**_deletus_**</span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:4">. Its general meaning is to “destroy or eradicate”, “erase or smudge out”, and “utterly remove”, and while the specific meaning in computing is a little less violent it has similar effect. In Python the meaning is a little indirect: </span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:5">**_del_**</span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:6"> is used to delete a </span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:7">_reference_</span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:8"> that the </span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:9">_user_</span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:10"> directly controls, which </span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:11">_may_</span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:12"> indirectly trigger deletion of the thing referred to from process memory, which the </span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:13">_interpreter_</span><span data-offset-key="8f1381dda84c4471ad28f6ddc3200b4e:14"> controls.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9735d9829a3e40b78db340433292bd8a"><span data-offset-key="9735d9829a3e40b78db340433292bd8a:0">The most common usage is to provide a single NAME:</span></span></span>

    del NAME

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="97b7b95ce5e84bef9d56d373bd22f769"><span data-offset-key="97b7b95ce5e84bef9d56d373bd22f769:0">However it is also valid to provide multiple NAMEs, comma separated:</span></span></span>

    del NAME_A, NAME_B, NAME_C

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b2af32994b4a45879c18c1063cf84ddd"><span data-offset-key="b2af32994b4a45879c18c1063cf84ddd:0">In either case Python will proceed left to right, deleting each NAME from the namespace in which the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#del" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="42676766da6145cd85b13b267722b6ba"><span data-offset-key="42676766da6145cd85b13b267722b6ba:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">del</code></span></span></a><span data-key="055c9450181949e8bc35085fd1d111e7"><span data-offset-key="055c9450181949e8bc35085fd1d111e7:0"> invocation has occurred.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b34c6e98b2154adfa7d98658a0b38e5a"><span data-offset-key="b34c6e98b2154adfa7d98658a0b38e5a:0">Because the effect is limited to the </span><span data-offset-key="b34c6e98b2154adfa7d98658a0b38e5a:1">_closest_</span><span data-offset-key="b34c6e98b2154adfa7d98658a0b38e5a:2"> namespace, you have to use </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#global" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="67cb456378a6468093e564ea0b8ffd24"><span data-offset-key="67cb456378a6468093e564ea0b8ffd24:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">global</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a4e2bf17d8564121baad1b15d5c1e379"><span data-offset-key="a4e2bf17d8564121baad1b15d5c1e379:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#nonlocal" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b348e0facc8d4256917078b25b755607"><span data-offset-key="b348e0facc8d4256917078b25b755607:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">nonlocal</code></span></span></a><span data-key="bbe03e482b2e4f819dde5921692fabb6"><span data-offset-key="bbe03e482b2e4f819dde5921692fabb6:0"> to delete a NAME outside the local namespace:</span></span></span>

    global NAMEdel NAME

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="63523db178d44a4ea3f52f2681f01f6d"><span data-offset-key="63523db178d44a4ea3f52f2681f01f6d:0">You can also use </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#del" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="930480bb1f3947d1b67ba072a35dd51c"><span data-offset-key="930480bb1f3947d1b67ba072a35dd51c:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">del</code></span></span></a><span data-key="62731d1d504344b1839474498e15cd7a"><span data-offset-key="62731d1d504344b1839474498e15cd7a:0"> to delete attributes of OBJECTs and member(s) of COLLECTIONs, however what actually happens depends on the type of the OBJECT / COLLECTION involved. The </span><span data-offset-key="62731d1d504344b1839474498e15cd7a:1">**list**</span><span data-offset-key="62731d1d504344b1839474498e15cd7a:2"> COLLECTION, for instance, allows you to use </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#del" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1c1534fc3ca44b3c81119e6dcf74e135"><span data-offset-key="1c1534fc3ca44b3c81119e6dcf74e135:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">del</code></span></span></a><span data-key="65b3437cb1874f6eaee20d91bf532557"><span data-offset-key="65b3437cb1874f6eaee20d91bf532557:0"> to delete both individual </span><span data-offset-key="65b3437cb1874f6eaee20d91bf532557:1">_indices_</span><span data-offset-key="65b3437cb1874f6eaee20d91bf532557:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="65b3437cb1874f6eaee20d91bf532557:3">_slices_</span><span data-offset-key="65b3437cb1874f6eaee20d91bf532557:4"> of its contents:</span></span></span>

    test = [1, 2, 3]del test[0]         # deletes the first itemdel test[:]         # deletes all items

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="53f114a9dcdc4287953c8bd6519a6664"><span data-offset-key="53f114a9dcdc4287953c8bd6519a6664:0">We’ll leave a further exploration of this for when we discuss the </span><span data-offset-key="53f114a9dcdc4287953c8bd6519a6664:1">_builtin_</span><span data-offset-key="53f114a9dcdc4287953c8bd6519a6664:2"> types in later articles. In the meantime, let’s finally meet the keyword that will let you start defining such type-specific behaviors for yourself.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3a71121c144546178904a3619fa42a96"><span data-offset-key="3a71121c144546178904a3619fa42a96:0">One for Defining New Types of Object</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8260476300f14a4786a2c65294cdc7dc"><span data-offset-key="8260476300f14a4786a2c65294cdc7dc:0">Up until this point I’ve been pretty vague about what an OBJECT actually is. In the </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_%28computer_programming%29" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="09d114e088d84f3e90753662ab3f8fb4"><span data-offset-key="09d114e088d84f3e90753662ab3f8fb4:0">Object-Oriented Programming</span></span></a><span data-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20"><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:0"> paradigm, also known as OOP, an object is, basically, a </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:1">_thing_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:2"> that has both </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:3">_state_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:4"> (in the form of named </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:5">_attributes_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:6">) and </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:7">_behavior_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:8"> (in the form of callable </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:9">_methods_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:10">). Two individual things of the same </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:11">_type_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:12"> may have different specific values for those attributes – we call them different </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:13">_instances_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:14"> of the same </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:15">_type_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:16"> – but they share the same overall </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:17">_interface_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:18">. However there’s a bit more to it than that; the programmer should be able to define partial interfaces, which we’ll call </span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:19">_traits_</span><span data-offset-key="016c678c0c6f4b4c8bce29dcd0429f20:20">, that types with similar needs can implement in different ways, such that they all share some common attributes and behaviors (a property known as </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polymorphism_%28computer_science%29" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="69f03acdb172405bb28bd27544da9b44"><span data-offset-key="69f03acdb172405bb28bd27544da9b44:0"><em>polymorphism</em></span></span></a><span data-key="4075cb8aed33452094a6852ae039ced6"><span data-offset-key="4075cb8aed33452094a6852ae039ced6:0">). Additionally these traits should be able to be passed from more generic types to more specific types via an </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inheritance_%28object-oriented_programming%29" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="72e2022a1c8d4c0eb0622484bd42b2e7"><span data-offset-key="72e2022a1c8d4c0eb0622484bd42b2e7:0">inheritance</span></span></a><span data-key="ac433b3ed5a646c09d0242197e7cf1a1"><span data-offset-key="ac433b3ed5a646c09d0242197e7cf1a1:0"> mechanism, much as a parent passes on traits to their children.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3c9146024bba4219859c1b0a7a65fd6d"><span data-offset-key="3c9146024bba4219859c1b0a7a65fd6d:0">You can take an example from nature; a duck is a type of bird, and it inherits certain traits it shares will all birds. All birds are a type of animal, and thus inherit certain traits shared will all animals. An animal is a type of life, and so on. Thus Howard, a specific duck, has all the attributes and behaviors of life, animals, birds, and ducks, all rolled up nicely in one instance of the duck type.</span></span></span>
