<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cf97973bebef4a9f87b82ba90da20469"><span data-offset-key="cf97973bebef4a9f87b82ba90da20469:0">In fact it is from just such an example of biological </span><span data-offset-key="cf97973bebef4a9f87b82ba90da20469:1">_classification_</span><span data-offset-key="cf97973bebef4a9f87b82ba90da20469:2"> that Python takes the keyword it uses for defining new types of OBJECT.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#class" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="29bde2ffe0034ea0a0c3443c9d6fde94"><span data-offset-key="29bde2ffe0034ea0a0c3443c9d6fde94:0">class</span></span></a><span data-key="c2c1b70573ae4ab28b4f3dbb3b9b5111"><span data-offset-key="c2c1b70573ae4ab28b4f3dbb3b9b5111:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#class-definitions" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4e7cd7d25cae4b1293bddc6dd43e5898"><span data-offset-key="4e7cd7d25cae4b1293bddc6dd43e5898:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="b4e826148e544be8b95bdfd088c3f5c0"><span data-offset-key="b4e826148e544be8b95bdfd088c3f5c0:0">Used to define a template for a new type of OBJECT.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a429542463684cc9a0fe7888863a8f87"><span data-offset-key="a429542463684cc9a0fe7888863a8f87:0">A noun borrowed via the French </span><span data-offset-key="a429542463684cc9a0fe7888863a8f87:1">**_classe_**</span><span data-offset-key="a429542463684cc9a0fe7888863a8f87:2"> from the Latin </span><span data-offset-key="a429542463684cc9a0fe7888863a8f87:3">**_classis_**</span><span data-offset-key="a429542463684cc9a0fe7888863a8f87:4">, which meant “a division, army, fleet”, “the people of Rome under arms”, and, oddly specifically, “any one of the six orders into which Servius Tullius divided the Roman people for the purpose of taxation”, which goes a long way towards explaining why English is such a difficult language to master. The general meaning we use here, though, is loosely borrowed from evolutionary taxonomy, implying “a group that shares certain inheritable traits”. The specific meaning in Python comes from Object-Oriented Programming and implies “a template for creating objects that share common inheritable state (attributes) and behavior (methods)”.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9ace71c6de72416c8fedd9afd2d0d5cf"><span data-offset-key="9ace71c6de72416c8fedd9afd2d0d5cf:0">In Python you define a new type by creating a new NAME that is also a CALLABLE; from now on we’ll call that a CLASS. The </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#class" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3d409e8693bb4b76aae18259669e3eca"><span data-offset-key="3d409e8693bb4b76aae18259669e3eca:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">class</code></span></span></a><span data-key="edeee50d0be64df6b3f02e4b273fc57f"><span data-offset-key="edeee50d0be64df6b3f02e4b273fc57f:0"> keyword is used to start a new BLOCK that defines the </span><span data-offset-key="edeee50d0be64df6b3f02e4b273fc57f:1">_implementation_</span><span data-offset-key="edeee50d0be64df6b3f02e4b273fc57f:2"> of that CLASS:</span></span></span>

    class CLASS:    pass

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="77ff5fb888444cff910f0944c3b3676a"><span data-offset-key="77ff5fb888444cff910f0944c3b3676a:0">The CLASS can now be called to create a new instance of its type:</span></span></span>

    NAME = CLASS()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="aa3b2a9dab10415fbe68b17c5af1ebbe"><span data-offset-key="aa3b2a9dab10415fbe68b17c5af1ebbe:0">Now from the above you might expect that instance to have </span><span data-offset-key="aa3b2a9dab10415fbe68b17c5af1ebbe:1">_no_</span><span data-offset-key="aa3b2a9dab10415fbe68b17c5af1ebbe:2"> attributes or behavior, but in fact it does have the </span><span data-offset-key="aa3b2a9dab10415fbe68b17c5af1ebbe:3">_minimal_</span><span data-offset-key="aa3b2a9dab10415fbe68b17c5af1ebbe:4"> interface that all OBJECTs share (it can be printed and used in comparisons, for instance, though not very usefully). It receives this because </span><span data-offset-key="aa3b2a9dab10415fbe68b17c5af1ebbe:5">_all_</span><span data-offset-key="aa3b2a9dab10415fbe68b17c5af1ebbe:6"> new </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#class" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="10080c0bb01e49e19a8533719cc2e22a"><span data-offset-key="10080c0bb01e49e19a8533719cc2e22a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">class</code></span></span></a><span data-key="9a3e0857dfde404685c18e8f45db27f9"><span data-offset-key="9a3e0857dfde404685c18e8f45db27f9:0"> definitions implicitly inherit from </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#object" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5a1b1e77b35c42598b2e14624c7f78bc"><span data-offset-key="5a1b1e77b35c42598b2e14624c7f78bc:0"><strong>object</strong></span></span></a><span data-key="accbb30c71dd4a91b82400fffa00597f"><span data-offset-key="accbb30c71dd4a91b82400fffa00597f:0">, which is Python’s </span><span data-offset-key="accbb30c71dd4a91b82400fffa00597f:1">_base type_</span><span data-offset-key="accbb30c71dd4a91b82400fffa00597f:2">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8fbbd11fac6f49a5b432fb4d4e9a6c6e"><span data-offset-key="8fbbd11fac6f49a5b432fb4d4e9a6c6e:0">You can also specify a more generic CLASS (also known as a </span><span data-offset-key="8fbbd11fac6f49a5b432fb4d4e9a6c6e:1">_superclass_</span><span data-offset-key="8fbbd11fac6f49a5b432fb4d4e9a6c6e:2">) to inherit from:</span></span></span>

    class CLASS(SUPERCLASS):    pass

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fc173caf73364354943c6405a14b0b6d"><span data-offset-key="fc173caf73364354943c6405a14b0b6d:0">In fact you’ll often want to inherit from more than one superclass in order to mix together their various traits. This is done by separating the superclasses with commas:</span></span></span>

    class CLASS(SUPERCLASS_A, SUPERCLASS_B):    pass

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1cdab873697d4e55888bf8ce73ac5d80"><span data-offset-key="1cdab873697d4e55888bf8ce73ac5d80:0">The notion of </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.7/tutorial/classes.html#multiple-inheritance" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9b1c7af8ea6543b0821c1f77b9c88193"><span data-offset-key="9b1c7af8ea6543b0821c1f77b9c88193:0">multiple inheritance</span></span></a><span data-key="f27737b6a11d451f9fe8120711abf95a"><span data-offset-key="f27737b6a11d451f9fe8120711abf95a:0"> can get quite complicated when more than one superclass defines the same attribute or method NAMEs, so for now let’s just keep our classes simple and assume no such overlap.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50"><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:0">Just defining the CLASS and its superclasses without giving it some attributes and methods of its own is unusual, so you’ll </span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:1">_normally_</span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:2"> see at minimum a custom </span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:3">_initializer_</span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:4"> method, which by convention is done by defining the special </span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:5">_double underscore_</span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:6"> (or “dunder”) </span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:7">_instance method_</span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:8"> </span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:9">**\_\_init\_\_**</span><span data-offset-key="d74c1e79687747b2b90c99648b7a5f50:10">:</span></span></span>

    class CLASS:    def __init__(self, NAME):        self.NAME = NAME

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2437235ec8ba4a1eb8954953b6e988fe"><span data-offset-key="2437235ec8ba4a1eb8954953b6e988fe:0">As you can see an instance method is just another kind of function definition made using </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4b90cc4988f04fa48afd2f7897b22417"><span data-offset-key="4b90cc4988f04fa48afd2f7897b22417:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c3fcdcab6107474d86c0ce965739c1b8"><span data-offset-key="c3fcdcab6107474d86c0ce965739c1b8:0"> . In fact a METHOD is just a FUNCTION that’s been added to the CLASS’s namespace. That’s right, the </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#class" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2429a4affa584bfb80a5f433692069da"><span data-offset-key="2429a4affa584bfb80a5f433692069da:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">class</code></span></span></a><span data-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361"><span data-offset-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361:0"> keyword also creates a new kind of local namespace, this one remains attached to the CLASS and allows names to be looked up on either the </span><span data-offset-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361:1">_instance_</span><span data-offset-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361:2"> or the class itself using the </span><span data-offset-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361:3">_dot access_</span><span data-offset-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361:4"> patterns INSTANCE.NAME and CLASS.NAME. Notice the </span><span data-offset-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361:5">**self**</span><span data-offset-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361:6"> parameter name in the method definition above? That’s the name given by convention to the </span><span data-offset-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361:7">_first_</span><span data-offset-key="a3f32b828b514fe7b35d11357886f361:8"> parameter of any instance method, and it’s how you access attributes set on the instance itself.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4963d6b8126d4cea8253af244038a4d2"><span data-offset-key="4963d6b8126d4cea8253af244038a4d2:0">This all sounds a little abstract, so let’s demonstrate it by building a CLASS for thinking about circles.</span></span></span>

    from math import tau​class Circle:    def __init__(self, radius):        self.radius = radius​    def diameter(self):        return self.radius * 2​    def circumference(self):        return self.radius * tau​    def area(self):        return tau * self.radius ** 2 / 2

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c223ec71e0fa4077a7838256132e1d6f"><span data-offset-key="c223ec71e0fa4077a7838256132e1d6f:0">Now if we create an instance representing the </span><span data-offset-key="c223ec71e0fa4077a7838256132e1d6f:1">_unit circle_</span><span data-offset-key="c223ec71e0fa4077a7838256132e1d6f:2">:</span></span></span>

    unit = Circle(1)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="147440b459204764b11d582eb22da634"><span data-offset-key="147440b459204764b11d582eb22da634:0">We can access and </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html#print" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1798a5013af74e4dae7b32362648485b"><span data-offset-key="1798a5013af74e4dae7b32362648485b:0"><strong>print</strong></span></span></a><span data-key="487e136a0ce8489a80101987eec9aa07"><span data-offset-key="487e136a0ce8489a80101987eec9aa07:0"> the </span><span data-offset-key="487e136a0ce8489a80101987eec9aa07:1">**self.radius**</span><span data-offset-key="487e136a0ce8489a80101987eec9aa07:2"> attribute:</span></span></span>

    print(unit.radius)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0f6e7e3c6e154636adf1a91318d03dbc"><span data-offset-key="0f6e7e3c6e154636adf1a91318d03dbc:0">And we can also call any of its methods, but notice how we never have to pass the radius of the circle as an argument, since the methods can all access that via </span><span data-offset-key="0f6e7e3c6e154636adf1a91318d03dbc:1">**self**</span><span data-offset-key="0f6e7e3c6e154636adf1a91318d03dbc:2">:</span></span></span>

    print(unit.diameter())print(unit.circumference())print(unit.area())

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fa11595d6454454fb5e146e9871551ef"><span data-offset-key="fa11595d6454454fb5e146e9871551ef:0">Since they’re the fundamental building block of </span><span data-offset-key="fa11595d6454454fb5e146e9871551ef:1">_everything_</span><span data-offset-key="fa11595d6454454fb5e146e9871551ef:2"> in Python’s </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="af81d1a1bdef48568012037ae68a7a25"><span data-offset-key="af81d1a1bdef48568012037ae68a7a25:0">data model</span></span></a><span data-key="96398224b3514b2ea7db3e114b85b261"><span data-offset-key="96398224b3514b2ea7db3e114b85b261:0">, there’s a </span><span data-offset-key="96398224b3514b2ea7db3e114b85b261:1">_lot_</span><span data-offset-key="96398224b3514b2ea7db3e114b85b261:2"> than can be said </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3.7/tutorial/classes.html#classes" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0b8a39aab26045f8a76692858d594013"><span data-offset-key="0b8a39aab26045f8a76692858d594013:0">about classes in Python</span></span></a><span data-key="3a2cd28f59e040d7a09dc1d94dec7d0e"><span data-offset-key="3a2cd28f59e040d7a09dc1d94dec7d0e:0">, and there’s a lot of subtleties that can go into their proper use (and improper abuse), so we’ll come back to them often in later articles in this series. For now though the important thing is to start to recognize how </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#class" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="39eb94bfad0c48b6b6a4483ffc9b0acd"><span data-offset-key="39eb94bfad0c48b6b6a4483ffc9b0acd:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">class</code></span></span></a><span data-key="6bf0c38f4da24b2e825be5a3d18d2a12"><span data-offset-key="6bf0c38f4da24b2e825be5a3d18d2a12:0"> is used to create them, and how instances are used when accessing their attributes and methods. It’s also helpful to know that there are quite a few “dunder” methods, and that these are used to implement a lot of the common “under-the-hood” functionality that supports all the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/functions.html" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="136227f017474f559913774a742877d4"><span data-offset-key="136227f017474f559913774a742877d4:0">builtin functions</span></span></a><span data-key="7fdfb614f79c478a8977167a3272c82a"><span data-offset-key="7fdfb614f79c478a8977167a3272c82a:0"> we’ll start to meet in later articles.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f0ae936c4cb74bbd916d04ac754590fd"><span data-offset-key="f0ae936c4cb74bbd916d04ac754590fd:0">One for Working Within a Context</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258"><span data-offset-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258:0">Sometimes there are actions you </span><span data-offset-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258:1">_always_</span><span data-offset-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258:2"> want to perform within a specific context, such as committing a database transaction or closing a network connection. These sort of things </span><span data-offset-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258:3">_usually_</span><span data-offset-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258:4"> involve some form of </span><span data-offset-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258:5">_exception handling_</span><span data-offset-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258:6"> or other boilerplate specific to the task, and that can lead to a lot of boilerplate that needs to be repeated. An example is something as simple as reading a file: opening the file must necessarily mean getting some resources from the underlying operating system, and you always want to free up those resources, even if you accidentally tried to open a file that didn’t exist or which you did not have permissions to read. The file is a </span><span data-offset-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258:7">_type_</span><span data-offset-key="81d29afdf2e1467ead829049a86d4258:8"> of OBJECT that will always carry that contextual need to manage a resource with it, and so you’ll need to write the same </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#try" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6bcc835f5a2545b8b8a120559c84f50b"><span data-offset-key="6bcc835f5a2545b8b8a120559c84f50b:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">try</code></span></span></a><span data-key="50de19ac125c412d9ce56517fb05fd30"><span data-offset-key="50de19ac125c412d9ce56517fb05fd30:0"> and </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#finally" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="6bafa5fd7b0d4cc7b4ab5e06eb0dc78a"><span data-offset-key="6bafa5fd7b0d4cc7b4ab5e06eb0dc78a:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">finally</code></span></span></a><span data-key="d06f895773ab413f8d5418106a1e41da"><span data-offset-key="d06f895773ab413f8d5418106a1e41da:0"> boilerplate </span><span data-offset-key="d06f895773ab413f8d5418106a1e41da:1">_every_</span><span data-offset-key="d06f895773ab413f8d5418106a1e41da:2"> time you open a file.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c5e46095ce5c49f2958ef3041fc1ada5"><span data-offset-key="c5e46095ce5c49f2958ef3041fc1ada5:0">Unless the language you’re working in provides a convenient means of ensuring that it happens for you.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#with" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="22412555610a49a888cb14a57100f032"><span data-offset-key="22412555610a49a888cb14a57100f032:0">with</span></span></a><span data-key="fbf1b5c17c424ead9ce2dca328bb82b2"><span data-offset-key="fbf1b5c17c424ead9ce2dca328bb82b2:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#the-with-statement" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cdcd353e205c439d9ad364174d156793"><span data-offset-key="cdcd353e205c439d9ad364174d156793:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="2964ceb248c14f438a0b6c562f0d2666"><span data-offset-key="2964ceb248c14f438a0b6c562f0d2666:0">Starts a </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#context-managers" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ed514edcb5da4132b8c761a7016839db"><span data-offset-key="ed514edcb5da4132b8c761a7016839db:0"><em>context manager</em></span></span></a><span data-key="db601fd3a4c04473b743c23c5bcff648"><span data-offset-key="db601fd3a4c04473b743c23c5bcff648:0"> BLOCK, which ensures that the indented STATEMENT(s) below it are performed within the context of the OBJECT being managed.Can also be marked with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="12df30da1e524d84a6a5a51230e43795"><span data-offset-key="12df30da1e524d84a6a5a51230e43795:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async</code></span></span></a><span data-key="0d93a0376b10469496d3a1387b8636ef"><span data-offset-key="0d93a0376b10469496d3a1387b8636ef:0"> , to start an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ba0adb82123b489097bc6120808d6b32"><span data-offset-key="ba0adb82123b489097bc6120808d6b32:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async with</code></span></span></a><span data-key="f417624a4d42413d99da43054b6e1c4a"><span data-offset-key="f417624a4d42413d99da43054b6e1c4a:0"> , see below.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0"><span data-offset-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0:0">A Middle English preposition that takes its pronunciation from one Old English term, </span><span data-offset-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0:1">**_wið_**</span><span data-offset-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0:2"> (“against”), but takes its modern meaning from another, </span><span data-offset-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0:3">**_mid_**</span><span data-offset-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0:4"> (“in association with”) which in turn comes from the German </span><span data-offset-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0:5">**_mit_**</span><span data-offset-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0:6">. The meaning in Python derives from </span><span data-offset-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0:7">**_within_**</span><span data-offset-key="a9310f32dcf34b2ea40848e74fb503d0:8">, meaning “inside the scope or context of \[some thing or event\]“.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e886d72c5ef7468aae5508c8ba9cf6e6"><span data-offset-key="e886d72c5ef7468aae5508c8ba9cf6e6:0">Any use of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#with" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0a302356c7644213971522c3d8d005f8"><span data-offset-key="0a302356c7644213971522c3d8d005f8:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">with</code></span></span></a><span data-key="558f45b0c1084cf8aac9367bc77be1c8"><span data-offset-key="558f45b0c1084cf8aac9367bc77be1c8:0"> requires an EXPRESSION that evaluates to an OBJECT that satisfies the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html#context-manager-types" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="0857a439a20e4bb8b2191af549173833"><span data-offset-key="0857a439a20e4bb8b2191af549173833:0">context manager type</span></span></a><span data-key="2fcd9dc854a54a7ab2d82c35a0fa8159"><span data-offset-key="2fcd9dc854a54a7ab2d82c35a0fa8159:0">’s interface, and thus has implemented both the </span><span data-offset-key="2fcd9dc854a54a7ab2d82c35a0fa8159:1">**\_\_enter\_\_**</span><span data-offset-key="2fcd9dc854a54a7ab2d82c35a0fa8159:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="2fcd9dc854a54a7ab2d82c35a0fa8159:3">**\_\_exit\_\_**</span><span data-offset-key="2fcd9dc854a54a7ab2d82c35a0fa8159:4"> “dunder” methods. From now on we’ll call that EXPRESSION a CONTEXT_MANAGER, to make the examples clearer.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="90ae1fa30966461e929c013c58c7d65a"><span data-offset-key="90ae1fa30966461e929c013c58c7d65a:0">In the most basic usage you simply start a new BLOCK:</span></span></span>

    with CONTEXT_MANAGER:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a6669c3404a042f682ff771b46e4e5b2"><span data-offset-key="a6669c3404a042f682ff771b46e4e5b2:0">Which will enter the context by calling </span><span data-offset-key="a6669c3404a042f682ff771b46e4e5b2:1">`CONTEXT_MANAGER.__enter__()`</span><span data-offset-key="a6669c3404a042f682ff771b46e4e5b2:2">, execute the STATEMENT within the context, and then exit the context by calling </span><span data-offset-key="a6669c3404a042f682ff771b46e4e5b2:3">`CONTEXT_MANAGER.__exit__()`</span><span data-offset-key="a6669c3404a042f682ff771b46e4e5b2:4">.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5ec5c72e426d418ebfc7348d6237e992"><span data-offset-key="5ec5c72e426d418ebfc7348d6237e992:0">But most often you’ll want to use </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#as" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="82c9e2d79b8544c79d09be0ec9a079d4"><span data-offset-key="82c9e2d79b8544c79d09be0ec9a079d4:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">as</code></span></span></a><span data-key="84a52400a9fe4b92a9a6c68d8731b88f"><span data-offset-key="84a52400a9fe4b92a9a6c68d8731b88f:0"> to assign the OBJECT returned by </span><span data-offset-key="84a52400a9fe4b92a9a6c68d8731b88f:1">`CONTEXT_MANAGER.__enter__()`</span><span data-offset-key="84a52400a9fe4b92a9a6c68d8731b88f:2"> to an alias NAME so the BLOCK can work with it:</span></span></span>

    with CONTEXT_MANAGER as NAME:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0fa50941013c445b8d5d355a5a123a63"><span data-offset-key="0fa50941013c445b8d5d355a5a123a63:0">This can save you a lot of boilerplate, especially with the many standard OBJECTs that already implement the context manager interface. For instance the recommended way to read a file’s contents:</span></span></span>

    with open(path) as src:    contents = src.read()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="358dc8db2c2e4497840308a408fcb047"><span data-offset-key="358dc8db2c2e4497840308a408fcb047:0">Is </span><span data-offset-key="358dc8db2c2e4497840308a408fcb047:1">_much_</span><span data-offset-key="358dc8db2c2e4497840308a408fcb047:2"> simpler than what you’d otherwise have to write:</span></span></span>

    src = open(path)try:    contents = src.read()finally:    src.close()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="dd6f14c4658940628b438c28e6be18ea"><span data-offset-key="dd6f14c4658940628b438c28e6be18ea:0">Occasionally you’ll want to work within more than one CONTEXT_MANAGER:</span></span></span>

    with CONTEXT_MANAGER_A as NAME_A, CONTEXT_MANAGER_B as NAME_B:    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a473df6e19fc496c819b35a722117265"><span data-offset-key="a473df6e19fc496c819b35a722117265:0">Which works exactly the same as nesting one </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#with" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fc9b70c2eed14b57b2a2400cb41c067d"><span data-offset-key="fc9b70c2eed14b57b2a2400cb41c067d:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">with</code></span></span></a><span data-key="b342425f10984bfbb3b52f41116ea832"><span data-offset-key="b342425f10984bfbb3b52f41116ea832:0"> inside another:</span></span></span>

    with CONTEXT_MANAGER_A as NAME_A:    with CONTEXT_MANAGER_B as NAME_B:        STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cd6d31931dd64efa8a53880d2799b1f5"><span data-offset-key="cd6d31931dd64efa8a53880d2799b1f5:0">You’ll get to meet quite a few context managers as you work your way through the Python standard library. And now you know that building your own is just a matter of creating a new </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#class" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="657c09c04adc421db8806a387c0d80d4"><span data-offset-key="657c09c04adc421db8806a387c0d80d4:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">class</code></span></span></a><span data-key="639d7148086c49b7905f8000aed8de3f"><span data-offset-key="639d7148086c49b7905f8000aed8de3f:0"> and implementing a couple of “dunder” methods.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c10003bed54747a9863f47e0b1e02d92"><span data-offset-key="c10003bed54747a9863f47e0b1e02d92:0">And, Finally… Two for Working Asynchronously</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="baa33446de8e44378d75b9af304c6382"><span data-offset-key="baa33446de8e44378d75b9af304c6382:0">Any function or method you write with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cb788c9fe28046d399d8fbddcf80cdb5"><span data-offset-key="cb788c9fe28046d399d8fbddcf80cdb5:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="e94de81e32ad4b878a71cb9d15c52c3b"><span data-offset-key="e94de81e32ad4b878a71cb9d15c52c3b:0"> alone is, by definition, </span><span data-offset-key="e94de81e32ad4b878a71cb9d15c52c3b:1">_synchronous_</span><span data-offset-key="e94de81e32ad4b878a71cb9d15c52c3b:2">, meaning that the moment you call it your running code has to stop everything else and </span><span data-offset-key="e94de81e32ad4b878a71cb9d15c52c3b:3">_wait_</span><span data-offset-key="e94de81e32ad4b878a71cb9d15c52c3b:4">, however long it takes, for your function to either </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4d6170c467d447cf9948768b651647b9"><span data-offset-key="4d6170c467d447cf9948768b651647b9:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="f61b58a6bf2b48d3a686eb90709a6a99"><span data-offset-key="f61b58a6bf2b48d3a686eb90709a6a99:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9109fb01f3ab4db896482c5e6c7a4239"><span data-offset-key="9109fb01f3ab4db896482c5e6c7a4239:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="59955b41ce7a4130af5c620324168a92"><span data-offset-key="59955b41ce7a4130af5c620324168a92:0"> control back to it before the rest of your code can be executed. For most tasks that happen on a local machine this is sensible and perfectly fine, especially when you </span><span data-offset-key="59955b41ce7a4130af5c620324168a92:1">_need_</span><span data-offset-key="59955b41ce7a4130af5c620324168a92:2"> the answer before you can proceed any further.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96"><span data-offset-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96:0">In much modern programming though it’s often necessary to interact with things that </span><span data-offset-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96:1">_don’t_</span><span data-offset-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96:2"> respond quickly, like network interactions with servers that could be a world away, and sometimes there’s </span><span data-offset-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96:3">_plenty_</span><span data-offset-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96:4"> of work you could be doing while you wait for them to respond. You still </span><span data-offset-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96:5">_need_</span><span data-offset-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96:6"> the answer, but you need it </span><span data-offset-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96:7">_eventually_</span><span data-offset-key="f4fa56a9b02b4566ad6848752e804e96:8">. One way this can be addressed is via </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asynchrony_%28computer_programming%29" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="cccd521830574df287c44758e4539e00"><span data-offset-key="cccd521830574df287c44758e4539e00:0">asynchronous programming</span></span></a><span data-key="5cae22493ff0468691dbd8c86b29ed06"><span data-offset-key="5cae22493ff0468691dbd8c86b29ed06:0">, which as of Python 3.5 has become a first-class part of the Python language.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fe532fd11e7f4842831fddc4d20c0563"><span data-offset-key="fe532fd11e7f4842831fddc4d20c0563:0">Asynchronous programming is an advanced topic that is fairly specialized, so using it is well outside the scope of this series. It’s also quite a new addition to the language, and its usage has fluctuated from version to version. Rather than try to summarize those changed I’ll just describe the very basics of using these keywords in Python 3.7 below. If, however, you’re curious there’s a </span></span><a href="https://realpython.com/async-io-python/" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c441f0e031ed47509ec7f631c00d2c4b"><span data-offset-key="c441f0e031ed47509ec7f631c00d2c4b:0">quite good async primer available here</span></span></a><span data-key="b37880a8802a44a8947e847e48faf133"><span data-offset-key="b37880a8802a44a8947e847e48faf133:0"> that seems to be kept up to date.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="eafa2b90a6da4285b47f50479c8f3009"><span data-offset-key="eafa2b90a6da4285b47f50479c8f3009:0">Because asynchronous code does the same work as synchronous code, but </span><span data-offset-key="eafa2b90a6da4285b47f50479c8f3009:1">_schedules_</span><span data-offset-key="eafa2b90a6da4285b47f50479c8f3009:2"> the execution of that work differently, only two new keywords needed to be added to the language.</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3d1b6bedfc6e42a4a2825ca1585068a2"><span data-offset-key="3d1b6bedfc6e42a4a2825ca1585068a2:0">async</span></span></a><span data-key="8f9979cb9e224718a4eb882f28a911d9"><span data-offset-key="8f9979cb9e224718a4eb882f28a911d9:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/compound_stmts.html#coroutine-function-definition" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="13f38f926d2c47d6bd6d78d4587ea9e3"><span data-offset-key="13f38f926d2c47d6bd6d78d4587ea9e3:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="500bd1387bc045eeb3ff651d35773cdc"><span data-offset-key="500bd1387bc045eeb3ff651d35773cdc:0">Used to mark another KEYWORD as one that works asynchronously. As such, </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="dcb09414703a46008bb92d2b53f82705"><span data-offset-key="dcb09414703a46008bb92d2b53f82705:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async</code></span></span></a><span data-key="437026f81d364b099ff1a298170d6987"><span data-offset-key="437026f81d364b099ff1a298170d6987:0"> </span><span data-offset-key="437026f81d364b099ff1a298170d6987:1">_cannot_</span><span data-offset-key="437026f81d364b099ff1a298170d6987:2"> appear on its own.With </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="c56a5aab98394b8f9d9bbf1efcf72a61"><span data-offset-key="c56a5aab98394b8f9d9bbf1efcf72a61:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="ed66394b2b5d483e820c755c3ea144e8"><span data-offset-key="ed66394b2b5d483e820c755c3ea144e8:0"> as </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="666ea9cb9fef43969e9dc06ab5e1b762"><span data-offset-key="666ea9cb9fef43969e9dc06ab5e1b762:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="d220860aa5c94387a1041815bab0a7a4"><span data-offset-key="d220860aa5c94387a1041815bab0a7a4:0"> to define an asynchronous function, also known as a COROUTINE.With </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#for" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="85b08e13289d4557a9de46d529d1e8fe"><span data-offset-key="85b08e13289d4557a9de46d529d1e8fe:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="91336cf1aac149b08f93054986641a84"><span data-offset-key="91336cf1aac149b08f93054986641a84:0"> as </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="19e9ed355f0344d4b25b3b47ea51e2e1"><span data-offset-key="19e9ed355f0344d4b25b3b47ea51e2e1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="6d890ba26afa4b22860708785d0db67a"><span data-offset-key="6d890ba26afa4b22860708785d0db67a:0"> to loop over an </span><span data-offset-key="6d890ba26afa4b22860708785d0db67a:1">_asynchronous iterator_</span><span data-offset-key="6d890ba26afa4b22860708785d0db67a:2"> inside an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="3fada41796ee43d69f7209fe5fe5b1cf"><span data-offset-key="3fada41796ee43d69f7209fe5fe5b1cf:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="fbd2cec62e194a1a9938a9586d9b5386"><span data-offset-key="fbd2cec62e194a1a9938a9586d9b5386:0"> .With </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#with" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a96094d2d2d0485bb67683026ecec2cc"><span data-offset-key="a96094d2d2d0485bb67683026ecec2cc:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">with</code></span></span></a><span data-key="11a392c1c2744294acd89bf940ac08f3"><span data-offset-key="11a392c1c2744294acd89bf940ac08f3:0"> as </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9ab15d6aab3a47c9b1784c5ad7e432a2"><span data-offset-key="9ab15d6aab3a47c9b1784c5ad7e432a2:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async with</code></span></span></a><span data-key="5222326d2e53493ba65669e8d039a19f"><span data-offset-key="5222326d2e53493ba65669e8d039a19f:0"> to use an </span><span data-offset-key="5222326d2e53493ba65669e8d039a19f:1">_asynchronous context manager_</span><span data-offset-key="5222326d2e53493ba65669e8d039a19f:2"> inside an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="585926293de74f609deab1e1850b4103"><span data-offset-key="585926293de74f609deab1e1850b4103:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="d1863bbecc1b424ca386de4753436af7"><span data-offset-key="d1863bbecc1b424ca386de4753436af7:0"> , see below.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b"><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:0">As you may have guessed, this is a contraction of the Modern English word </span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:1">**_asynchronous_**</span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:2">, which is formed by combining the Latin roots </span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:3">**_a-_**</span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:4"> (“not”) and </span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:5">**_syn-_**</span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:6"> (“together”) with </span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:7">**_Khronus_**</span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:8">, the Ancient Greek personification of </span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:9">_time_</span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:10">. It unambiguously means “not occurring at the same time”. In Python it more specifically marks an operation as “not occurring in the same time as the caller”, which allows the caller to wait for the result of that operation, which will occur at </span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:11">_some_</span><span data-offset-key="c111b2dfdeef4ab19d05b6499ad6404b:12"> point in the future.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="321ffa189ec84527b63425804cc93ec9"><span data-offset-key="321ffa189ec84527b63425804cc93ec9:0">Because the meaning of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ce44b0a7e6a94557a2047d7ba2ddfef7"><span data-offset-key="ce44b0a7e6a94557a2047d7ba2ddfef7:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7df47ffa2da247be8ed351fd0fada562"><span data-offset-key="7df47ffa2da247be8ed351fd0fada562:0"> is tied to the KEYWORD it marks, its usage is always the same:</span></span></span>

    async KEYWORD

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e8b7aff056cc4c37ac9360e3b1149508"><span data-offset-key="e8b7aff056cc4c37ac9360e3b1149508:0">However, unlike other any other keyword we’ve seen, the usage of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4f1c74ba37ba43b3a2e8f3c130932c8e"><span data-offset-key="4f1c74ba37ba43b3a2e8f3c130932c8e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async</code></span></span></a><span data-key="539d4d3b6a2f43da98e6fd7d1aa82606"><span data-offset-key="539d4d3b6a2f43da98e6fd7d1aa82606:0"> will </span><span data-offset-key="539d4d3b6a2f43da98e6fd7d1aa82606:1">_always_</span><span data-offset-key="539d4d3b6a2f43da98e6fd7d1aa82606:2"> begin with the definition of a new COROUTINE:</span></span></span>

    async def COROUTINE():    STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8d009c6b18924cd4b446b0241200de24"><span data-offset-key="8d009c6b18924cd4b446b0241200de24:0">Both of the other forms of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="560f43ce3b104958ae627f8ec78bf733"><span data-offset-key="560f43ce3b104958ae627f8ec78bf733:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async</code></span></span></a><span data-key="1377d10a947042b79eeb2caee29e47ab"><span data-offset-key="1377d10a947042b79eeb2caee29e47ab:0"> exist to allow you to work </span><span data-offset-key="1377d10a947042b79eeb2caee29e47ab:1">_within_</span><span data-offset-key="1377d10a947042b79eeb2caee29e47ab:2"> a COROUTINE with </span><span data-offset-key="1377d10a947042b79eeb2caee29e47ab:3">_other_</span><span data-offset-key="1377d10a947042b79eeb2caee29e47ab:4"> COROUTINEs, and thus they can only exist </span><span data-offset-key="1377d10a947042b79eeb2caee29e47ab:5">_inside_</span><span data-offset-key="1377d10a947042b79eeb2caee29e47ab:6"> an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5f962852c30c4c58b7915c608cbaafc1"><span data-offset-key="5f962852c30c4c58b7915c608cbaafc1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="520aee6c6a2542899521126bbd8d31c0"><span data-offset-key="520aee6c6a2542899521126bbd8d31c0:0"> .</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="429e10c560e84331a956843d9285adf5"><span data-offset-key="429e10c560e84331a956843d9285adf5:0">For instance you can use </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="fe23fd4a20ee4df3b7fdaee8bf7e3731"><span data-offset-key="fe23fd4a20ee4df3b7fdaee8bf7e3731:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async for</code></span></span></a><span data-key="382e4a47df8a49bc86c5578e52db6a12"><span data-offset-key="382e4a47df8a49bc86c5578e52db6a12:0"> to loop over an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#asynchronous-iterators" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="77129070c42e4d66ad2052046a2de6d0"><span data-offset-key="77129070c42e4d66ad2052046a2de6d0:0">asynchronous iterator</span></span></a><span data-key="d34c3b68cb8e417a819e319798382b4f"><span data-offset-key="d34c3b68cb8e417a819e319798382b4f:0"> such as a GENERATOR COROUTINE (which is simply a COROUTINE that uses </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#yield" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1c7072ee1b734888a3fcd72ecce026d0"><span data-offset-key="1c7072ee1b734888a3fcd72ecce026d0:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">yield</code></span></span></a><span data-key="410068cf8d134f6eb0dafc23e6ce7d5f"><span data-offset-key="410068cf8d134f6eb0dafc23e6ce7d5f:0"> instead of </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#return" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="ec3705cd342e44ecbbdd2d335a4ece40"><span data-offset-key="ec3705cd342e44ecbbdd2d335a4ece40:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">return</code></span></span></a><span data-key="103dd38507a540e6ad35d38241e9b353"><span data-offset-key="103dd38507a540e6ad35d38241e9b353:0"> ).</span></span></span>

    async def COROUTINE():    async for item in GENERATOR_COROUTINE:        STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8a4ced22545349198b687a6bfa05341b"><span data-offset-key="8a4ced22545349198b687a6bfa05341b:0">You can also use </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b2774c2a4eec4a9494660e32484c942e"><span data-offset-key="b2774c2a4eec4a9494660e32484c942e:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async with</code></span></span></a><span data-key="6a69c0f926da483e99857286037e582c"><span data-offset-key="6a69c0f926da483e99857286037e582c:0"> to perform work within the context of an </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/datamodel.html#asynchronous-context-managers" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="52a43e0f1e73450dac5fb7921fc19b9a"><span data-offset-key="52a43e0f1e73450dac5fb7921fc19b9a:0">asynchronous context manager</span></span></a><span data-key="fceffe805cf9475ab727d07ceb5b6d53"><span data-offset-key="fceffe805cf9475ab727d07ceb5b6d53:0">:</span></span></span>

    async def COROUTINE():    async with CONTEXT_MANAGER_COROUTINE as NAME:        STATEMENT

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d4e1e16180ff43f3b6b0ce5fce11487d"><span data-offset-key="d4e1e16180ff43f3b6b0ce5fce11487d:0">Virtually every COROUTINE will need to wait on other COROUTINE(s), which is why there’s another keyword that can only be used within an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="728516d916e141939f4ee152ea5d49fb"><span data-offset-key="728516d916e141939f4ee152ea5d49fb:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="bf9b3755055b4b5ea4d61cd9a87da2ca"><span data-offset-key="bf9b3755055b4b5ea4d61cd9a87da2ca:0"> .</span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#await" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="a93cef866c764313be708f406ccb9627"><span data-offset-key="a93cef866c764313be708f406ccb9627:0">await</span></span></a><span data-key="fe65c330f5d242038ed139cdc663bd14"><span data-offset-key="fe65c330f5d242038ed139cdc663bd14:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/reference/expressions.html#await-expression" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4e96d5647d114aa4af373645155b600e"><span data-offset-key="4e96d5647d114aa4af373645155b600e:0">docs</span></span></a><span data-key="5754e8b7f5574f2d913d931b6037561c"><span data-offset-key="5754e8b7f5574f2d913d931b6037561c:0">Used to suspend the execution of the COROUTINE it is found </span><span data-offset-key="5754e8b7f5574f2d913d931b6037561c:1">_within_</span><span data-offset-key="5754e8b7f5574f2d913d931b6037561c:2"> and waits for the COROUTINE to its right to complete; can only be used inside an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="2e43cd68c42241ca95b4ae57a936dcb8"><span data-offset-key="2e43cd68c42241ca95b4ae57a936dcb8:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="bd4e19d81c7e451e877ceb03ef2f64c8"><span data-offset-key="bd4e19d81c7e451e877ceb03ef2f64c8:0"> .</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6"><span data-offset-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6:0">From the Middle English verb </span><span data-offset-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6:1">**_awaiten_**</span><span data-offset-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6:2"> (“to wait for”) from the Old French </span><span data-offset-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6:3">**_awaitier_**</span><span data-offset-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6:4">/</span><span data-offset-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6:5">**_agaitier_**</span><span data-offset-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6:6"> (“to lie in wait for, watch, or observe”). The general sense is more active and hostile than </span><span data-offset-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6:7">**_wait_**</span><span data-offset-key="e2411add285c4680bf18e3e0204ff3f6:8">, which it’s a modification of. In asynchronous programming it means to “\[suspend execution\] and wait \[for something to finish\]“.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d1af312584d749de93df763a5ea112b0"><span data-offset-key="d1af312584d749de93df763a5ea112b0:0">The </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#await" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="5d0e307aad8144949f5ea15666b5bfa0"><span data-offset-key="5d0e307aad8144949f5ea15666b5bfa0:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">await</code></span></span></a><span data-key="d1f221e142b64157816d3c86e9b2d8dd"><span data-offset-key="d1f221e142b64157816d3c86e9b2d8dd:0"> keyword is always going to be used to call a COROUTINE inside an </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#async" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="925cfbbba2fb4bf6af729e18216a8a54"><span data-offset-key="925cfbbba2fb4bf6af729e18216a8a54:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">async def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="8b570e8dc60f4d5c9199e97f408ca05d"><span data-offset-key="8b570e8dc60f4d5c9199e97f408ca05d:0"> :</span></span></span>

    async def OUTER_COROUTINE():    await COROUTINE()

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9a6a952fe38f4f26b66298673f3b337e"><span data-offset-key="9a6a952fe38f4f26b66298673f3b337e:0">Which will pause the execution of the outer COROUTINE and wait until the called COROUTINE, eventually, returns control. Any VALUE returned by the called COROUTINE is passed through </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#await" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="b83341ea6a854e8eba2e90483188c2cc"><span data-offset-key="b83341ea6a854e8eba2e90483188c2cc:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">await</code></span></span></a><span data-key="c0dbf9d9051d4cd9937541621a39ea14"><span data-offset-key="c0dbf9d9051d4cd9937541621a39ea14:0"> , so you can think of </span><span data-offset-key="c0dbf9d9051d4cd9937541621a39ea14:1">`await COROUTINE()`</span><span data-offset-key="c0dbf9d9051d4cd9937541621a39ea14:2"> as an asynchronous EXPRESSION that will, </span><span data-offset-key="c0dbf9d9051d4cd9937541621a39ea14:3">_eventually_</span><span data-offset-key="c0dbf9d9051d4cd9937541621a39ea14:4"> evaluate to whatever the COROUTINE returns when called.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3900f3ec41c64bedb95c83ac15aaa9ba"><span data-offset-key="3900f3ec41c64bedb95c83ac15aaa9ba:0">Of course now that you’ve got the basics of doing asynchronous work down, how do you actually </span><span data-offset-key="3900f3ec41c64bedb95c83ac15aaa9ba:1">_perform_</span><span data-offset-key="3900f3ec41c64bedb95c83ac15aaa9ba:2"> such work? Well, as of Python 3.7 that still requires using functionality provided by the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/asyncio.html" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="607daae00cd04ba1a20bb9155c603a57"><span data-offset-key="607daae00cd04ba1a20bb9155c603a57:0">asyncio</span></span></a><span data-key="250362e83c964606bdf2e39072f2d8c6"><span data-offset-key="250362e83c964606bdf2e39072f2d8c6:0"> module, the details of which are </span><span data-offset-key="250362e83c964606bdf2e39072f2d8c6:1">_well_</span><span data-offset-key="250362e83c964606bdf2e39072f2d8c6:2"> outside the scope of these articles. See the </span></span><a href="https://realpython.com/async-io-python/" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="05e8d11dd30345099b1fd949d93d668d"><span data-offset-key="05e8d11dd30345099b1fd949d93d668d:0">async primer</span></span></a><span data-key="729cc04a7b2e4b1b9858491e946e7510"><span data-offset-key="729cc04a7b2e4b1b9858491e946e7510:0"> I mentioned earlier for details.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH700-04e1a2a3--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="502d47a179034cc580b13715e450a052"><span data-offset-key="502d47a179034cc580b13715e450a052:0">Whew…</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7"><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:0">There you have them, Python’s 35 keywords: in and of themselves not enough to make you fluent in Python, but if you’ve read this far and digested it you’re well on your way to truly </span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:1">_understanding_</span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:2"> (and not merely </span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:3">_using_</span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:4">) the skeleton of </span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:5">_what is going on_</span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:6"> in one of the fastest growing general programming languages around. In the next post in this series we’ll take a step away from </span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:7">_words_</span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:8"> and look instead at </span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:9">_symbols_</span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:10">, with a dive into Python’s slightly smaller, but thankfully </span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:11">_much_</span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:12"> simpler, list of </span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:13">_operators_</span><span data-offset-key="3fa0e21fc21b4748939fbbc63e5496a7:14">.</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="153eb7629edf412b80bceeef49913a1d"><span data-offset-key="153eb7629edf412b80bceeef49913a1d:0">Technically </span><span data-offset-key="153eb7629edf412b80bceeef49913a1d:1">**def**</span><span data-offset-key="153eb7629edf412b80bceeef49913a1d:2"> is a </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clipping_%28morphology%29%29" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="36061377a5dc4f749dde9ba7a9e910ab"><span data-offset-key="36061377a5dc4f749dde9ba7a9e910ab:0">final clipping</span></span></a><span data-key="53341e50f7e84d128b3eb515459ad646"><span data-offset-key="53341e50f7e84d128b3eb515459ad646:0"> or </span></span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apocope" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4f76d8edd3fd405591da89965d3c2af5"><span data-offset-key="4f76d8edd3fd405591da89965d3c2af5:0">apocope</span></span></a><span data-key="241fe56d868b404799f1ba22326e8d4d"><span data-offset-key="241fe56d868b404799f1ba22326e8d4d:0">, a specific kind of contraction. English is hard enough already, so I’ll use the more general term. </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#fnref:1" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="4aba5a6a09a54ff58e25ed8e4705d47c"><span data-offset-key="4aba5a6a09a54ff58e25ed8e4705d47c:0">↑</span></span></a><span data-key="cd84a6eb53cf4c24a22d9cc849ae8330"><span data-offset-key="cd84a6eb53cf4c24a22d9cc849ae8330:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e1248fd6444041ccbef08d2878f44fc6"><span data-offset-key="e1248fd6444041ccbef08d2878f44fc6:0">There are 35 keywords as of Python 3.7, the current major version of the language as of the time of writing. New Python keywords are added quite rarely, and it’s even more rare for keywords to be removed, but in whatever version you’re on you can use </span><span data-offset-key="e1248fd6444041ccbef08d2878f44fc6:1">`from keyword import kwlist; print(kwlist)`</span><span data-offset-key="e1248fd6444041ccbef08d2878f44fc6:2"> to view the current list. </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#fnref:2" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="30981e8755a24956b93c3ff96daad661"><span data-offset-key="30981e8755a24956b93c3ff96daad661:0">↑</span></span></a><span data-key="27a8cd6237cf4b2d9e90c5987342a74a"><span data-offset-key="27a8cd6237cf4b2d9e90c5987342a74a:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="56cce505dc5f43fe8527bf7dbc67a2c3"><span data-offset-key="56cce505dc5f43fe8527bf7dbc67a2c3:0">Putting </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#def" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="daef2921ed8e4db2ac2761929703b6f1"><span data-offset-key="daef2921ed8e4db2ac2761929703b6f1:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">def</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7bb6a0675e3f4c94bdf856b089f579ae"><span data-offset-key="7bb6a0675e3f4c94bdf856b089f579ae:0"> on a single line makes the equivalence with </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#lambda" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="9d59f335e1084ee2935d6b4c6b79f2c0"><span data-offset-key="9d59f335e1084ee2935d6b4c6b79f2c0:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">lambda</code></span></span></a><span data-key="7e27564c18b440e48037473a260de989"><span data-offset-key="7e27564c18b440e48037473a260de989:0"> more obvious, but for the sake of readability don’t do this very often. </span></span><a href="https://yawpitchroll.com/posts/the-35-words-you-need-to-python/#fnref:3" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="976a573a216f40b58ce77a4a1ffae3c5"><span data-offset-key="976a573a216f40b58ce77a4a1ffae3c5:0">↑</span></span></a><span data-key="9246c4e49d88489fac73487c1f0c0f4b"><span data-offset-key="9246c4e49d88489fac73487c1f0c0f4b:0"><span data-slate-zero-width="z">​</span></span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--UIH300-2063425d--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--UIH200-50ead35f--textContentFamily-49a318e1">Whew…</span></span>
